O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, most dear sons, I have completed this book for you which is the last of medical science together with its fulfillment and have made an end by its explanations and through its elucidations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of the hands, namely "surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of the hands is neglected in our region and is foreign to all, its knowledge has been lost and cut off, and there remains nothing of it but small descriptions in ancient books that have been passed down by hand.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	From this has come error and vanity, and intentions have been clouded, and knowledge has been pushed aside.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or it seems to me that I will revive it along with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will come with the forms of cautery instruments and other tools for work together with the adjustment of their preparation as required.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good master of hands is found in our time, the art of medicine has extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for one who undertakes this to excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that they know the judgment of limbs, their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones, nerves, muscles, and the number of veins, and the movement and position of moving and resting vessels, and where they emerge.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus Hippocrates said that the name with the wound is great, and with the action is little; especially in the art of surgery.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that those who are not knowledgeable about the aforementioned matters, should beware so as to not fall into error and cause harm to people; just as I have often seen many of those who involve themselves in this science without knowledge or experience, and thus abandon reason.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a foolish surgeon cut into an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman and severed the arteries there; so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another surgeon treating a bladder stone in a man and carried away with it a part of the bladder; the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if he were cut open, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another physician who took care of the Duke of our land, who had a broken leg and an open wound from the break; and the physicians, full of ignorance, set the fracture onto the wound with strong ligatures, leaving no room for drainage, and left him like that for some time; they commanded him not to untie it; and he remained like this until his leg became completely swollen, his foot as well, and he came close to death.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go treat him, and I hurried to come and release his leg; and when I released it he found peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But nonetheless, the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, and it could not be healed; and the corruption continued to spread throughout the limb until the entire limb was lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And then I saw another physician who would destroy an abscess instead of treating it, and then set it alight with the malevolence of his authority.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	Because cancer, when it is riddled with melancholic humour, should not be treated with the iron [blade] unless it is in such a position that one can entirely remove all that is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear son, it is necessary that you know that surgical work is divided into two categories: namely, works where there is danger in many situations; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For this reason, it is necessary for you to be cautious so that the foolish doctor cannot speak ill of you. Take up your arms in consensus and approach your patients lightly but firmly, using the best method so that by God's grace you may attain salvation and be praised; leave behind terrifying diseases with great severity; remove your weapons from whatever makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other in glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on any illness as a cure unless you are called a foolish doctor.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauterization and other medical treatments using heat, and the chapter is organized from head to toe; it describes the forms of instruments, the implements for cauterization, and everything that is necessary in this practice.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and the use of cupping, wounds, arrow extractions, and similar procedures; this chapter describes the order and forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and distortions, and related matters; it is organized from the head to the feet, and describes the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Before we remember the work, it is necessary for me to explain the quality of aid and harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the longest word and most subtle science, a hidden response; many sages have spoken about it, agreeing with each other; I will suffice with few words of theirs, as I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization aids universally all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: these are a warm complexion without matter and a dry complexion without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In a warm and dry complexion combined with matter, some argued that cauterization is greatly beneficial; while others said the opposite: that it has no value for illnesses arising from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is inherently warm, and it should not be used to treat illnesses arising from warmth or dryness; and the one who disagrees says that cauterization provides great relief for hot and dry ailments present in the human body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	When you compare the human body's moisture to the warmth of fire, you find the body cool.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, let no one intercede who has not experienced it, and who does not understand through long practice the chapter of cauterization, and the diversity of human constitutions, and their dispositions and the causes of their illnesses, and their occurrences and the passing of time; we have no fear for other constitutions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the doctors assembled and agreed upon the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that cauterization with fire is one of the secrets of healing, and of greater benefit than any burning medicinal substance.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not arise except on the member that is cooked, and it harms no other member if properly used.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Irritating medicines come from one member to another in remote fashion, and cause the member illness of slow healing; and by chance they kill the patient. Fire for its height and for the goodness of its substance does not do this, if there is no superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have found by experiment and through the length of my service and study in the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse myself for the length of speech, because it does not please me that I should deprive you of the secret which is reposed in fire, and the quality of the work, how it cures bodily illnesses, just as the philosopher says in demonstrating it; now receive it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be done, and chose a suitable time.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that cauterization is appropriate at any time, for it alleviates sudden harm with its aid; especially when the cautery is needed urgently for pain or haste so as not to wait for a greater evil to come upon the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, dear son, as the foolish doctors do; for with a disease that is cured by cauterization there is no recurrence; and they say it thus; but it is not as they believe, because cauterization is only a medicine that alters the complexion, dries out the humors which are the cause of pain, and is better than other medicines due to its swiftness in action and the power of its effect.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	Et it is a powerful thing that the illness comes sometimes according to the constitution of the patient and the location of the disease and its nature; and are gathered in him the superfluities through the acquisition of meat and similar things, if it were not for cauterizations administered where there is little superfluity and moisture, just as dental cauterizations for pain, and similar things, and such pains do not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cauterization comes after medicine, their thoughts are mistaken, and cauterization is indeed the final stage of medicine because when we apply different treatments for a disease and they fail, then we apply cauterization, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	So it is clear that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that cauterization with a gold instrument is more beneficial than with iron, and they said this because of the quality of gold and the excellence of its substance; and they claimed that the color of cauterization does not cause corruption, but this is not true as I have proven it, and I have found that it is indeed true in some people; and cauterization with gold is better than with iron, just as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	However, when you heat a gold instrument, you cannot know when it is hot by its color, and it cools down quickly; if one heats it too much, it melts in the fire; thus there are many obstacles to this method.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use fire cauterization which we have tailored to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Here we have ordered this chapter on the head to feet, so that it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	Olive oil cautery.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	This cautery is beneficial for moisture and coldness in the brain, and there are two ways it is done due to a sickness called "soda", and because of many humors that descend from the head into the eyes, ears, and with numerous dreams, tooth pain, sore throat, and especially all illnesses that come from coldness such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient should be purged with a solutive medicine, modifying the head three or four nights according to what their constitution and fluids can bear; then let the head of the patient rest.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on top of yours; afterward, put the root of your palm onto the root of his nose between his two eyes; allow your two middle fingers to come close together, then bleed a little and warm up the cautery called 'olivare', this is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place it on an ink-stained support, and make it descend while squeezing your hand back and forth repeatedly in a twisting motion; then lift your hand slightly, and withdraw the place if you see a small bone appear; if you don't see it, resume cauterizing until you do see the bone as I told you; afterward take a pouch of silk, and put in it some soft cotton, and place it on top, leaving it there for three days; then apply moist cotton wool soaked in butter; leave it on until the scald is healed; afterwards treat the wound with an ointment called 'tetrafarmacon', until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the ancients say, that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself; and thus, it heals better.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	They say that one should leave the cautery in place until a part of the bone is burned, and then remove what has been burned from the bone, and it shall be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	Some say that one should leave the cautery in place, pressing it down with such force that it pierces the bone as wide as the needle women use for their seams, so that the humors may flow out more readily; and then let the wound remain open for a long time; afterward, it must be cleaned and sewn shut.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	These two methods of cauterization seem to me not at all good for every case; only in some patients where there is fear may it be effective; and I must leave its use entirely, as it weakens the tissue due to continued action by nature, just as we have seen in other body parts; even when the patient's tissue is naturally weak, and the first method of cauterization seems more safe and beneficial to me, and this is what I generally employ for a successful outcome.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	Of old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in all the head there is chronic pain and it persists for a long time, the patient must use herbs and pills called "cochie", and purgatives for the head, oils and poultices; and if one applies the cautery as we mentioned before, but it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take note if the patient's shoulder is of a strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize beneath that cautery just mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After that, make a cautery on each corner of the head down to the bone, as mentioned before, and perform the cautery where it is called "vasselz"; these are places where cups are applied; and be gentle with your hand so as not to reach the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than the others, and I will speak of it later; and make sure that the cauteries on the corners are more subtle than those used for the top of the head, and this is how you do it:
dou cautere dou chief	For cauterization of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in a part of the head and extends up to the eye, and the skull is cleaned by appropriate medicines, and other treatments I have mentioned for different diseases are applied but provide no relief; then treat it with cauterization using two methods: medicinal paste and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The medicinal paste cautery is done as follows: take a fig of almonds, remove the skin and pound it into a fine powder with two eggshells, then make an incision in the temple where the pain resides in such a way that you can insert the almond powder under the skin; once inserted, bind and hold it tightly for twelve hours; afterwards, untie it and treat it with strong garlic juice, leaving the wound open for two or three days; then apply cotton soaked in butter until it is healed.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment, wait until it is healed; and if you see any of these symptoms reappear, use some of the burning medicinal remedies that I have described in my twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is done in this manner:
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery with this implement:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called a "clamp" because its head is shaped like a clamp with a slight curve and an appearance of smallness in the middle; place it on the painful area, and hold your hand so as to slightly twist the iron, until half of the blade's edge is scorched; then lift your hand before burning the artery which lies outside, from which flows copious blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After apply cotton soaked in linen oil, and place it on the area for three days; then put moistened cotton with butter, and subsequently treat the wound until it is healed; if you wish to cauterize this migraine using the 'cultellare' cautery at its tip, take care not to cut the artery during this treatment of a migraine that is not chronic.
de emigraine	De l’emigraine.
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we mentioned earlier in the division of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the cautery methods previously described in medicine or iron do not suffice, then it is necessary to heat the 'cultellare' cautery until it turns white; perform a cut approximately half an inch long on the area where the migraine occurs, take your hand away once, being careful never to cut through an artery nor reach down to the bone; and watch over the jaw so that when someone chews their mouth does not open widely, do not allow the nerve to be stretched or spasms to occur in the patient; further watch out for excessive bleeding from an artery after it has been cut as this is very dangerous especially if you are not a student nor experienced; but leave the work half done. I will now tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery has been cut, and show where such treatment is found within this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizations are not sufficient for the illness, and the patient is still suffering, cauterize him near the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, apply the cauterization method we mentioned in the chapter on arterial extraction, using the cautery with two knives; this cauterization is better and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	From the pain of ears due to coldness.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is ear pain due to coldness, and one has applied dissolving medicines and other treatments as we have said in the division, but the pain does not subside, then heat this cauterization point, which is called a "pin," and its shape is as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After prick around the affected ear, or around both if pain persists in both, and move slightly upwards from the root of the ear once you have marked the site; make ten pricks around each ear; then treat the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	Of the torture of the mouth.
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture that must be treated with cauterisation is apart from those caused by flux, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not use cautery for similar conditions arising from dryness and nerve spasms.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this similar form of torture caused by fluid from ulcers and head purging, as well as gargling, and it doesn't improve, then it is necessary that you cauterise the patient with three cauterisations: one at the root of the ear, another slightly outside the temple, and the third at the join between the two lips; apply the cautery to the part that appears healthy, and perform the cautery towards the top of the ear a little below the crown of the head, and another on the temple as long as a thumb; leave the cautery in place until half the heart's beat has passed; this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it resembles the cylindrical instrument that we mentioned before, but it is slightly more subtle and requires a slightly thicker blade; treat the area as described earlier until it heals properly.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is an old ailment and you treat it as we have described earlier, but there is no improvement and the patient has no fever, then apply four cauterizations: two on the two corners of the head, one in the middle of the head, and one at the location called "vessel" as mentioned before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; treat them as described previously.
de litargie	From lethargy.
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, give the patient large herbs and pills that soften the brain; afterward, rub his entire head with oil and apply a mustard plaster on the occiput as written in the treatise about plasters; here is how you perform the cautery: do it as I have described above.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healed like this, then it is good; and if not, make three cauterizations from within the head down to the neck, with a space of two finger widths between each cautery; treat him as you would others, and if you want to proceed, and the patient can bear it, then apply one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, add two more on the two horns, treating until he is healed; and let these cauterizations be called 'olivare', as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	From the coldness of the head.
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	The head must be cleaned of hairs and other things as we have said before; then shave the patient's head, and apply a cauterization in the middle of the head and on each horn, and one behind and three along the spine of the neck; if you need to do more, and the body is moist and the patient can bear it, and the disease is severe, apply four cauterizations along the spine of the back; let them burn until the greatest part of the heart is scorched, then lift your hand; treat until he is healed, and let these cauterizations be called 'olivare' as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptic should not undergo fire cauterization unless they are phlegmatic; and it is necessary to first modify the brain with herbs and other treatments we have mentioned in the section for when the patient is large and suffering, unable to take medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot endure this, let them perform gargles and mastication to modify the brain often with good meats; then raise their head in the middle, and apply cauterization as we have said before, and cauterize on the vessel and each corner; and if the patient is strong and suffering, perform cauterizations as I said for one who has paralysis and body weakness, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cauterizations be olive-shaped according to the method I described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, perform this subtle cautery as follows:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When the cause is melancholy due to excess humours or corrupted moisture and thick phlegm, then cauterize with three cauteries as we have said for one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if the cause is melancholy due to humours declining into melancholia and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that purifies the brain, according to what was previously stated in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	First, bind the head of the patient; then make a well-formed linen pad in the shape of a circle and place it on their head; have the patient lie with their legs crossed, holding them firmly from all sides; apply the liniment, preferably old sheep butter; heat it to moderate fire so that the skin can withstand its application; empty the circle within the head, let it cool down; perform this once a week for the patient along with other good treatments until they are cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Where you see cauterize with points, make several at each point of the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This manner of cautery moistens the brain equally; then apply cotton dampened with butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes' soreness.
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When soreness first comes to the eyes by means of the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient things purifying for the head, protect them from all moisture, and make them sweat in the bath several times while fasting.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After this, command him to rub his head and make a cautery between the temples; do two cauteries above the two temples if the soreness descends into both eyes together or one if it descends into one alone; and be careful not to cut any veins or arteries beneath the heart when cauterizing; make sure the cautery is as long as the width of the temple; beware excessive blood loss, and if you see too much blood issuing forth, stop it with whatever power you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and the incision, cautioning how to staunch it; sometimes the cautery or iron is applied below the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	the body of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed to flowing over the veins, or close to the arteries that appear outside the head; and it is evident that they are cold, phlegmatic excesses, then perform on them the cautery which I mentioned at the beginning for weeping eyes: one cautery in the center of the forehead, two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries with an iron below the two bones; and if further treatment is necessary, carefully cauterize above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	Through the body of tears from within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat him according to what we have said in the division, and he does not benefit, then give the patient to drink three nights of cock's broth; afterwards, raise his head, and cauterize him at the middle of the olive-shaped bone; and make two 'clavilis' cauteries above the two wrists, a little below the hairline; be careful of the artery so that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the 'clavilis' cautery:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery called 'olive'.
de coi ci est li forme:	For this reason, it has this form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that [the patient] has two cauterizations on the two index fingers as long as the fingernails are; and do not remove your hand from it until a third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair which pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, in which case one performs cauterization according to two methods: that is, with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and remain even, then place the patient in your care; afterwards, trace on paper for the eye a shape that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; then put moistened cotton with egg white and parsley poultice on the eye, then heat the cautery which has this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After cauterizing the shape you have marked, do it again and again many times until the heart of the area is burnt; and the sign of success in this work is that you see the paper shrivel, and the hairs rise to the tip of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it thus for three days, then put moistened cotton with butter until the scald is gone; afterwards cure with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if afterward the hairs grow and the skin is softened again, then resume the cautery on that same spot as you did initially; but if the hair has fallen out, cauterize it until the skin is raised to its natural level, and be even, without pricking the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The burning medical cauteries are that you instruct the patient to leave the hairs as long and even as they can be; then make parchment in the shape of a myrtle leaf; take French soap and live heat, each one part by three parts, and grind them together well; do it quickly so that it doesn't cool down, then spread it on the form you have made like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the skin around the eyes; if the disease is only in one eye, operate on just this one eye, but if also in both; put cotton moistened with egg white below the eye; keep the patient's head still and point your finger at the medicine, press the thumb and forefinger every time the patient feels a stinging sensation from the medicine, for they will feel it as if it were fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for some time, remove the medicine with your hand.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the bite has passed, lift the place of water, and observe if you see the paper raised just as it was raised by the constraint of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is not, apply more medicine to the place where the medicine has been opened, until your work is even and your eyes are precise; then put on moist cotton in butter until the burning heart is cooled, afterward cure the place of ointment which is called "diaphoretic" or another, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must be mindful of your work, do so with great care to ensure that none of the medicine reaches the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft afterward, and the hairs grow back in the eye, you must repeat the medicine on that spot which has softened from the paper itself, just as you did before; after healing it until it is healed; and this is the form of the myrtle leaf:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this be your guidelines; and do not deny the correct path to one who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	On the treatment of fistula by cauterization:
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary for you to perform cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	For the sick person, command them to place their head on your lap; hold the minister's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or shift; afterward, apply moist cotton in egg yolk or parsley juice onto the eye; then heat the cautery which is like this: and there are holes at the top of the head just as with a quill pen, along with the cautery; if you wish, point them from one end to the other, and if you wish, make it also like a tent; but nonetheless, what has been described here (the quill-pen) is more useful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After that, press the fistula if it is open and remove the pus, then dry it; and if it is closed, operate on it and draw out the bowels; afterward, apply a hot cautery moderately, and keep your hand near the cautery at the part of the nail above the eye, so that your hand does not slip; place the cautery in the fatty tissue around the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you cauterize down to the bone, it would be effective.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, restart the cauterization once more, and if needed repeat again, leaving it for three days; afterward apply damp cotton soaked in butter, and treat it with a drying ointment until it heals, and if forty days pass without healing, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and continue according to what comes in its chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	There is also a method of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients mentioned.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	For a fistula, open it up, then insert into the gap one subtle chamois of its own kind:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and make it to the size of a .З. of lead; and hold your hand or arm firmly, and do not let the patient move at all, so that the molten lead does not flow into his eye; and one must put on the sick man's eye moist cotton wool in egg white or in wax: the lead thus fills the place of the fistula, and the wound heals with wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cautery we have mentioned, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, one must administer an opening in the hand, and bring the fistula to the body of the nail according to what is appropriate for its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	cracks on lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Often there are cracks on lips, which are called "chaps," especially on children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as mentioned before in the division of treatment, and the treatment is not effective, then heat a small knife-shaped cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	Place it on the cracks until it reaches the bottom; afterward, treat the area with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	on abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess forms at the root of the throat or in the uvula, palate, or tooth roots, it then causes decay and becomes rounded, swollen, and fistula-like; you treat it as mentioned before in the division of treatment, but it does not heal: then you must take a cautery according to the size of the fistula; after that, probe the opening of the fistula, and keep your hand steady until the hot iron reaches the bottom or back of it; do this once or twice, afterward treating as mentioned before in treatments, until it is healed; if it heals like this, it's good; otherwise, you must uncover the area and remove the corrupted bone according to what you find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	From the movement of the teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but it doesn't work, then place the patient's head on your lap; afterwards heat the cautery which will be formed as follows here: put a rod over the tooth; and insert the hot cautery inside immediately, holding your hand so that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and resume the cauterization according to your desire; after fill the patient's mouth with salty water, and let them hold it for an hour and rinse thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this way, the moving tooth is confirmed to be stable, the soft gum is restrained, and the corrupted moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	From the toothache pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache pain comes from coldness, whether there is actual cold or not, and medical treatments are ineffective, then two types of cauterization are necessary: butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Butter cautery is done by taking cow butter and putting a bit of it in an iron or brass spoon; then take cotton and wrap it on the point of a needle, dip it in boiling butter, and place it on the aching tooth until it cools down; do this often so that its virtue reaches the root of the tooth. If you want to moisten wool and cotton with cold butter and put it on the aching tooth, place an iron heated by fire on top until the heat reaches the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery with fire is such that you take a rod of iron or copper, and it should be thick enough so that the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; afterward heat the cautery, from which the form will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand there until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And the patient should fill their mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then let it cool afterward; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make any type of lip cautery that you want, according to your abilities; and this is the shape of the rod:
des scrophules	The sores
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the sores are caused by phlegm and cold moisture, and they do not respond to digestion through medicine, then heat up the cautery tool which is described below, and make two openings for the smoke to exit from the other side of the cautery; place the hot cautery tool on the abscess once or twice if necessary until it reaches the base of the abscess; if the abscess is small use a smaller cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it like this for three days; then apply moist cotton with butter until the burning sensation is gone; after treat the area with ointments and bandages until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture prevails over the channels of the lung, especially when it arises from a cold constitution, then the patient must first be cleansed with dissolving medicines; afterward, cauterize at the root of the throat, but beware not to reach the throat itself, and only burn a little of the heart.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, apply another cauterization at the joint where the neck meets the head on top of the spine, and let the cauterizations be those called 'clavicle', as described before; treat the area as mentioned previously until it is healed.
de la toust	Of the cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all lung diseases are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or dryness, especially if it is an old illness, then perform two cauterizations above the clavicle in their armpits; another cauterization between the breasts, which should be those called 'clavicle' according to the form described before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see fit, perform cauterization by pricking with the 'punctum' cautery as described before in the ear disease section; and let the punctures be up to 30 or so around it.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the area according to what has been said before, let there be three rows of cauterizations following this pattern:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And because these cauterizations are lighter, you do three at once.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	Of the shoulder dislocation:
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After, remind the patient to lie on their back and side; then lift the heart which is inside the thinness of your left hand's fingers; and if the joint is dislocated within, heat the cautery that has two cords, here is its shape:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the heart until it is pierced to its side, and there would appear the shape of the cautery as four cauteries; and for this reason, the cautery has three cords, so that the figure of cauterization consists of six cauteries; and the nerves according to a subtle tent, and this is the shape of the cautery with three cords:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And sometimes it is adjusted on this one nerve, for which there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After apply the pork rind cautery, grind it with salt; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limb for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated again soon after, then quickly apply a thick clavi-shaped cautery or many cauteries at the base of the bone.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	Because the joint is closed again, and moisture is removed, the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and excessive moisture come to the stomach, removing it from its natural state, and catarrh is multiplied within him, and usual treatments are not effective, then the patient must be reminded to sit upright, extending their legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Of this one thereafter make three cauterizations one below the armpit of the size of a thumb, on each whole side, and two cauterizations outside the two sides so that the shape of the cauteries is in three angles, and has such space between one another that they are not joined together when they cast out corruption; and be the cautery so perfect that it cleanses the two parts of the heart, and be the figure of the cauteries according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and for him who will fear this cauterization, cauterize by pricking and bleeding on the stomach at one point according to the size that you wish to assign; then cauterize it entirely with the cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the wound we treated before, until it is healed.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver is afflicted with pain due to cold and moisture and excessive gas, as it has been moved from its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is treated according to what we have said in divisions, but it does not benefit them, then the patient must be reminded of their own nature; and apply three cauterizations according to this form, figure, and quantity on the liver, below the hypochondria where the waist of a man lies; and leave space between each cautery equal to the thickness of a finger; and let the cauteries be as long as the body, without pressing too hard with your hand over the entire cautery; and only burn half the heart, and have the patient stand upright on their feet; if they cannot, then lie them down, extend their legs, and lift their arms; this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if it is your wish, cauterize these cutellarius cauteries, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and be cautious not to burn the entire heart, for you would cause all the body to wither; and do not reach up to the mouth, as the heart is very delicate there, and know this by observation.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you wish to know if it is within the flesh of the liver or its membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient will feel pain but not too intense; and if it is in the membrane, they will experience excruciating pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And so when this wound requires treatment, it is necessary for the patient to be reminded of their head; then bleed from the spot where the abscess is located, and afterwards heat the cautery which resembles a rod, from which this form arises:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the wound until the heart is burnt, and it reaches the bone, so that the flesh is all charred; afterwards treat according to the cure for wounds, until it is healed; and none but those who have studied long in the art of medicine, through whose hands these illnesses have sometimes been cured, should use this cautery.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he may operate boldly, yet it seems to me that one would be better leaving him alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Scarification with moxa.
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make moxa scarifications with the roots of aristolochia, and in this way: take a long root of aristolochia, the largest you can find; let it be dry, and also as thick and long as your finger; soak it in oil, and then take it to the fire, and scarify between the jugular vein and collarbone, and two small scars slightly below, towards the part that is under the beard; and two scars between the fifth rib and sixth rib, on a slight slope behind; one scar in the middle of the chest, another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two at the sides of the previous scar between the two shoulders; do not press your hand hard, but make them lightly as if you were scenting.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And some ancient experts say that men should use cauterisation with fire like the barber's tool, heating it up and placing it between the ribs until it reaches this abscess; if it alleviates pain, as we have said about liver abscesses.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this operation there is fear that the patient may die now, or a fistula forms which cannot be healed.
de la mice	Of the mouse.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the illness of a mouse according to what we have said about dividing treatments, and it does not improve, then there are three kinds of cauterisation which are all good.
