Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	The first method is to perform three or four cauterisations in a line according to the length of the mouse, following the shape of the liver cautery we described earlier; do not press your hand on the entire cauterisation, and have the patient lie prone on their back; another method of cauterisation involves heating the cautery with two nerves as we showed for shoulder dislocation; lift the heart which is at the location of the mouse, or where the disease comes from towards the left side, and elevate it according to the centreline of the body, and let the cauterisations be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After treatment when there is long-term suppuration, this requires more frequent changes than other treatments mentioned previously.
de ydropisie	Of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not suitable for dropsy, except in the case of the condition known as 'ascites'.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we mentioned earlier in the divisions, and your treatment does not bring improvement, then you must perform four cauterizations around the chest, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the spleen, two behind the back on the spine, and one near the navel; ensure the cauterization is close to the heart.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, leave the open cauterization to allow long-term suppuration, but do not let go of the patient's treatment after the cauterization; healing will be hastened and the two intentions will come together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly is the clover we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what was previously stated.
de l’enfleure des piez	Of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the foot is swollen in a person who has dropsy, and it is full of yellow water, you should cauterize on the back of the heel between the little toe and the ring finger; raise your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not go too deep, lest you dry out the yellow water, and let the cautery be according to this shape:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	Afterwards, make two cauteries on each leg at the tip of the little finger; let one cautery be lengthwise below the knee in front and another outside, halfway down the leg; leave the cauteries open for a long time without treating them, until the water is gone; afterwards treat the other treatments that we have mentioned.
de la menoison	From the mansion
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the problem with the stomach comes from cold and moisture, such that the retaining and digestive powers which are in the stomach and intestine become weakened, and it cannot be cured by ordinary methods; and you see the patient suffering greatly and of strong constitution, then make a large cautery on the stomach according to what has been spoken of before concerning the stomach cautery or circular cautery; and four small cauteries around the navel like the clavicle cautery, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see abundant moisture and the patient suffering, perform a cautery on the wrist, one cautery above each elbow, and two small cauteries on the stomach near the large one, for the treatment is beneficial when there is good assistance.
de la cure des emorroydes	For the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When hemorrhoids are found at the base of the rectum, either one or multiple, and they are old, consisting of large cold and moist corrupted humors, and treatment as described in divisions is not effective, then apply cautery: three cauterizations on the spine above the buttocks, arranged diagonally, and one underneath the anus for two days; if you suspect that their stomach is chilled, meat is not being properly digested, and swelling of the face is observed, then apply one large cauterization on the stomach as previously mentioned, another one on the liver, and one more under the navel with all three cauterizations being clamped; leave the cauterization open for a long period.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, let the wound heal until it is healthy again.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	Of fleshiness, which is named 'thelul'.
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you treat thethelul, heat the cautery until it resembles a razor, and then place it fully heated on top of the treated thethelul; leave your hand there long enough for the cauterization to reach the depth of the vein, from which blood will flow out; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of thethelul, cauterize each section as we have described previously; after that, treat it with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you use a larger cautery on alchatim, it will provide greater help.
de plaie mal curee	Of an improperly treated wound.
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, as we will discuss in its place, such a disease arises that can only be healed through cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When an abscess comes about and is filled with suppuration and corrupted moisture, you should examine it thoroughly with a fine needle, taking care to know the entire depth of the abscess.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heating the cauterizing iron like a razor, insert it into the abscess according to how far the needle went in, and repeat the cauterization as many times as needed: once, twice or thrice; but take care not to burn any nerves that are nearby nor large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the abscess reaches into the body of the bladder and intestine, avoid these places with your cauterization iron, only cauterizing fleshy areas; also know that this is not always effective, so proceed carefully. After treating such an area, heal it thoroughly, but if it is salty and matter has been draining for a long time, then know that it is fully healed; yet if the pus keeps coming, realize that there's an opening to bone at its base, corrupted through and through: this will be discussed in greater detail elsewhere.
de la maladie des reins	Of kidney disease
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the kidneys, and there is severe flatulence, and it does not resemble a female condition, then you must perform cauterization over the kidneys on one side and the other at the clavicle we mentioned before; and if we cauterize in the middle, there will be three cauterizations in a line, and they will provide greater relief.
de la vessie	Of bladder disease
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, such that the patient retains urine, then cauterize outside over the bladder where the arm hairs begin, on both the right and left sides, each cautery should be as long as the nail of a thumb; and perform one cautery outside the back, or two if needed; and let the clavicle cauteries follow the form described before.
de la marris	Of the sad/unhappy [person]
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the womb is cold and moist, preventing conception, and the flowers [eggs] are corrupted with late termination; when they come, great pain is felt: then it must be treated with three fire cauterizations around the navel, as we have said in bladder cauterization, and two outside the back; and let the cautery be clamped, as we have said.
de la hainche	Of the hip [joint]
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When viscous moistures descend to the hip socket, causing its dislocation from its place, and the sign is that one thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the place of departure is found visible, then you must cauterize the patient on the hip socket with one circular cautery, and mark in front of the place around the socket as it turns, so that the socket is inside the circle; and let the cautery be like that used for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this caustic is not present to you, make three large olive oil caustics, and let the caustic be as perfect as all hearts; and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	Of hip pain
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain arises in the hip joint, caused by cold and dampness, and the patient has been treated as we have said in the division but there is no improvement, and the illness is chronic: then you must purge the patient of gross humors with fetid pills or other good similar pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After making the caustic application; and the manner of the caustic is according to two methods: that is, with burning medicinal substances, or with fire cautery.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Cautery with fire is done in many ways, one of which is as follows: apply three triangular cauteries to the hip bone like this; make them deep and large, leave some space between each equal to the width of your thumb, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped. Sometimes a cautery is made in the middle on top of the head of the hip bone, for which there are four done according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see fit, use the circular cautery we previously mentioned for hip dislocations; but do it in such a way that the circles enclose the entire hip bone and all the space around the heart is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	This is how it's done for sciatica when the pain is in the hip and doesn't extend down to the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes down to the thigh and leg, make two cauterizations where the patient says the pain is located, and four cauterizations above the ankle on the left side, slightly less; let the cauterizations be cutellary, and burn away the thickness of the heart; and if the patient feels that the pain extends down to the toes or close by, cauterize it with three points or four at the point called 'point'.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	If necessary, do more; and if you know that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, perform a cutellary or circular cauterization, and be very careful with all your cauterizations not to leave it so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who were cauterized on the ankle of their foot, and they left it until their leg was entirely swollen, and their feet as well, and all their feet were pierced and corrupted.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After an abdominal operation from which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, cauterize in one part and then in the other, according to this method.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the sages said about cauterizing the hip, regarding this method, make such an iron tool and have it as wide at its head as a two-digit navel (or slightly less), and have it perforated with holes and let there be the space of one thumb width between each perforation; and the perforations should be oriented towards two sides, and they should also be like knots, and let there be a well-made iron handle attached; and this is its form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And heat it until it is all red and throw hot coals on it, then put it on the sick hip bone and turn him onto his healthy side; cauterize once with one iron and leave it three days; then apply an ointment plaster, and leave the wound open a long time; afterwards treat with ointments until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasis says that we use this cautery rarely due to its appearance and because few people use it; yet it is one of the good cauteries, which can be tolerated if applied where there is no fear.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cauteries of medicine that burn are made with a latticework instrument in which the width of the opening is adjusted by means of sliding margins, and it may be made of copper or iron at one side; have two feet high and each foot equal to the thickness of a thumb; they are open from above and below, and join together according to this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After, place the box of the hip on the patient lying on their healthy side, and quickly press your hand firmly above the hip box; afterward, pour between the two circles of hot water that has been heated one peck over fire, and leave it for an hour's time, and let the patient bear the heat and burning.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is true that there is a cauterization as well with fire; and when the cauterization has passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the hip in warm water, and leave it thus for three days, and apply butter until what is black from the scalding is removed; and leave it three days so putrid matter is extracted; and this would be the last aid after the cure of ointments until it is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or down to the leg, make an instrument for him that holds heat according to what you did at the hip similarly; and this is how to apply hot poultice, which I have written about in the treatise on medical correction.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take quicklime and alkali, equal parts of each, grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	where there is a small opening through which the point of a razor can enter; place another well-sealed pot on top of it, and put sweet water above the lime and alkali so that there are two fingers' worth of water over the powders when you have tightly sealed it with your hand; leave this setup until sweet water and moisture has descended into the sealed pot, then take all that water and pour it back onto the lime and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And so it will be very hot and administered in many medical procedures and cauterizations of other members, for it does the same work as fire, and has other medicines with which one can cauterize well the hip, such as thistle and acacia honey and heated soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment where a man was cured of hip pain and sciatica, and he praises it greatly, saying that no other treatment was applied, and that he was healed in one go when this cure was performed, and he had bathed as he teaches below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says to do it in this way: take some fresh and dry verdigris, grind it very finely with one pound of grease, put it on the hip, thigh, and leg where the pain is located, then bandage it; leave it for three hours or as long as necessary until the patient no longer feels the burning sensation.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then have him enter the bath until his body is a little raised, and let him go into bed, and the pain will leave entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use the cautery with such treatments unless it is after the evacuation of the body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dyascorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat fat, it helps greatly; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and grease it with old oil, and place it on the hollow which is between the thumb of the foot and the other one called 'foscile'.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After that, take dry goat fat and hold it to the fire until it becomes charcoal, and place it on the linen, leaving it there until it is extinguished; repeat this process again, and do not stop doing so until you feel that it has reached up to the hip, and that the pain has ceased; and this kind of cautery is called 'goat cautery'.
de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether due to falling or impact or excessive strain, or similar matter spreading coldness, for none of these situations is cauterization useful except for that which arises from an influx of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	One must, after ensuring the patient is free of foul-smelling pills or other similar substances that could be applied to their back where the pain persists, make three rows marked with ash, and in each row place five cauterizations or more according to the potency and quantity that the patient can endure; and let these cauterizations be made following the method called "poking"; and if you wish, make three or four cauterizations at the middle of the clavicle following this pattern:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this illness comes to small children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a narrow chest when lying down, and fear; you find in the last vertebra of the spine and in us an appearance that arises on other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this one and treat it, cauterize it with the red-hot iron according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	The cautery should thoroughly burn each part of the vertebra equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see it, cauterize around the vertebra with the iron making two or three pricks, and let these be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treat the place until it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful not to apply the iron in a bend of nerve tissue.
de la dolor des jointes	From the pain of joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of joints is caused by moisture that spreads to every limb of the body, and when the pain occurs in the foot, which doctors call "podagra" properly, and when it is due to cold and cannot be cured by medicines, then it is treated with cautery in this way: make a mound of cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a need to apply it to the sole of the foot, make a cautery at what we call "the point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	If the pains reach up to the knees and other joints, and this happens frequently, apply three or four cauteries on each knee, all olive-shaped; and if you need more, do more, but do not hold your hand there longer than it takes for the heart's iron to burn.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knees and back, administer the cautery as we have described in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make two lines of points around the wrist; and if there remains any pain in the fingers, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the elbows or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care for the patient and give them medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you provide good care and purge the phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	On fractures of the hip.
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When fracture occurs in the thigh, and the bones descend into the hips, if it is recent, on the day you treat it, make sure he does not eat; and have him use things that empty the belly so that the excrement leaves his stomach; afterward, make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his breath until the bowels are restored, and bring them up with your two hands, and bleed underneath the fracture near the hip bone, and over all of it make a sign similar to half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery in this way:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as they are white and emit no odor.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Put the balls back in place; and have your assistant hold their hand over it so that it does not return backward; and support the patient's legs well, and put a pillow underneath them and another under the knees to hold their hands; then apply the cautery with all your might, and press down straight until you reach the bone; if you do not make it the first time, repeat again until you come right up to the bone; be careful that the ball does not jump out when you are doing the cautery so as not to burn it; for fear that by this the patient may die or have some other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	Know that if you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is useless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And the cauterization for children should be subtle according to their size, and for adults it should also be proportionate; after three days treat the place of the cautery with butter until the burn is healed; afterward cure other ointments so that it heals, and let the patient lie on their back for forty days until the wound is fully closed; and make sure that their nourishment is satisfyingly long so that the bowel does not protrude when they try to go into rooms.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when they wish to get up, provide them with a well-made bandage, and wear it for another forty days; ensure good rest, let them work little by little and avoid overfilling their drink or food intake, as well as too much screaming; once these instructions are followed, the patient is fully healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	Et I shall say hereafter the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, if it requires fire cautery, burn the third part of the heart; afterward treat as we have said; and some ancients say it must be cauterized with a three-angled cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	But first mark the place of incision and make a line across the width above the rupture, then another outside it; hold your hand in between during the entire cautery procedure.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauterizations are lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	From old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, either from falling or injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and medical treatment is ineffective, then it must be cauterized with the cautery called 'point', and the cautery should be applied according to the length of the limb, its smallness, weakness, strength, and location of torsion, as well as its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If it is healed from the first cautery, that is good; if not, apply another cautery over the previous one, for such is the custom, as it must be changed to the limb nearest to it, which is why you should continue with cauterizations until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	Of surgery.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The months are aided sometimes by cautery with great help, especially illnesses that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	If you see him being cauterized, pay attention if the illness is in its beginning stage and if it has been cured according to what we said before regarding divisions. If the disease persists or stays around and you suspect that corruption could affect the whole patient then perform five cauteries on his head: one behind the ear at nine o'clock, another towards the forehead near the end of the hairline; two more by the temples, and finally one at the back of the head. You must allow the heat to penetrate as deep as your hand reaches so that it reaches the bone, burning until you see scabs form on his skin allowing vapors from any thick humours within him escape - cauterize him over his nose according these instructions above.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	Et si la maladie est répandue partout ; et qu'elle perd manifestement, il faut que tu la cautérises avec ces cautères que nous avons dit pour le chef, et un cautère sur le nez, et deux cautères sur l’épine du cou, et six cautères sur l’épine du dos, et un grand sur la croupe et un autre à côté, et deux sur les deux épaules ; et deux sur les côtes, et deux sur les tendons de la cuisse, et un sur chacune des articulations des mains et des pieds, et sur les creux des mains ; et prends garde aux nerfs qui sont sur le talon arrière, que tu ne les brûles ; et parfois fait on cautère sur l’os du poignet, et un autre sur l’os de l'estomac, et un autre sur le foie.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	Et sache que plus tu fais de cautère, plus tu l'aides, et cela lui profite ; et sache que les malades ne sentent pas de douleur au cautère comme les sains la ressentent, car leur corps est déjà tout corrompu.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterizations be large and small according to the members and joints, depending on how you find them arranged with the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating it, place the part in flour paste mixed with honey and other treatments until it is healthy.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling occurs in any limb and is treated with medicines, oils, and poultices, but it is not healed, then apply cautery to the limb according to its size: let the cauterization be a little deep into the flesh; treat it afterwards with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cautery is made on the hand, foot or back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; yet be careful not to do so unless you are knowledgeable about limbs and the exits of nerves moving the body.
de albaras	For boils
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is persistent, and medical treatments are ineffective, then cauterize it with a perfect cautery, according to the quantity of the heart's species, until the whiteness is removed, and its color changes; then treat it with a mixture of flour from vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of pigeons and doves, each in equal parts; blend everything together, bind it with a cloth, and expose it to air until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	treatment of cancer through cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When cancer appears at the beginning, and you want to stop its growth, then cauterize it with a circular-shaped cautery around the entire area of the cancerous growth.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise ones said that a cautery should also be applied to the middle of the chancre; and yet it does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen this happen once; and it is more proper for it to be cauterized around, with the "circular" cautery, as we said before about many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	Of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has an illness called 'adubelati', and it prolongs death either due to the excessiveness of its nature or because of the patient's wateriness when they are decrepit (meaning very old) and have little blood, or due to the season; and you see that their death is hastened: then cauterize them all around with many small cauteries, pricking [with each]; afterwards leave them be.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced through all the cautery, heat the cautery with what is formed here:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	Place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced the heart, and make such cauteries that the patient feels them outside in a way that reduces the course of corruption.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After treating it, wait until it is perfectly healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire treatment with iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	There is another kind of illness called "corrodens", which is nothing but the wasting away of limbs, as it withers the limbs just like fire dries up branches.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a place that can endure fire cautery, then heat the small and large clavicle cauterizers very slightly, according to what is appropriate for the location where the illness is; afterward cauterize it from all sides so much that you eradicate every corruption, leaving nothing of it behind, such that everything corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Leave it for three days, and apply to the cauterized locations a soft ointment with oil so that the scalds from the fire are removed, along with all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	Afterwards treat the resulting wound with ointments that produce flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days you see that healthy flesh is not growing, it is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on what remains of the corrupted places.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this treatment was sometimes cured by medicine alone instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless fire cautery is more helpful, and I have already described the cure with medicine in another section: use it when you need to.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	sores that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often, on the feet due to injury, a disease arises which we call a 'claws', and it is a large faulty growth that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cauterization for this disease follows two methods.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery, and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat a hollow quill-shaped cauterizer like a goose feather until it is red hot, and make sure it is good iron of the right size so that it can cover the nail on all sides, and has fine edges; after, put this very hot on the nail, and turn your hand around the nail until it reaches the base of the nail; then leave it like this for three days until it begins to discharge pus; afterwards make an emollient with crushed mallows and raw wool grease, and let the emollient stay on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat the place of application with soothing ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are caused by the corruption of the body, occurring frequently in hands and feet, you must apply hot water cauterization; it is done like this: take a copper or iron rod, or a goose quill, and place over the wart and arum, which means verrucas warts; place the rod so that it surrounds it entirely, then pour some hot water into it, hold your hand firmly, and press your hand turning it in such a way that the edge of the rod reaches the base of the wart, allowing for deep penetration by the hot water down to its root; allow the patient to experience the stinging sensation from the hot water for an hour; then leave them like this, and all roots will be completely eradicated.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another until you have treated all those that are in the body, then treat them with ointments which generate flesh.
li cure dou trembler	The doctor of trembling/shaking.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When someone shakes due to coldness of nerves or quartan fever or any other, you should make four cauterizations on the spinal column or three if on the back, one between each vertebra; and one cautery on the foot, and one above the stomach at the olive-shaped organ; thus will stop shaking and hasten recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	Stinking pustules/blisters.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes on the body appear swellings or stinking blisters that come from gross corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	So it befits the first when they appear that one performs a cauterization on each head of the pimple: a subtle cautery with myrtle wood, so that its point is taken by fire, or with long aristoloche root, or with the lens-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And one should cauterize them at the beginning when they first appear, according to this method, and they cannot grow from then on, but the excess that causes them is broken, and they are healed; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	There are often great outpourings of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes on top, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cauterization of the member, and with similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to staunch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger on the wound's injury, and press hard so that blood is calmed beneath your finger, and no more drops out; then put many small and large olive oil cauterizers onto fire until they are all red; then take one, big or small depending on the wound and the location of the artery, and place the cauterizer on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep it there until the blood is stanched.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if the blood should spurt when you lift your finger from the wound, and the cauterizers have cooled, then quickly take another one of the cauterizers that are on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	Do not cease doing this one after the other until the blood is fully stanched; and beware that you do not burn the nerve nearby, and that no further harm befalls the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be properly stanched especially if the artery is large, unless by one of four methods we have mentioned: cauterization, or extraction if it has not been treated, or tight binding with thread, or medicines placed on it which possess the power to stop blood; and let this be tied and held firmly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring about restraint by tightly binding it with cloth or placing hot objects on top of it, or other similar methods, will not be successful if there is no benefit from doing so.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they have neither mirror nor medicine at hand, then one must place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we've mentioned before, and stretch it until it is constricted over the wound and the vein; do not move your finger, but moisten it with cold water often so that it is very cold to freeze and thicken the blood and constrict it; then make preparations beforehand for what they will need in terms of cauterization and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book on surgical treatments.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all about illnesses that require fire cauterization or burning medicines, and their effects, causes, instruments, and forms of cauterization; I placed this chapter on the head down to the feet, and I will go through this same route in this chapter so that what one seeks may be found more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, as I begin this work, dear son, you must learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first about cauterization, and thus it requires even greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to undertake foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For people come for treatment in many ways.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	Some come of such a state that they are so afraid with their illness that they die quickly from the fear and severity of their condition; and one must have fear for these cases.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And some will give you their opinion, saying: "Wait, I am healed"; but the illness is deceitful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You must not consent to those who come to you with such mannerisms, but put greater trust in your honor than in your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely in matters of which you are certain and from which you can gain fame and profit; and make use of prognosis and indication in treating your patients for their benefit; this will help you acquire a good reputation, glory, and praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	My dear son, may our Lord give you good understanding and guidance, and may he breathe into you the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter by dividing it into chapters, according to what is set forth in the chapter on cauterization, which I divided for you from head to toe, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Head full of water.
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this illness often comes to children at birth, and when the midwife grips the child's head too tightly; sometimes it also arises from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this illness occur in anyone but children, and all of those whom I have seen were doomed to death; thus it seems best for me to leave off treating such cases.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose shoulder was full of water, and the head swelled each day to such an extent that he could not bear it; and the moisture grew so much that he died, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone on the scapula, between the heart and the bone; and in cases like these where the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should make an incision in the head a thumb-width wide; and it should be as long as two thumbs, so that the moisture flows out; and see here the form of the spathula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess larger, then make two incisions in the form of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and you see the sutures of the head opening on each side, and the water leaps forth when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not respond to treatment: then you must make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision extract all the moisture quickly.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Afterwards bind the wounds with cloths and apply powders, then add wine and oil, and leave like this for five days; then release it, treat the wound regularly and anoint equally, and give the patient dry meat to eat until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another method of incision is to observe where the swelling and accumulation of pus appear; for sometimes it presents itself in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and other times on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Cut there where the abscess appears and the pus accumulates, and open it according to your ability; be careful not to cut an artery, for if blood flows out, the patient may die from loss of blood and moisture evacuation.
de reume	Of rheum.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a disease called "cataract" in the eyes or throat, and it is chronic with no improvement from medical treatment, then the final remedy is cauterization along with cutting of the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	You should therefore make the patient turn their head back when cutting these veins; afterward rub this place with a coarse cloth until you can see the arteries appear, then strap the patient's neck tightly with another piece of cloth; then observe which way the vein flows, and which are the two that lie on either side behind the ears, those being the ones to be replied upon; then mark out these veins, and cut one and then the other with a sharp spatule in two parts, so that your incision reaches down to the bone, doing this across the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see it, push the spatula beneath the artery and the cup above, cutting as deeply as necessary through it.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is cut open, blood will always spurt out upwards continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open easily to palpitation, you must measure a space of three fingers wide and make an incision until the bone; the quantity of blood that comes out should be six fingers deep, perhaps more or less depending on how much the patient can take and the fullness of the arteries. Then look at the wound: if there is any bone still visible, cauterize it so no abscesses form, then pull back the skin and bind the wound; apply treatment until it heals up.
de emigrainne	Of a migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When an old migraine comes with a persistent cough due to the moisture of tears and heat in the temples, along with old frequent seizures and similar symptoms, and despite being treated with various medical cures, none provide relief - we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have explained.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	The method of extracting them is as follows: the patient should shave the hair from their temples and pay attention to the artery that appears on the temple, for it becomes visible through its pulsation, but may be harder to see in some people with cooler skin tones; if it is less visible, the patient should constrict their neck with some cloth, then rub the area with a coarse cloth and apply warm water until the artery becomes clearly apparent; then take the spatula which has this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then scrape the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then pull it upwards with pincers, and remove any remaining membranes from each side; and if the artery is delicate, turn it towards the tip of the hook, then cut off that part according to the size of two joints.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, the blood will not flow out freely at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	Pull out the blood from six places to three; and if the artery is large, you must tie it in two places with a strong double thread of silk so that there will be no further swelling before the wound heals, and blood flows freely; then cut off the excess between the two ties at the same time, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with the knife cautery until the bone is exposed, so that the joints are severed; this is a delicate operation if the patient has no fever and is of warm constitution.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery is helpful to finish moisture; therefore, it is of great help for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, one should fill the place with old cotton and apply well-made bandages; and when you release them, treat with dry medicated dressings that promote flesh growth, and with bandages until it heals; and if blood escapes from the artery while you work, quickly cut it off with cautery, or use vitriol and squeeze it in your hand to stop the bleeding; and if you don't have these present, put your thumb over the wound until the blood coagulates, then wash the area with cold water until the bleeding stops, and apply pressure as needed; and what is tricky and lighter in extracting an artery is that you cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery in two parts, but make sure the incisions are deep to retain heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too thin, they retain less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have a gap of two fingers' width between the two blades, and then when you have pressed them into place, put the hot iron on top until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein into two places; let these be separated by the two shoulders since this cautery is not continuous throughout. And this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes flow down from the veins that are above the top of the head with force, and it does not benefit to treat it with medicine, and you see the patient's face turn red, and feel a sensation of trembling on their forehead; and their eyelids are thin and moist so that the hairs inside have fallen out, and they are scalded by the heat of the tears, then this treatment is necessary.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», and it is that you do to the rear of the patient who has this illness the hairs which he has on his forehead; then make three incisions equally spaced along the length of their forehead. One incision should be positioned in the center, extending downward toward the nose; the other two are placed above the temples near the hairline. Take care not to cut into any arteries located at those points and keep your hand away from where the mandibles connect. Each wound should measure three fingers across when closed together. Have ready a piece of sponge cloth with lots of soft fabric strips for absorbing blood; then insert this narrow spatula made up of two parts whose shape looks like:
