de la char des gencives	On the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a fleshy growth appears on the gums, which the ancients call "albulus"; you must hold it with forceps and cut it at its root, allowing the bowel or blood to pass; then apply ground vitriol or other styptic and drying powders; if this flesh grows back after incision, and does so repeatedly, cut it a second time, cauterizing it: it will not return after cautery; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	of sores
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes sores are found on the gums inside the mouth, rough and unsightly crusts; sometimes teeth are black or yellow and green, so decay has reached the gum, making the tooth stink; you must seat the patient between your hands with his head in your lap, and extract any loose teeth or crusts until nothing remains; do likewise for blackening, greening, yellowness, and other discolorations, cleaning them thoroughly; if what caused this is not removed at first instance, repeat the process on the second and third day until everything has been cleaned; be aware that teeth require various forms of instruments to extract depending on what the work requires, as the rasp used for extracting teeth from outside the gums has a different shape than one used between the teeth; you should possess all these forms and others.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth for its pain that you delay the extraction as much as you can, because it should not be done at all; for it is a highly important substance until such time as there is no excuse to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is forced to extract, you must be certain of which tooth is causing the pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain leaves the patient, and they believe it is in a healthy tooth, leading to the extraction of a good tooth; yet the pain does not leave due to this, as the true cause remains, which we have already seen with these sufferers; and when you are sure of the painful tooth, you must scrape all around it with a strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides; then move it with your fingers or delicate pincers in the first place and gently remove it, so that it is well loosened, then firmly grasp the pincers; and have the patient's jaw in your holy hands between your knees, hold it tight so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth without breaking it, and if it cannot be done, take one of these instruments and gently insert it from each side, moving it like you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is perforated and worn down, you must fill it with small pieces of cloth where the holes are; gently grasp it with the forceps so it does not break when pulling; one must work very carefully around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Be careful not to break it and leave a part behind, as the remaining root can cause even greater pain for the patient.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Beware not to act like the ignorant surgeon, who in their haste and boldness sometimes breaks the tooth, and fails to achieve what we have described; but instead causes great harm due to the remaining roots or broken pieces, as we have often seen; when the tooth is extracted, clean the place with wine or oil and silk; if there is bleeding, which often happens, fill the place with powdered vitriol; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, with which one extracts teeth first, should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you extract the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should have thick bodies so that they do not bend during extraction, and be well-made iron, and have teeth to hold the tooth firmly.
de la racine des dens	From the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains after extraction, you must place moist cotton wool soaked in butter over the socket for one or two days,
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the socket softens, you can insert the forceps which are called 'algefri', giving the head the appearance of a bird's beak; and they should be made like this:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these tongs, then you must uncover the flesh all around the root, and place the instrument known as 'althali', which is a type of pliers, like this:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	Let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps due to this, it is good; if not, then assist with all instruments, of which forms come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you require assistance from this instrument with two blades, here is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron instruments that are used in front of the teeth, as well as this large instrument resembling tongs, which has this form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be outside that it cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their works and the illness show them, because there are such illnesses where the ancients did not teach any instrument for its diversity, and if one breaks from the chariot or the other bones, in that case look for instruments that they need, which I told you, and help with gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be thick and well-holding to hold the bone so that it does not slip away but can grasp and remove it; then restore its place with medicines suitable for this purpose, and if there is any decay in the bone, and it is small, then take out all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, and the form is ugly, especially in virgin women, you must know if the tooth was born after the other teeth  and it's not right where it should be, and can't be treated or filed down: then extract it; and if it's hollow with the tooth, take this instrument of which here is the shape, and is similar to a little beak, and let it be made of iron that's sharp on top
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the gum several times with your hands for the hardness of the tooth, and so you don't move the other teeth, and if it's apparent that one can file it down, then file it with this type of rasp as shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it's also like the rasp used to make needles; and you file the tooth several times with your hands gently, so that it doesn't move when biting; then plane it at the end with any type of rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and hurts the tongue, file down its roughness until it's even, so that it doesn't hurt the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When teeth loosen
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth loosen due to impact or falling, and the patient cannot bite down without them falling out, even after being treated with constricting medicines which prove ineffective, they must be secured with a gold wire, as silver wire turns green and rots but gold does not change; let the wire be neither too thin nor too thick according to the space between the teeth; if you wish to straighten the teeth, take the wire and pass it double through two healthy teeth, then place the loose tooth or teeth in between them until you have reached safely the healthy tooth on the other side; restart the covering process towards where you began and gently yet firmly pull your hand so that there is no movement; let the ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the shoulder joints with a wire using pincers, and join them back together, and put them between healthy teeth, and make sure it doesn't injure the tongue; then leave it so tight for as long as it can stay that way, and if it loosens or the wires twist, tighten it again with another piece of wire; and if it stays in place like this, it will serve you forever, and here is the shape of teeth and how to fix two healthy teeth and two damaged ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place immediately, as we have said; and do not let anyone but a wise and skilled person interfere, and sometimes you make a false tooth from cow bone, placing it where there is a gap, then tightening it like we said, and it will stay in place for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	To cut the tongue's tie.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	This tie that comes beneath the tongue by nature at birth, or due to an accident of a healed wound; and the procedure is as follows: you open the patient's mouth, have their head in your hand, and lift their tongue; then cut the nervous tie broadly so that the tongue detaches from its base, and if there is hardness or swelling caused by sudden injury, insert the uncine and cut this tie broadly; be careful not to go too deep as it may pierce the artery beneath; when you are done, rinse with rose water and oil, or cold water, then place a linen cloth under their tongue; the patient should hold their mouth open each night so that the wound does not heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, apply powdered vitriol to the spot; and if the blood escapes, then cauterize with the fig-shaped cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	if you see it turn red or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a cancerous sore; if it starts to lighten in color and moisture appears, then remove the crust and clean it with a thin spatula, and relieve it on one side and the other; and if blood escapes during your work, apply powdered vitriol until it stops flowing, then return to your work until you have treated everything thoroughly; then raise the area gently with ash and silk, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	From abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes lumps come inside the throat called "godath," which are properly known as tonsils, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, take care: if it is a hard abscess with little sense of feeling and faint color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is swollen, do not touch it with iron due to blood loss; but let it be until it becomes soft, then you can remove it, or else it would rupture on its own; and if it is white in color, moist, and the root is subtle, prepare your tools for cutting, but first ensure that the abscess has cooled down and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, and his chiés soit en ton sain, and li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, and presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; and soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	When you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the onion and fix it into the almond, then pull hard on top as much as you can; and pull something out of the cloth with it, then cover the instrument, from which this is made, that looks like a pair of tongs; and nevertheless the head [of the instrument] is bent, and one side against the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you don't have this instrument at hand, use the pincers, from which this is made:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And they should be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have extracted one of the almonds, extract the other in the same manner; after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, warm water and vinegar, or if there is bleeding, then gargle with water, boiled pomegranate skin or myrtle leaves and similar things until the blood has stopped; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses occur in the throat besides the two almonds, so extract them therefore like the two almonds equally.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that had formed inside her throat; it was a small one, but it almost completely blocked her airway so that she could not breathe through it, and she could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if left like this for just another day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	The abscess was so swollen that two tubes had been inserted through the two nostrils to keep it open.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore hurried and inserted one tube into one nostril, then the other into the other nostril, and I opened her mouth and pressed on her tongue; after inserting a tube into each abscess and cutting out some of it, only a small amount of blood came out; thus the woman's airway was now clear and she began to drink water and then wine, and I did not stop cutting away at this abscess for quite some time; but the abscess would grow again and fill up the space that I had emptied until once more it became very large; so I seared it with a red-hot iron inside her throat: thus it stopped growing any further; from here on in, I left these matters to God.
de l’uve	Of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When rheum descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called a "perpendicular"; and if it is below, thick, and round, it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the sore has healed, and it is subtle, then you must cut it; and for one which is round, gathered together, and not long; and it is bloody or of a false color or black, then you must avoid incising it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner I have described, regarding its whiteness and length, you must make the patient sit facing the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument we have mentioned before; then insert the hook into the eye, and draw it out, and cut it with one of two instruments I said in the incision of the testicles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut any flesh beyond what is superfluous outside the natural limit; for if you remove more, it will be harmful to speech and voice; and after the incision, treat it as we have said in treating the two almonds, and continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears cutting, you must employ an engine for their sense of fear to be cauterized.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	The manner of the cautery is sharp, like a needle.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should place their head in your lap, and then press their tongue against the instrument we mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and seal it with hot sharp liquid so that it is neither too thick nor too thin; and use this device, which has the following shape: [shape description here]
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cauterization. If it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calmly and mix hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, artemisia, and similar herbs, combining all or some of them into a pot with ease; boil and ensure the pot is well-glazed with strong earth, containing within it an instrument pointed like so:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or copper, with one end inserted into the mouth of the patient so that the vapor rises to the eye through the nose until the eye is withered; then repeat often until the eye dries out and make sure not to do this at the beginning of hot abscess emergence because many things happen; nor perform it except during the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and place a piece of egg shell inside the patient's mouth so that it does not become too hot; for the egg shell does not allow the vapour to damage the mouth, and this is a good treatment combined with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often there is an obstruction in the throat due to a fish bone or any other object; therefore, you must extract whatever you can see and press the tongue towards the sun with all your strength so that you can view the object; for what does not appear and remains stuck in the throat, you must make the patient vomit until the food is digested in the stomach; perhaps then the object will be expelled through vomiting; or have the patient swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel [orange peel?], or a lettuce root, or a crumb of dry bread; tie a string to the sponge and then have them swallow it; when it reaches the obstruction, it will expand, and then you can pull it out; if it does not come out with what we have said, take an instrument made of lead in this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instruments be bent at the head so that they can enter the throat more easily, and keep his head raised upwards; watch out not to touch the epiglottis for it may cause choking, nor should you push on the bone too much; better have the patient do it himself because he knows where it hurts more; let him put them down or pull them up as long as they go evenly deep until they reach their deepest point.
de la sansue de la gorge	Of the worm of the throat.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never has the worm been cured by medicine, as I said in the division of treatments; and when it doesn't work, then look into the patient's throat under sunlight, while you press their tongue with an instrument like the one mentioned before.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the leech, pull it out with your little fingernail or use delicate pincers suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if that does not work, take a hairy goose quill and push it down the patient's throat; then insert the hot end of an iron rod into the tip of the quill and repeat this procedure frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And keep the patient soaked in water all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then fill a glass with cold water and open the patient's mouth, pouring it in without allowing them to swallow; keep moving their hand frequently and as soon as the leech senses the water it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not fall out as mentioned above, then fumigate the patient with asafetida using the instrument I described for smoking the eye; do this several times because it will eventually drop without causing any damage.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the method of fumigation is that you take a pot with visible coals and cover it with a perforated lid in the middle, through which the head of the instrument should be inserted; then add your fumigating substance, and have the patient put the end of the tube into their mouth and close their mouth so that the smoke doesn't escape but instead goes down to the tonsils. The tonsils will now become red, and if they don't, repeat the fumigation several times; let the patient suffer from thirst, eating salty things without drinking water; eventually, it will be necessary for them to spit it out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to treat tonsils is like a curved pair of pliers when you can see it, designed to enter the throat; and it resembles a bird's beak with roughness like a file, so that whatever it grasps cannot be released. Here is its form: [drawing or image could go here]
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to the following recollection from this book and others, and they vary in perforation and size; they occur in two ways: one is due to its own nature, and the other because of moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for those places where they occur in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For abscesses of the head are different from those of the anus, and abscesses in fleshy places are different from those that occur in joints, and each has its own treatment.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And one should not lance abscesses when the bowels are dead according to their condition; and for those that must be lanced when they are ripe, and do not die according to their condition, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses develop around joints, and one leaves them until they are completely rotten, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint become corrupted, which is why this causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Where an abscess is located near the main limb, and if you delay perforating it until it dies, this will harm the main limb; when it is near the fundament, pierce it before it dies; and one must not perforate an abscess which appears without complete digestion, unless it is near the fundament, so that it does not rot completely, become elongated inside, develop into a fistula, and cannot heal for a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the moment for perforating an abscess which has died according to its completion, and this is when pain subsides, fever decreases, inflammation of the skin reduces in redness and swelling, and other symptoms; one should perform the perforation at the lowest point of the abscess, where it appears most mobile; making the incision on the surface of the body, and if the abscess is located on the hands or feet, joints, nerves, arteries, and all equal surfaces without curvature.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in fleshy place, it is better that you leave the perforation until it is confirmed to be digested completely, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before then, the body of the abscess will be elongated and full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if for any abscess that is pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to what the limb needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must bring small abscesses with small openings; and for large abscesses, make large openings, and many incisions according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and for such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core, do so when it is fresh like cloth, and is softened, then you must do as with boils: and there are those which are split into three angles, and some that are cut like myrtle leaves, like abscesses from scurf; and there are those in which a round incision is made, other incisions and similar cuttings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement;
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirits sometimes flutter with the exit of bowels, which may cause the patient's death, and you might not notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and once you have pierced your abscess, dry the wound, and examine if the abscess wound is small; and if it's a full-blown ulcer, provide linseed or old cotton bandages; and if it's a large abscess with numerous perforations, ensure each one contains a tent-like structure so that they touch each other; and if you've cut away some of the skin around the abscess, fill this gap with either old cotton or shavings of linen cloth without moisture, bind it until the third day; then remove it, clean it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is bleeding during your work, bring cold water and apply it gently, moistening the cloth, and place it over the bleeding site repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the bleeding persists, apply compresses and poultices, and use the powders I mentioned on various occasions in this book. If it is winter and the skin or abscess is very sensitive, it is appropriate to place warm wine-soaked cloths over them; but if it is summer, and the skin is fleshy, use water-soaked cloths or cold oil-soaked ones instead, for up to three days as we have said; then remove the compresses, dry and treat the wound as required until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this must be universally known in abscess treatment: now I have told you how to proceed with abscess treatment, and here is the chapter.
des soros	scars
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	From the brain of the head come small abscesses, and they are like threads, just like a hen's egg yarn, and there is an abundance of similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some fatty and soft ones where there is moisture like pus; and of the kind that are hard and stoney to cut into, and one must have no doubt if an artery does not interfere.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is such that you test every instrument which is called an "entromissoire", from which its shape originates, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they do so above the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, thoroughly remove and scrape away the skin that contains this moisture, for it will return if nothing is left behind; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if present; if not, use water and salt, apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; this will draw out whatever remains from the night before.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you know for certain that nothing remains from night to night; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess persists in a fatty area, remove it in this way from end to end; cut away your edges and scrape off all the skin around it, focusing on draining out as much pus as possible where it lies; but if an artery opposes you, then do what I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this for an abscess if it is a hard one, and of cutting and treating as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	He cuts into the hard abscess and moist tissue, which is less painful, as they contain little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And for some of these abscesses or bumps where there is no moisture involved, I recall one abscess that I lanced from the head of an elderly woman; and I found it as hard as a stone, rough and white, and could not break it; had anyone struck it with any instrument, they would have caused her as much harm as if it were a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	Other abscesses that occur on the head are those which come from children's heads and at the roots of their ears, should always be lanced as low down as possible to allow for drainage; they should then be treated appropriately.
des scrophules	Of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often these abscesses occur on the neck, and under the arms, and in other places of the body, and they are very common, and become intertwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own place, just like the abscess of the head and other swellings we have mentioned earlier; there are many similar cases.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	Some contain moisture, and there are others that are malignant and refuse to respond to treatment.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that are well-disposed to treatment and resemble the colour of the body, move from side to side without being too close to any nerve in the neck or artery, and is not deep; you must cut it on top, peel back its skin on each side, and stretch open the two lips of the heart with hooks if necessary, just as we have said before about abscesses in the head; drain it thoroughly, be sure that you do not damage any nerve or vein, avoid sharp instruments so that the hand does not slip, and do not go too far ahead to cut what should not be cut.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not allow you to work, then put in the wound ground glass or some powders that stop bleeding, and hold the wound; leave it until the abscess is eased, and the wound is softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding is stopped, return to your work until you complete it; then check with your right index finger if there remain any small scabs, cut them and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large wound in the root of the scab, it is not fitting that you cut that scab at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall by itself without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton steeped in Egyptian ointment, and heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove the entire scrofula, you must then join the two lips of the wound together, stitching them now, as there is no excess tissue left due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you must cut out the root of it and extract the pus, then stitch it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For scrofula with excess tissue, pierce it where the dead flesh ends; and perforate it as described before, depending on the situation, then treat it with poultices and similar things so that it does not corrupt what remains of the corrupted tissue; and when the wound is clean, treat it with ointment to promote flesh growth until it is healed.
de squinance	to a twisted place
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the operation to cut into the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is a record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those with squint, it is necessary that the fold in the throat called the "epiglottis" be avoided; and do not seek treatment from them, because all the veins and passages of the patient are affected by those who have abscesses hot in the mouth, or in the throat or tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is in the passage of the windpipe, it is necessary to cut through the epiglottis to avoid the danger that comes from suffocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, when we want to split the epiglottis, that we split it below III circles or IIII with a small crosswise incision between the II circles or through the quantity of the wound on the surface, not in the cartilage; and these veins are suitable for the section of the epiglottis where there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from inside.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat thoroughly, then cuts the heart until reaching the windpipe; and remove the blood vessels, should you see anything, and then cut the surface as we have said; and it is proven by the section of the windpipe which must be through the broken place, and by the defect in the voice; and leave the wound open for some time.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed which you fear will lead to strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound from the heart, and cut it completely clean without the cartilage; then administer medicines that foster flesh growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Al-Bukhari states that one should not proceed until the throat is entirely blocked, and the patient is judged to be at death's door, and breathing stops.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cauterize the epiglottis so that the patient cannot inhale, and they breathe through the wound, thus saving them from death; and for this reason the ancients ordered to leave the wound open until the evil of the illness has passed, and it passes in three or four days. Then they ordered to sew up the wound and cure it until it is cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a damsel took a knife and thrust it into her throat, cutting part of the windpipe; I was called to treat her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found blood issuing from it, I knew she had not cut a vein or inflicted damage on her throat, and breath was escaping through the injury.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, treating it until it was clean; all that befell the damsel was hoarseness of voice, and afterwards she returned to her senses; thus I say that there is no fear in cutting into the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the thick throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cist apostemes is called "hernie de gorge", and it is a large abscess in the colour of jaundice, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural, and accidental; where there is no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is of two kinds, one resembling fat lumps, and the other type resembles an abscess that comes from our arteries; and there is fear, and it should not be treated with fire unless it is small, and you must test and probe thoroughly: if you find it similar to a fatty lump, and it cannot open into any vein, then cut it as you would a boil, and treat its covering entirely, until it is healed perfectly.
des nous	de us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of addressing us, all of which I will describe here; now it is necessary that I explain the entire distinction between our group and theirs.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that theirs is marked by chills and fever, until the boiling passes, and the putrefaction is complete; then the fever and chill subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	Among our group there is neither chill nor fever nor pain, and it contains I syfac, which is its own sack and is according to the colour of the body, and begins like a boil, and becomes large; and there are two types, either hard or moist, and very varied in colour as I have said before.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	You must, when you come to the treatment of the bone, first test and inquire about all the instrument called an "introducer," according to how its form will appear in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of examining abscesses inside us is that you take hold at the moistest place you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers back and forth until you know the instruments have pierced the heart, then do so according to the size of the abscess; then remove the introducer, taking care not to drop it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If running moisture is short and whatever its color, do it as I have said for other abscesses; if after the introducer no moisture comes forth, know that it is fatty, so make a cross-shaped incision, take pincers, and gently peel away the skin on either side and hold the coat in which it lies so you draw it healthy with the bone; and if you cannot draw it out whole, then pull it apart piece by piece until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if anything remains inside, it will cause the wound to return many times; and if a small piece remains, and it irritates you, fill the wound with some sharp corrosive powders, constrict the wound, apply warm soothing abscess-relieving substances over it, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the swelling is large, cut both lips of the wound, and treat it with something that promotes flesh growth.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the wound opposes you or others are in a hurry, apply powdered vitriol, leave it on for two or three days until the wound rots and stops bleeding; then return to cut away whatever remains of the rot.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the shapes of the instruments used for incision, and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small; there are also three types of squares called "albaret", and one type called a "breb"; these also come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, to probe fistula abscesses; they are like the needles used for sewing wounds, made of yellow brass, iron or silver, with those made of yellow metal being more valuable; they are also coated in black pitch when probing fistula abscess cavities; they too come in three sizes: large, medium, and small depending on the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the uncines are very similar, as you can see here: large, medium, and small; and there are uncines with two curves in three ways too; and there are uncines with three curves, also in three ways; and there are uncines with two curves, and uncines with only one curve, also in three ways; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of these has what one makes sharp, and there are some that do not cut the flesh except from one side, with which one removes the scabs, so as not to damage the vein or nerve; and for these introductories there are the dull-pointed ones in many, so that the patient does not perceive them when opening an abscess; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and one should only use them on fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, armpits, and similar areas; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling a scab remover, according to this shape, with which one stops the blood flow.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is sometimes put back into place by clamping veins or arteries together, but other times according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, appearing like the breasts of women; they remain ugly and swollen, and if one wishes to cure them, it must be done according to this form from line b. to g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape the fat and fill the wound with medicated meat, then bring together the two lips of the wound by stitching them up, and treat it until it is healed; if the breast sags downwards and its consistency is softened due to its size like that in women, make two incisions above it through two similar cuts so that one may be attached to the other at each end so that the largest line contains the smaller according to this form from line b. up to g.; then remove the skin between the two lips, and take out the fat, and use what we have mentioned about stitching and powders, and anything else necessary for treatment until it is healed; if it isn't healed or the incision isn't complete because the patient doesn't want to rest or due to loss of blood, you must fill the wound with wet cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; leave it until it drains out all remaining fatty tissue then treat him again until he is fully healed.
des apostemes des asselles	Of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come beneath the armpits are like hard scrofula, or it has sides, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b. to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the entire bowels that are in the abscess are emptied, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it there until the next day, then remove all the cotton and treat gently until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is similar to scrofula, treat it as we have said for scrofula incisions, and if the wound contains bowels, apply cauterization as mentioned before.
de la routure de l’artere	From the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it is fused together, there are often abscesses that form, and likewise, the vein also becomes swollen and abscessed; you can identify this when it is due to the artery because the abscess will be long in its entirety; and when you feel it with your fingers, you will sense a constriction; if it is for the vein, then there will be visible swelling on the surface; it is foolish to cut into such an abscess, especially when it is located below the axilla and at the breastbone, or around the neck and in many other areas, as it would be very extensive.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must therefore avoid iron treatment and do so for the one at the head as well, and in case of swelling due to a ruptured artery, make an incision above the skin lengthwise; then open the cut with scissors, and separate the artery from its surrounding tissues until it is exposed; insert a needle underneath and pierce through to the other side, securing the artery by running a double thread through two points as I have shown you in the extraction of the two arteries found at the temples; then press on the area between the two threads with your finger until all blood has been expelled from there, and treat the abscess; gradually release the pressure point so that the ties come loose; proceed to clean what has been treated, ensuring it is properly healed; if the abscess results from an incision into a vein, you should hold in place with your hand whatever part of the abscess you can reach while keeping all skin intact, then insert another needle underneath where you are holding the abscess with your hand and pierce through so that there is a double thread on both sides; fasten the abscess by tying off either side as I have explained to you using one end of the two-part string; if you suspect this will not hold, place yet another needle at any point along its length directly beneath the incision made with the first needle and secure these threads in four places; cut away all excess from the heart of the abscess until nothing remains but what is tied off; apply a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil over it before administering further treatment in form of tenting or ointments to ensure complete healing.
des apostemes des ners	Of abscesses of nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses occur in nerves when they are damaged or due to excessive work, and similar things.
