Certaines fois vient rupture dans l'angle, comme nous l'avons dit, et les tissus deviennent apparents ; mais aucun intestin ne descend vers le cou, et s’il y en a un qui descend, il est peu nombreux et réparé à chaque heure ; néanmoins, s’il reste trop longtemps dans cet état, la blessure ou le séphac augmente jusqu'à ce que l'intestin descende ; et cela arrive par l'extension du syfac qui est dans l'angle, comme nous l'avons dit, car il est étendu, puis adouci et enflé les tissus deviennent apparents ; et la guérison s’opère par cautérisation, comme nous l'avons mentionné auparavant; et parfois, elle est guérie avec du fer de cette manière : le malade est souvent couché sur son dos entre tes mains, puis coupe le lieu de la rupture enflée d'un large diamètre correspondant à trois doigts ; ensuite retire le syfac qui est sous la peau que tu as ouvert, puis prends l’aiguille et place-la sur le lieu apparent du syfac; appuie l'aiguille au fond du ventre, puis coupe les deux tissus apparents du syfac au-dessus de la tête de l'aiguille, et coupe chaque côté ; ensuite retire la tête de l'aiguille, sans couper du syfac ni étendre l’œuf ou autre chose, comme je te l’ai expliqué dans le traitement de la ramification des intestins; puis soigne-le en suivant le traitement des plaies.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you treat the child, clean him/her thoroughly and cure the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The surgeon is constrained, and has no appearance in the fracture; cautery is more suitable here, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	From softening of the tendons of the neck.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	In many cases the tendons of the neck are softened in certain men due to softening of the internal muscles and this is visible. And when one wishes to treat it, you must make the patient lie on their back; remove the softened tendon from the natural skin, then sew together both lips with a stitch. If wished, cut away the superfluous part of the softened tendon into three or four firm stitches, then cut between these and cure as other wounds, until healed and remove stitches.
dou chastrement	Le castration.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castrations are forbidden in our law, and for this reason, I would prefer not to speak of it in this book; and it is only necessary for two reasons: one is so that the surgeon can know how to respond when asked about it and perform the cure; and the other, because we often need to castrate certain animals to assist us, such as goats, sheep, cattle, and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castrations are performed in two ways: either by traction or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the method we perform through traction, have the animal sit in warm water until the testicles are softened and hanging; then take them in your hand, gently stretching them until they are repositioned and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of castration by cutting: you must hold the animal and press its skin with your left hand, then bind it with a cord, and strike each testicle once with one blow when they are well-stretched; leave some of the skin from the scrotum and the fine membrane that covers the vessels; this method of castration is more certain than that which is done by ligature, because after the latter operation something may remain of the testes, whereby lust will be excited in the animal; then treat the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Of hermaphrodites:
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is of two kinds in men: one is when between the two testicles there appears a structure resembling the opening of the female organ, where it may have hair and sometimes emit urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is so in women, and has on the wrist as well as a rod and two knots.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of men and women is such that you remove all joined flesh, and treat them like other wounds; in the second manner, for men whose urine comes out through the skin above the knot, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Of the testicle.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Testicle is a joined flesh on the natural part, so ugly to behold; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must hold the excess of the testicle with your hand or pincers, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest blood flow out, then treat any other cure as you would until it is healed; and there is another flesh that grows at the mouth of the wound, and remove it, and perhaps it will burst, and it is like a cow's disease, thus the ancients called it "cow-like illness".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	You must cut it as we have said for tentigene, and treat until it is healed.
de erratique	Of erratic.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic is when the woman's nature is not pierced or the opening is small; whether it is natural by birth or an accident due to illness that has occurred; or if it is attached to flesh, a subtle sinew or tendon, and remains completely inside the belly, side, below, or wherever; and prevents conception, childbirth, and perhaps flowers (a period) from occurring; this knowledge is gained through observation of the womb.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If it protrudes obviously, use your fingers or a rod (rait).
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is very soft, and it is close to the two lips, hurry up and do this: put your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then stretch the two lips apart so that the soft cervix becomes rounded, and cover the os uteri; then take wool, dampen it in oil, and place it on the spot, and make the woman lie with a man every day until it cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the cervix is hard and thick, you must cut it with the spatula which looks like myrtle leaves.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the os uteri is made of new wood, suspend it on a hook and cut it; and have ready some medicines that stop bleeding, such as dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg white; then bring a large piece of lead pipe so that the wound cannot heal; and let this go on for a long time, and bring her a dry linen tent; then treat other wounds until she is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when a child is born with a caul, you must cut it according to this method, unless there are embedded abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that is embedded in the caul, one must not attempt to cut it open.
des emorroides	Of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually bleed, and when hemorrhoids are old they become dry; I have previously spoken about their similarities to other conditions, as well as the signs, and now I shall tell you which ones can be cured.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and dry hemorrhoids, when they are completely inside the anus and cannot be felt, should not be treated with a cauterizing iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the marsh, where one can feel them, are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	You must therefore place the woman in a cold house, then extend the tumor with tongs and cut it at its roots, then sprinkle it with medicines that restrain blood flow, such as dragon's blood, incense, and similar things; then press her feet against the wall for an hour, then immerse her in cold water; if bleeding occurs, have her sit in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate rind, galls, and other like substances, and then take barley flour, mix it with honey and egg white, and make an ointment to be placed on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops bleeding, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, have the patient undergo cupping therapy on their back and breasts without causing injury; then take linen, dampen it in juice of plantain or goosefoot with old wine, and apply to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Once the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until it heals; and the one called 'albathir' is red, resembling a harsh scab, so you must cut it as I said for 'thelul'; and then treat it until it heals.
des apostemes de la marris	Abscesses of the scrotum.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many types of abscess develop in the scrotum, such as cancer, stony abscess, herpes, cysts, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary then that I speak in this treatise of the hot abscess which forms in the armpit, which is not one of those abscesses that fall away; and if you wish to know the work of iron, look to see if the abscess is acute at its beginning, full of heat and fever, and if it turns red when you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not hasten to pierce it, but let it die until the pain subsides; then have the patient sit on a seat, and provide two small stools for them to lean against, supporting their back and bringing their feet up towards the outside of their legs; and let their thighs be spread apart, with their arms placed beneath their knees, binding them well with a strong bandage. Then suck out the pus from the right side, and introduce the instrument used to open the armpit, which will later form here; and when you wish to introduce this instrument, it is necessary that you first make a small incision in order to know the depth of the armpit, so that what enters with the instrument does not go too deep inside, and does not harm the patient. If the instrument is larger, one must cover the depth of the armpit with cloth, so that the instrument does not cause pain; and it should have its horn at the top, while you hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess opens, and one makes it soft with their hand, they must cut open its head or spit out pus; and when the bowels are empty, then one should place wet tents soaked in rose oil or dry green oil into the wound; put the tent deeper inside the wound's cavity and add clean woolen cloth wet in water or boiled mashed mallow on top of the abscess and wrist; heal it after two days of this treatment until the wound is healed. In some cases, one should raise the abscess and wound by enema with water and honey, then with water or roots of iris and long aristolochia boiled; then go back to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is covered in the cavity, then one should be careful to not burn with iron; but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary first for the midwife to know the nature of childbirth and its signs: when you see the woman press downwards and wish to smell something: then the child hastens to come out quickly; therefore, know that these births are natural, and the infant comes out head-first, with the midwife assisting him/her; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press her belly so that the infant comes out soon; for when he descends face down, the midwife assists him, and the woman is relieved of excesses through proper delivery; and those who come otherwise do not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes it comes feet-first, and the body or shoulders come out first, or the hands, or it may come out belly-first, or often with other poor positions; the midwife must therefore be wise and skilled in these things, avoiding mistakes and deception, and I will show you all the ways to help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out headfirst due to natural birth, and the woman labours painfully, and her strength is weak, have her sit on a saddle or be held by women; then stimulate her nature with oil from fenugreek that has been cooked, and insert between her two legs the small spatula of which here is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And split the amniotic sac, and cut her nail so that the moisture within flows out; and press on the woman's belly until the child descends, if it does not descend, then administer an enema to the woman with a mixture of fenugreek mush and sesame oil; then make her sneeze using condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for one hour: now extract the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out first, you must gently pull them back one at a time; and if they cannot be pulled in, place the woman on a chair, and lift her feet upwards; then stand up the chair on the ground, and hold onto the woman, so she does not fall when rising; and if the hands still cannot be pulled in, and the child is dead, cut its hands with the knife mentioned before, and extract the child, resetting it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the emergence of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child rises to its feet, you must push them up; and then turn them back and forth until they are steady; then take one foot and stretch it gently.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When they jump up to their thighs, you must instruct them to grasp it, and make them sneeze hard; if they jumped freely, may God wish it so.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if they were not able to do so as we said, then turn them back and forth until their form is natural again.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For at that point, they will be lightly built.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if they do not succeed as we said, then take some musk root and almond oil, and molten gum, and grind it all in a mortar; apply this ointment to the genital region of the woman inside and outside, then have her sit in warm water up to just below her ribs; once she is softened from beneath, make a collar of myrrh for her, place it underneath, and leave it there for an hour; then have her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze hard, and hold her mouth and nose shut, gently press her belly, for the child will now jump.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the exit of the child onto his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes out in this manner, put the nurse's hands here and there; then let her be attended to by someone else for her neck, and hang his feet downwards, and let him lie on the bed; and fold his hands here and there, then take his hands on her stomach, remove the cushions from underneath so that she is lowered down; if the child does not breathe, take his feet and move them vigorously, then push up his belly, then put both your hands inside; assist the child in breathing here and there; instruct the woman to hold herself until the child has exited.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the exit of the child that comes out with one hand hanging downwards
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I must arrange to bring the hand back: if you cannot pull it back, have her get up and walk; if she can't walk, then make her lie on the bed, and vigorously move her legs upwards; then administer the medicated oil that I have described above; if she does not deliver the baby, then have her sit on a chair, then try to bring the hand back; and assist the child in breathing according to his natural form, and make her sneeze, and instruct her to hold herself until the child has completely exited.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	Of the emergence of the child onto its mother's neck, and it has spread out its hands, and its face turned towards her back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I agree that the midwife should hold her hand, then turn it back and forth, and move it lightly; when it is even, apply some moistened wool mixed with oil, as we have said, and tell her to move it gradually; once you've done this, make her sit on a chair, and ask her to cough; make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same way for all secondary dislocations.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way during the secondary dislocation, scrape away the secondary material with your nail until the moisture is drained; if the child falls on its face or neck, pull it from under her nose so that it's not obstructed, and kill the child; then push the child inside again until you've placed it correctly, and tell the woman to cough once: then it will come out gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	On dislocation of the hip joint.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You should know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born at once; this is not a strange thing, and it often happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two heads are strange and do not live, if they have such a name; I know that they be multiplied, and they come apart through the surgeon's work which divides them, which is tied to their navel; sometimes they issue naturally like one child alone, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue violently, then treat them as we have said, and let the surgeon be skilled, and do his work quickly and lightly; and act thus for their salvation.
de plusors enfans	from many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	There are seven or more formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, and they are all shaped like children by the measurement of the glorious blood, and it is fitting that the priest knows all this, for perhaps similar things may happen to him; he should act accordingly.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman for a dead child in the womb, as I said in the division, and there is no natural delivery, and you must perform manual labor; it is necessary that you know if the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fear of death. The woman should be positioned on her back, with her legs elevated, and her hips inclined downwards. Have an assistant hold her down firmly onto the bed so as not to hinder the extraction of the child. Then, anoint the mouth of the womb with moist oils mixed with a poultice of althea and fenugreek seeds and flaxseed; then grease your hands with these same oils and poultices. Afterwards insert your fingers gently into the womb. Take care that if the foetus is presented headfirst you do not injure its face by inserting your fingers in places where they should not go, but rather in a suitable place for the extraction of the child's body parts; prick with the finger(s) in their eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under the beard or around the jawline or near the sides. If however, if the presentation is feet first then insert your fingers between its thighs and at the midsection and prick there as well while being careful not to touch any vital organs. Make sure you are holding onto one of your fingers with your right hand and use the curvature between two fingers from your left hand for leverage when pricking into various parts such an eye or neck etc., until finally extracting whatever remains inside through gentle pricking motions using all available digits at once in any direction possible including upwards towards the head region if need be according to what has been described earlier on. This is how you should form your finger:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then insert another hook opposite the first one, or use a third if needed to ensure equal extraction; then stretch it evenly by moving from side to side, to get it out, and make sure the hooks are serrated to hold it in place, just like this:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	If any part remains inside, anoint the wound with one of your fingers coated in oil, then push against that part and pull the other part; if there's still a point remaining, place this hook higher up and keep doing so until it comes out entirely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	If one hand comes before the other and you cannot reset it due to constriction, then you must wrap it in a cloth until it is fully extended; cut off the skin at the wrist joint or with a knife, and do likewise for the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; 
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is on their feet, then the traction is light, and the alignment to the mouth of the womb is also light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If they are trapped in the belly or pelvis, it is necessary that you extract them with the cloth wrapped around your hand; and make an incision into the belly or pelvis until the moisture inside flows out; and if other parts have been removed but the head remains, push your hand up against the base of the womb, and draw the child forth to the mouth of the womb; then insert one or two fingers, and pull it through; and if the mouth of the womb is narrowed due to hot inflammation therein, there must be no effort made to enlarge this, but rather moist and fatty substances should be applied; administer plasters, as well as mild water-based softening and moisturizing agents.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on their side and you can make them lie flat, follow what we have said for a living infant; but if it does not work, then cut it into pieces and leave nothing of the caul.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	Once you have done this and the child is treated as we said for hot abscesses that come in a womb, if discharge of blood occurs, it should be bathed with cold water while being held still, and other treatments will follow.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had contained one child who died, then another was conceived on top of it and the other died too.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess formed on her breast and swelled until it opened up, beginning to emit a foul smell.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought long about it, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong attracting plaster, and an bone came out, then after some days another one followed.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, for the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it might be the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I felt the wound and extracted several bones until the woman improved; she lived for a long time with one piece of bowel missing; I have never forgotten this chapter except that when masters find an unusual case, they must know how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring the marrow to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the form of the pressor, for which we have two straps; and turning back to the second head of the two limbs.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle than those of the restrictor, and they should be made of ebony or boxwood; the mouth of the trunk should be two inches wide, and the margin of the trees should be one inch; it should be a palm and a half long; and between the two limbs are two adjustments of this same wood, which are firmly attached to each other at one end and at the other, being half a palm or slightly more in length; these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the marrow to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, should be made of ebony or boxwood, resembling a pair of forceps; it will have two jaws with two adjustments, as you see here, one palm in length and two fingers wide; when you wish to open the mouth of the instrument completely, have the woman sit on the bed, feet hanging down and legs spread apart, then insert the two adjustments placed together into the mouth, and hold the head of the instrument beneath between her thighs; then operate your hand with the entire instrument as if it were forceps, equally so, according to the quantity you wish to open the mouth of the cavity, until she does what is required.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all well-crafted and their designs are varied; when the physician has them ready to use, his work is faster and he is held in higher regard by men for the quality of his treatment.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despair of having the instrument ready at hand, for their need is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second stage of labor is prolonged, you should instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze forcefully, and press your hands over her mouth and nose; if she faints due to this, it is beneficial.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take a pot, make a hole in its lid, and place herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; cook all these herbs or some of them in water over a fire; then insert one end of the pipe into the pot's opening, and keep the other end inside the patient's mouth, allowing the steam to enter her; then make her sneeze as we have explained.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If it escapes the initial injury.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment, and does not go away, instruct the nurse to wet her left hand with oil of sesame or muskroot juice, and then insert it into the vagina, and locate the secondin; when she finds it, she should grasp it and extend it little by little straight upwards, so that the patient does not choke during extraction; but she must move it lightly to the right and to the left, and then pull; it will come out and disengage.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the womb is narrow, we have mentioned the treatment of sneezing and herb fumigation; and if it does not go away with all that we have said, take care not to force the extraction; but you must tie what is at the mouth of the womb to the woman's thigh, then administer a four-fold ointment as an enema; this will ripen and reset it, and it will come out; however, when it does, bad odor may arise in the stomach and head, and harm the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary therefore to use appropriate fumigations for this: some of the ancients have tried fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain her flowers (menstrual flow) and secundines (afterbirth) is as follows:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is of glass, similar to a vase, and has a refined head in the shape of nature (human form), with wide openings above the fire; place the fumigation on the coals, and let it be consumed entirely, then start another.
de percier lou fondement	To pierce the foundation (womb).
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born without their foundation being pierced, but have a thin membrane (amniotic sac) covering it: therefore in the bath she must pierce this membrane with her finger, and not use a sharp probe, lest she injure herself; then place upon it moist wool soaked in wine and oil, and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not heal, insert a plank peg into the hole, and leave it there for several days, removing it when the child wants to go outdoors.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	This wound closure can sometimes occur suddenly from a wound or abscess; you must cut this sudden formation, and it should be treated as described with the plank peg.
de la fistule dou fondement	From the anal fistula.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Anal fistulas that form beneath the anus are nodules and growths which originate from inside or outside the anus in the area between the two parts; when there is a single or multiple fistula, and if this growth has been long-lasting it develops into a wound with moist white proud flesh or soft bumps, and sometimes these fistulas break open; they are recognized by those who experience them during defecation or flatulence, and perhaps a worm may jump out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that perforate up to the bladder, and up to the middle of the penis; they reach up to the hip joint, and as far as the knee's navel.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one recognizes a fistula that perforates the anus, and does not perforate: it is when you insert your index finger into the anus, and gently push a fine needle of brass or iron into the fistula if there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is tortuosity, insert a thin tent made of lead or a horsehair so that you feel the tent or hair with your finger; and if you do not sense it, and there comes no egestion nor wind nor excrement as we have said: know that it does not perforate; hasten to treat it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula pierces all the way to the bladder or the urinary duct, then urine leaks out, and it cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it pierces down to the hip joint, then the wound extends all the way there; if there is no twisting or swelling causing pain around it, then one must simply wait for it to heal naturally, and no medicine nor immediate treatment with ointments will help; in such penetrating fistulas, there is no cure except time and patience, and vain are the foolish surgeons who intervene.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the case of a fistula that is not penetrating and not old, there is hope for healing with iron, as I have witnessed; and this is how one must proceed: the patient lies between your hands on their back; you lift their legs up to their thighs, and tilt their thighs towards their belly; then insert an iron probe or a wooden stick if it's twisted, until you locate where the fistula begins.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the anus, you must insert your index finger there, and if you sense that it has pierced the tendon, and is uncovered where you feel between your finger and the flesh, then know that it is perforated; do not labor to heal it since it cannot be cured.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is said that one can indeed heal some of these cases, but it rarely happens; and the aid one offers here is to heat the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned before, and insert it while hot into the fistula until you reach the anus; do this two or three times, until you know that those faulty tissues are burnt away which resemble bird feathers; then treat with moist bandages smeared in butter, so that any remaining tissue comes out, and then heal with ointment, binding flesh together
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If this cannot be healed in any other way, and if it penetrates within without piercing all the way to the right side of the fundament, and between your thumb and the incision place a thick covering of skin or syfac, and you see the fistula at that which sews the covering of the heart; then cut away from the beginning of the fistula, push forward towards the tent, and cauterize after so it reaches the head of the tent; and the tent will be released and fall out; then clean those faulty skins that appear like a bird's feather, and leave nothing behind.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood defeats you and escapes between yourself and the work, then cauterize it with fire or astringent medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two good things: namely, the burning of adjacent flesh, and the stoppage of blood and drying of moisture; then the treatment of wet tents with butter or crushed substances until the wound heals and bows away, and the flesh burns in the bow; then treat the wounds with softening ointments that harden hard flesh, and they are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	When it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes up to the anus, and is removed from the body, put your finger into the anus, and inquire of it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent and find skin or syphac or flesh between two, where it is about to burst, if there are no other signs of hope and confidence, through administering one of three methods: cauterize it as we have said, cut until deep, or apply tents and treat like before; do not go too deep so that you do not cut the muscle holding the anus together, which would cause incontinence; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will heal, or remove that covering and clean it once it has been cut near to the anus, with tent or other pointed instrument; then soften that faulty flesh found within the wound for as long as you can; then try to restore the wound, and keep the fistula outside of the anus: this is a lighter matter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are formed in this manner: it is when you push the probe into the fistula, and it is located on the side of the anus near the skin above, take a perforated probe with an opening at its head in this shape:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And insert the bent wire into it [the probe], and push the probe with the wire all the way into the fistula until its head is inserted.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it [the fistula] is pierced on the inner margin of the anus, then withdraw the wire from that opening, just as you would insert your finger into the anus; and pull out the head of the wire, and bring together the two ends, and press them against each other, and leave it for one or two days; sometimes restrain [the patient] so that the wire cuts through these tissues that are between them, and excretes; then treat the wound until it is healed and closed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not burst, make it burst by any means you can, unless it is too deeply embedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not suitable to perform the ligation if it is too deeply embedded, and then treat it as we have said until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the sharp-pointed spatula used to make the fistula is very acute on one side and cutting on the other; and not so on the other side, because what should not be cut must not be cut, as you see here:
des emorroydes	From hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: they can be inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there may be small or large ones, which produce blood; sometimes, there is one, sometimes many. They emerge from the anus and at its upper end. But those that come out have little moisture in them, rather a bit of yellowish water or a bit of blood, and they are the color of flesh. To treat hemorrhoids inside the anus, you should instruct the patient to strain themselves to go to the bathroom until the anus is outside, and its edges open; then be quick and grab it with pincers or hold it with your fingernail, then cut at their roots. And if the hook cannot hold them due to moisture, take hold of them in a piece of cloth, cotton, or chamois leather; pull them out with two fingers, then cut them off, and apply some hot powder on them as cauterization. Or you can cauterize them as mentioned in the chapter on cauterization: one can treat them by other means until they are healed. And if the anus cannot come out, then give the patient a mordant and bitter enema to wash what is inside of it so that it may emerge; when patients strain themselves and their edges become outside the anus, there treatment becomes easier. It is such: you grab them with your fingernail or pincers, cut them off, then treat them as we have said until they are healed, taking care to avoid incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to stitch the wound, you should proceed as follows: take a length of thread, insert one end into a needle, draw the thread through until the other end appears on the opposite side; turn over the two ends of the thread under the needle so that they are doubled up and tight. Draw the thread tightly, tie it off with a knot, remove the needle, and repeat this process for all but one stitch which is left open to allow excess blood or fluid to drain out of the wound. Finally apply an ointment made from rose oil or wax onto the wound, cover it with a cloth soaked in the same oil/wax mixture, ask the patient to rest; then leave him be until he passes stool and urine, at which point treat his wounds again using other treatments until they heal up completely
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying of feces or foundation (base/ground)
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is constipation in the intestine, caused by natural constraint, or when the illness is old and medicine has no effect on it.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You must reset the point of a spatula or your fingernail on the bark above it, so that it does not get wet; then treat it until it is firm as necessary; and if it cannot be healed, start the shaving again more vigorously than before, until it bleeds profusely and becomes scaly; then treat it until it is cured.
dou fremit	where there is trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A formica is a small faulty appearance between the body and goes very deep inside it; sometimes it finds cold, and one feels trembling like death all over the body, especially in hands more than other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is such that you take a cane made from a goose quill or a strong vulture feather, and place this cane on the swelling so that the purple circles touch the swelling all around; then turn your hand over the entire cane so that you grasp it all around the swelling, and put it in perfectly, and uproot the swelling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you wish, make one from a brass or iron cane according to this form, and let it be hollow underneath and solid above.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not pierce it, to hold it with your thumb and forefinger, and squeeze it; And if you wish, cauterize the swelling, as is described in the previous chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	Of the form of the clyster.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is the silver clyster made nor of quicksilver, or molten and cast bronze; and sometimes small and great instruments of these are made according as they have been adapted to.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These then which are adapted in the treatment of children and for those who are feeble and suffer pain, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the great and small clyster is above broad, where the bellies are tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if it has a discharge or the bellies are tied, as you see, and the head is pierced within; and have on one side two apertures, and in the other one; and be the bellies where the medicines are put of a beast's bladder or parchment, and be pierced all around with small apertures, and have between each aperture one finger's breadth, then push into these apertures one strong thread of twisted thread bent in an X or elsewhere around, and assemble the belly like a goatskin; and when the medicine is within, so bind it to the instrument before with a strong thread, then clysterize; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the doctor's hands not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg white, or something similar, then gently insert it; then have the assistants squeeze his two hands together until they are both visible, then withdraw the enema, and raise the patient’s legs against the wall, and if the doctor wishes to remove it, hold it as long as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night through, this is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you enema him for a protruding belly disease, and the doctor is in a hurry to remove it, then recommence until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the haemorrhoids are at the anus or abscess, then let the enema be as gentle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle enema with which the skin is tightened.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed the treatment of wounds in the previous section; now we will explain the remedies and medicines used for their care according to the procedure.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, where on the body they occur, and what causes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	Wounds are caused by various things such as the impact of stones, sword cuts and stabs from knives or lances, wood, arrows, or similar objects; they can also be classified according to their location on the body, like wounds on the neck, head, foot, belly, liver, and other parts. I will explain the treatment for each type of wound, starting with those affecting the head as a simple case, since further complications may arise in subsequent chapters.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is due to a stone impact or similar things, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large, and you have slight doubt of an incipient abscess: then let it bleed immediately with the cephalic vein especially if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the bleeding be on the opposite side of the injured part; and keep the patient away from overeating wine and fatty meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, let his meat consumption be reduced, and do not drink any wine or eat any flesh at all; put on the wound, if hot abscesses appear, only moist cotton dipped in rose oil or astringent wine; but if there is no hot abscess, then apply to the wound, while it is fresh with its blood, and has not been moved by air yet, some powder that I will mention shortly; and if the wind moves it, then apply certain ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword cut or similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with stitches, then join them by sewing, as I will explain for wounds in the belly, concerning its suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound exposes bone, is gaping, and holds only by a bit of skin, cut off this piece; then treat the wound with medicine, restore hard flesh in place of leather, and instruct the patient to eat coarse meats, such as beef and wheat puddings, also poultry, and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find rotten flesh on the skin, and it has not reached the bone, cut away all the rot and throw it out, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which will not stop bleeding despite treatment, tie off the artery, and if you find it severed, bind it with a thread; and if this brings no relief, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: you must apply this powder which binds them as soon as the medicine moves in.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The manner of the powder is as follows: take one part incense; two parts dragon's blood; three parts quicklime, and finely grind the powder. Apply it to the wound, pressing firmly until it dries well and joins with all its blood. Then bind it tightly, leaving it untouched if there is no swelling; for the medicine must remain until healing is complete.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes quicklime alone is used when one lacks incense or dragon's blood, but the medicine must have already moved into the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the medicine has moved into an internal wound, then do not apply this powder there; instead use some gentle ointments or a poultice of barley flour made with water and honey until it becomes soft. Then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture occurs along with the wound, and it is minor, then extract it using fine pincers; I will tell you about head fractures later on.
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound occurs on the neck and it is straightforward, there is no significant difference between this and a head wound; however, if the windpipe or artery of the neck is severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the windpipe, there are no other options but to leave it untreated, and put nothing constricting on it, as this damages the windpipe and makes it recede; nor should anything cold be applied to the wound, because the substance of the windpipe is cool, and its continuation upwards is connected with the brain, which is the highest organ in the body. However, the treatment should involve moist poultices: boiled calamine washed in warm water mixed with rose oil, cooked leeks likewise boiled in warm water, or other metallic stones prepared in this manner, along with various ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut it open and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it heals.
