Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and filled with hair and pus, cut them open at a lower level; if an artery is severed and blood flows out, cut it further, tie it off, and cauterize as needed; if the windpipe or heart is damaged but breathing passages remain intact, incise over the heart on the neck of the throat without damaging the throat itself while restoring its natural shape; then compress gently and leave for a few days before treating with healing ointments until healed; if the wound has affected bone and broken pieces are present, remove those you can, and let those you cannot until the wound putrefies, relieving pressure and draining discharge; for fresh wounds apply powder as described previously.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has formed a fistula, treat it as I have described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	Of wounds from lances or knives
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a lance or knife wound, and the wound is deep, examine whether wind escapes from the wound when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is fatal. If it is not deep, and fresh with all its blood intact, do not put powder on it in the first hour nor bandage it for the blood may leave entirely, return to the heart, and kill the patient; instead apply an attracting ointment and dress it twice a day; if you have no ointment, insert old cotton into the wound to absorb moisture, and let the patient sleep on his back for three days or four or more so that he does not suffer any spasm nor ill tremors of the heart or shortness of breath. When these good conditions are present then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure it then with dressings and other treatments until it is healed; if it cannot heal, operate as you see fit to treat the fistula; apply proper wound care after surgery.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a sword or knife incision and it is simple, on the chest or back, treat what is in front of you; if it is large, stitch it; if small, use powder; if it has pierced bone and removed pieces, clean the wound and realign the torn tissues if they are separate; if not separate, allow the wound to fester so as to ease extraction; for other wounds on other body parts apply judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Rupture of the abdomen.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupturing of the belly can be large or small and even minor; from a large wound, sometimes the intestines or their nerves protrude due to this cause and the suturing is more difficult, and at times the smaller wounds are worse than the larger ones because it's harder to put back in the intestines without putting them back piece by piece as they swell up quickly when exposed to cold, making it even more difficult; therefore, a medium-sized wound is better since one can restore the intestine to its place more easily than the others. And know that there are four kinds of abdominal ruptures: two common types occur in the suturing of the belly, and the other two are for the suturing of other wounds in the body, and while these latter two types may be used in any wound they are more proper to the belly and I will explain each one.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and something from the intestine comes out, and it is a difficult thing to treat, it can be done in one of two ways: either due to the small size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or soft cloth in tepid water only, or cook it in water with vinegar and cypress and spike, and apply it to the intestine until the swelling is gone; and sometimes do this with restraining wine, and use mild heat to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subside, moisten the intestine with water or let malves be cooked in water, for by doing so it eases its entry a little; and if nothing can enter, then make a small incision in the wound with an instrument used to remove hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is to use caution when cutting, as one should not cut unless there is great necessity; and this is the instrument to do it: make a cut inside along the curvature and outside, and see here its shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have been ruptured, remount it there according to its natural form in its own proper place, if you are able, for this must be done.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower part of the belly, you must make the patient lie on their back, placing their legs higher than their head; if it is in the upper part of the belly, then place the head and chest higher than the lower parts; and also, if there is a rupture in one of the two halves [of the belly], consider that the affected part should be placed higher than the other; thus you must apply what I say for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds use what is provided for you, then take between your hands a soft and gentle instrument that can hold the entire rupture in its grasp; gather together the lips of the wound; this is how to commonly sew [wounds] -- it's when you take a needle or multiple needles depending on the width of the wound, leaving one finger-width at the front of the wound where you insert a strong thread with a single needle. Pierce through both pieces of skin and through what lies beneath the skin; do this until that part is pierced entirely by the other side, then gather together the two ends of the siphac [?] four times. Then twist a double piece of string around the needle in two parts; assemble the two sides of the wound evenly, leaving one finger-width and insert another needle; tie the thread as you did with the first needle, continuing this process according to what is required for multiple needles until the entire wound is closed off; the needles must be medium size -- between fine ones that cut all the flesh and thick ones which are too big to properly enter. For this reason they should be of a middle thickness and do not insert them beyond the flesh and skin so as not to tear open the wound before it has healed, then trim down the ends of each needle so that they don't cause any pain when you sleep; place some linen or strips of cloth at the tip of these needles for protection. Leave this in until the wound is fully sealed shut. This method using needles is more appropriate for small wounds as only one or two needles are necessary, while another common method uses a second type of sewing that gathers together both sides of skin and siphac with one needle having a strong middle-size thread; once you've pierced through all four pieces simultaneously, return the needle to the starting point in a way similar to how cloth is sewn; leave two finger widths between each stitch. This method can be used on humans -- I stitched up a man who had a wound inflicted by a blade on his belly which was more than one palm wide and opened up intestines that were well over two palms in width, the wound being right through the middle of his stomach.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I repositioned his intestines after they had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound was sutured fifteen days later; I treated him, and he healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the doctors had judged him to be a lost cause and die, but it was a miracle; I did not treat him with any ointment as there were none to be found in that place nor any medicines either; instead, twice daily I placed old cotton on his wound, soaked in honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will explain to you the two proper ways of suturing: take your needle and pass it from outside through to inside; when its eye emerges on the other side, leave the tip of the needle or stylet where it came out, then pierce again from within outwards so that both ends emerge externally; this type of suture is performed like how a furrier sews furs together, you leave one end of the suture material from one side and pick it up on the other, repeating until all suturing has been completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, as Galen describes it properly, is such that some do, who naturally bring the two parts together and apply one head of the wound to the other, in this manner: insert a needle into one head of the incision nearby, and pierce only that place; leave both heads of the wound. Then turn the needle, and make it go through from outside to inside, at the two heads of the wound; then pierce each with another point from outside to inside, in the other two heads of the wound on the opposite side. And this is the ordinary method of suturing and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this word, and some bear witness that one must suture the belly with two needles, each having thread; and you should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew leather straps; and know that when the tear is in the middle of the belly, then it is more difficult to suture than the other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, rather than let it air, clean the intestine, and sew; then apply a powder on suppurating flesh, and if the wound has moved, apply any present ointment until the wound heals; and caustic the thread, and unite the edges, and the gape; then treat the wound as with others, until it is healed; and if you don't have medicines, apply right away when it begins to suppurate old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you don't need other medicines in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will affect the main limbs, it is necessary that you moisten light linen with temperate warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the armpits and under the arms; and if there is pain or putrefaction in the bowels, which often happens, then perform a clister of tepid black wine, especially if the putrefaction reaches the intestine; pierce it inside, and know that when it's the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called 'jeun' cannot be healed when it is injured, and this is due to the delicacy of its veins, and for the subtlety of the entire body, and its proximity to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the abscess jumps out of the wound, reset it backwards like the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned green or black, you must tie up the dark part so that no blood runs from it, for there are veins and arteries inside; then cut away what is between the ties, and place both ends hanging down below the wound until outside to ease its extraction when the abscess falls out, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the mouth
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round and the wound small, it can be restored in some people, for I saw a man wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right of the stomach, and became inflamed and turned into a fistula, from which issued waste matter and flatulence. I treated him according to my ability, and did not cease until he was healed and his skin joined together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him healed, I doubted that the patient would have pain in his belly; and there was no pain, but he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experts said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in this manner: take large-headed thorns, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the thorn has opened its mouth, place it on both lips so that it constricts its opening above; then cut off the head of the thorn, and this will hold such that it cannot become unbound, then apply another thorn in the same way as before, until the wound is completely held together; seal the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, and ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, 
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it heals, is universally called a "fistula", especially when it is covered and closed.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is truly an indurated and white nodulation, where there is no pain felt, and it is also covered like the feather of a bird; sometimes, the wound discharges clear pus, while other times, it is thick; some are small, others sufficient in size; I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound that has not healed and lacks tissue is due to only one of nine causes: namely, lack of blood or matter; its malice; having hard tissue inside and on its lips which prevent new tissue from forming; too much pus; putrefied tissues and poor quality matter; inadequate treatment; the nature of corruption in a pestilence; slow digestion characteristic of a region that delays healing; or the presence of veins or bones; I have previously demonstrated all these causes, their signs, and medicinal treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now you must let me tell you about the treatment of fistula, which is done by manual operation.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistula occurs in any part of the body; for there are fistulas that come to large veins, arteries, nerves, or at the anus, intestine, bladder, some ribs, spinal cord, or any joint of hands and feet; and so on to the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All the fistulas that are of this nature are difficult to treat, and there is only work and ignorance involved; if there is any fistula that does not reach the place I mentioned, and you have faith in its cure, and can identify it, then take a probe made of bronze or iron, whether the fistula is straight, so probe it; but if the fistula is twisted, seek with a subtle thin probe of tin, for tin bends following tortuosity; if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot fully explore it with probes, then clean it by enema through one opening, because moisture passes from one hole to another, cleaning it up; then probe carefully as best you can, so that you may know whether there is bone or nerve present, also whether pus flows out perfectly, and ask the patient thoroughly about pain they feel when you press with your hand, and where they feel this pain; once you truly understand the location of the fistula, if it is far from a joint, nerve, artery or vein, or any place that I have mentioned to you, then treat it as described above, removing all corruption and decaying flesh inside; after which cure so that it is healed, and if the fistula is deep at its proper site, cut down upon it thoroughly as much as possible, followed by immersing probes in hot water medicine and inserting them up to the head of the fistula, until the redundant matter remaining at the bottom has been eroded away; then apply stimulating ointments that heal healthy flesh, until it heals; if it does not heal with this treatment, cauterize as we have said, and if bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If wound or abscess does not trouble your principal limbs as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered with signs of decay and blackening, wait until all rot has been removed, then treat the surrounding tissue by cutting away any infected material until it is clean; and if it is not healed, and swelling returns like before, know that you did not go deep enough: uncover and probe again so as to be at the bottom, remove all corruption, restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the rot is too deep for you to reach it; there are other tools provided by nature; and if some small bone has decayed, and you can remove it with pincers, extract it using suitable instruments for such a task, but if many bones have been affected, take them all out at once, leaving none behind; and if moisture obstructs your work, yet presents no problem or fear, cut through both flesh and bone until the bones are free.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them within an hour, apply something that causes festering to the wound, and let it rot away the flesh around the bones; then they will more easily reset the bones; and if this is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh, scrape only the corruption until all blackness is removed, then restore the wound; but if a great part of the tissue is corrupted and goes down to the marrow of the bone, you must care for it and cut away all that is corrupt, then cure it so that it may heal; I will tell you about a fistula which befell one man in his leg, from whom you can take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from an internal cause, so that the matter came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess which had no outward opening; but the doctors in their foolishness worked on it so much that they opened up the abscesses, and a great deal of pus ran out, and became fistulas, and there were many holes which all discharged foul and moist matter from his body; and many physicians put cures around it for two years, and among them was no wise man in this art, until I was called upon, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was treated, and that which flowed out of the holes in great quantity; and the young man's flesh became red and took on a yellow color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one came against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hastened and cut into one of the holes until I exposed a part of the bone, and found it corrupted and perforated, with the corruption reaching deep into the bone; I cleaned what appeared to be the corrupted bone, hoping there was no other corruption beyond what I removed; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines over a long period, but it would not heal; so again I started anew, exposing the bone as before, and found the corruption had spread further into the bone, which I then cleaned, removing it, and endeavored to heal the site; yet I could do no more than cut around one palm of the bone, finding it all too soft, then restoring it with medicines; and it healed swiftly, mending quickly, requiring no further treatment except for the weakness of the patient who couldn't endure more, and my fear of his death.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For he bled often during the evacuation, but he was entirely cured, and in place of the bone, a hard flesh grew, which had good properties and caused no harm or opposition at all, neither before nor after.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be treated this way: take a linen thread, and strain it over the head of the exposed bone, and have someone pull it upwards; and place another larger thread of linen on top of the flesh that covers the bone, stretching the head so you may push away the corrupted flesh, exposing the site where you wish to operate without cutting or harming the flesh; and place a red-hot iron or board underneath the bone in order to cauterize the corrupted flesh; it is necessary to treat as much as one can see and feel of the corruption, treating again if needed.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part of it, uncover all the flesh; then place a hot iron underneath, and with the help of silk thread remove the corruption from one side to the other, and let the suture be made as long as the length of the corruption has been measured out, just like we said before. And if the corruption is in the joint, cut off the corrupted joint and attach the bone on the other part; and if the corruption is in the continuation between two joints, there's no other way but to remove it by cutting; and if the corruption is located at the wrist of the hand or the ankle of the foot, this thing will be very difficult for you. Nevertheless, you have to investigate the said corruption and how it opens up before your eyes, and then cleanse it in every possible manner without harming the vein or nerve. Know that there are many kinds of cutters and silk threads to remove these bones according to their position, appearance, size, subtleness, length, shortness, hardness; therefore, each type of work must be fitted with its tool. Know also that your work will show you which instrument you need by the knowledge acquired from this art and by considering the kind of sicknesses; so think about what tools you need according to their use.
dou feu	From fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head spoils either from within or from without; and when you have treated that corrosion with medicinal cures, and it does not improve, then you must cut off that limb up to the place where the corrosion originates, so that the patient escapes through this means of death, or by evil, which is greater, because of the loss of a limb; and there are signs such as the limb becoming black, so that it seems burnt from fire, and after blackening, for that corrosion moves from member to member, and seizes the whole body; you must hasten to cut [it off], and if this is due to the sting of some venomous beast, like a sea scorpion or snake and similar creatures, if the corruption is at the head of the finger, then cut it off, and do not give space for it to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; 
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	Et si décolement de sang vient quand tu ouvres, cautérise le lieu sans délai, ou applique certaines poudres coagulantes; puis reviens à ta médecine jusqu'à ce qu'elle soit achevée, ensuite attache le membre avec un bandage adéquat, et soigne-le jusqu'à ce qu'il guérisse; je vais te raconter quelque chose qui est arrivé à un homme au pied: il avait une tache noire ressemblant à une brûlure de feu, et cette corrosion apparut d'abord sur son orteil, s'étendant jusqu'à tout le pied; quand l'homme vit la corrosion, il se hâta de couper le pied, et fut guéri; longtemps après, la corrosion revint sur le doigt de sa main, et il vint me voir, je lui appliquai des agents répercussifs après avoir purifié son corps, mais les corrosions ne pouvaient cesser; il voulut que je lui coupe la main, ce que je refusais, car j'avais espoir de faire reculer le mal; je craignis aussi qu'en lui coupant la main, il ne meure, sa constitution étant faible; l'homme se désespéra, retourna chez lui et se hâta de couper sa main, et fut guéri; je n'ai relaté cette histoire que pour que l'on fasse autrement à l'avenir si le besoin s'en fait sentir.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Some times an abscess forms in the flesh and stays for so long that it makes a large gathering of pus; and then swells up and bursts open, releasing its contents like a vase would do; while leaving behind an empty space as thin as fabric, not reaching bone or nerve; this kind of illness is called "sain", and not "fistule"; but if the hole reaches down to the bone itself, it becomes known as "fistule"; with such skin you must remove all that tissue around it, especially when delicate like a piece of cloth; it should be done quickly before corruption sets in.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you fear the skin will rot and corruption is not deep-rooted, but rather thick with flesh, then cure it thus: first check whether the breast is large, and the pus inside has a foul smell; in that case clean it out as follows using Egyptian medicine made this way: take equal parts resin, oil, and litharge; put them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and thick like honey; then take as much of it as you need, mix with water and honey, fill the breast with it through a small hole, and hold it there for two hours before emptying out its contents by squeezing gently; repeat this process several times till the breast is thoroughly cleaned and all pus has been drained off; alternatively use ash water if Egyptian medicine is unavailable: simply burn grapevine wood into ash, pour some water over them to form a mixture, then clean out with it as long as you are certain the breast is well cleansed; if patient cannot bear either treatment for any reason, resort instead to honey and water mixed together or slightly thickened with ground litharge - honey possesses both cleansing and purifying properties while wine helps dry out pus quickly; once you have done this several times over and the wound is clean enough in your estimation, it's time to apply an ointment that encourages flesh regeneration: for this take diafinit emplaster, mix it together with rose oil or even better, wine; or apply ointments whose properties I will describe in detail under Ointment section below. If the hole left by incision is too small and catheter cannot pass through easily then slightly enlarge its opening using a thin iron rod first before applying Egyptian ointment (or Basilicon). And if wound happens to be very wide open instead, simply stitch it up leaving just enough space for catheter insertion - if discharge comes out from above, remove any material blocking access below so that catheter can go deeper inside.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	For when the bowels are intact, no flesh is allowed to be entangled; and if you cannot cut under the sinew as you wish, arrange it in such a way that the bowel moves to the lowest point it can reach, for when the bowel is complete, no meat is caught in its folds and if you cannot cut under the sinew as you desire, make sure: that the bowel runs lightly downward; and leave none of the bowel behind. And take binding medicines to place on the wound, spread over a linen cloth which covers the whole wound then cut with force at the right side of the sinue A hole wider than the first, extend soft ointment onto another piece of fabric according to the amount of space in the hole and put it on the wound to ease the bowel do not remove the large outer cloth for many days afterwards; and that which is placed over the breastbone, often removes a bowel, and know what comes out of the bowel whether it be poison or little or much or digested or undigested. And note if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess present, when your medicine has spread in this manner and you see nature rising above the wound, then know that the breastbone has healed already; move the patient from bed to chair the next day, or on the third day, and once you undo the bandages around the wound, change into another piece of cloth and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast vomits undigested food after many days, know that the breast is not healing.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons take long to cure, do not despair of healing, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are people whose wounds heal slowly with charring, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested food vomits from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healing; and if the breast takes time to dry up, and it is distant, then apply drying medicines moist in substance and dry in virtue, such as a definitive ointment, for there is a large part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take definitive ointment, and make it with rose oil, and mix it with equal amounts of old wine; then cook it and use it; and the same can be made better when cooked thickened, if a definitive ointment is not available, or you can take myrrh and aloes and incense, grind them, and powder them over honey while it is on the fire; then glue a cloth to it, spread it over the breast, and sometimes they administer long aristologist roots, and celestial lily roots, which are like barley flour and centaury; and use either simple or composite remedies: grind them, make a powder, and put it on the honey I mentioned, and apply it; and if the cure is prolonged, and it is not healed by this treatment, then know that corruption has reached perfection, and made an impression on the bone, or hard parts, or the ligaments; so treat the fistula cure as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	Of the abscess under the nail.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that forms beneath the nail of the thumb, or the big toe, or it may occur in other places; and when it becomes old and untreated, it turns into a warm abscess, suppurating and spreading until it reaches the root of the nail, and even tears off the entire nail; causing corrosion down to the bone, resulting in foul-smelling pain, and the finger or toe becomes swollen, with discoloured flesh.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we said in the previous section, and the treatment doesn't work, then you must cut away all the redundant matter that remains beneath the nail, and then cauterise the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterizations are a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is sound; and if the nail presses into the flesh, beginning to prick and wound it, then you must place the point of a needle underneath the nail that pricks the flesh, push it upwards, and cut away this flesh subtly and lightly, and apply onto the remaining flesh burning and corrosive medicines to remove all; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	If the corrosion is in the bone, cut it away, and treat with fire, for as long as the corrupted bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see the finger corrupting, cut it off from us as it is said before, then treat until it is healed; and if it is wounded, and pierced, and there is great pain felt, you must first dress the wound; then trim the nail with a sharp spatula by cutting across from above, taking care not to reach the flesh underneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and should this happen, apply something soothing.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain of the wrist of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	Some people are born with very fleshy index fingers, sometimes there is one with a claw-like shape or it has bones and occasionally it comes out with a nail, some appear in the base of the knuckle while others come out near the root of the finger joints.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	The one that is born in the base of the knuckle rarely moves while the fleshy ones do move, cut off the claw-like with a sharp knife at its root
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that grow near the knuckles can be treated by trimming them, take care when doing so.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	With those that appear at the back of your hand, start by cutting the flesh all around it down to bone and then carefully remove the bone with an appropriate tool, clean well until the wound is dry.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come to the fingers together arise from birth, or from sudden wounding, or from burning with fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	You must cut this suture so that the edges may be brought together according to their natural forms; then place between them two tents or oily rose-colored cloths moistened, lest they should unite; you may also put in between two pieces of soft lead until the parts are united as they ought to be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If there is any swelling on the palm of his hand, cut this suture as it ought to be done.
des vils	swellings
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Swellings are large open wounds full of melancholy superfluities that occur in various body parts; and they more often happen in the legs of those who walk and work and carry burdens than elsewhere.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	You must therefore administer a purgative of bile to him at times, and then treat it with basil juice.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is done in two ways: one is when you cauterize it and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you open a vein, and drain all of its blood.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is done in this manner: first bathe the leg in very hot water until the flesh becomes softened, then remove the patient's leg from above the thigh down to below the knee; then make an incision at one place or another with a wide cutting instrument, then draw out and drain the black blood by hand from one end to the other, for as long as the patient can tolerate it; and then bind it up, and instruct him to abstain from eating food that produces black bile; and repeat both the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full, unless it is harmful to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: raise the patient's leg, even if it has a lot of hair, then place it in the bath, and pour warm water over the leg until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you have no bath, heat it by the fire, then cut along the vein from the knee to the ankle, or below the calf; next remove the skin with an onion, and peel back the vein on either side until it is exposed when pressed; and one will see it as red and black, and where it enters the skin like a white cord; then push the wire underneath until it is raised from the skin, and cut it lightly with an onion, then cut in another place three fingers above; next peel back the skin over the vein until it is exposed, then lift it up with the wire as before, and cut at another uncine, as you did first; then make a further incision or more if necessary, and lift it again, and cut near the toe joint, and draw and lift to the second incision; next extract from one incision to the other until all is removed, then cut away the rest; and if you cannot pull and lift it, push a needle with double thread underneath, tie and pull it through, and insert a wire beneath it, and turn your hand from side to side until it comes out; take care not to cut it because if you do you will not be able to draw it or lift it without harming the patient; and when all has been drawn, place wet wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the wound site; treat him until healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and enveloped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must split it crookedly but do not cut it; and draw it out as we have mentioned before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron with which we cut the vein is curved and does not slice, so that it does not cut the vein; and it has a thick curve because if it were slender, it would cut through the vein. But let it be thick as we have said, and here is the form:
de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is entangled in the legs, in warm parts where there are no plants or trees, and on land with little moisture; and perhaps it occurs elsewhere other than in the legs, like the rottenness that arises from beneath the skin, as worms and insects arise within the body, bred between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that a great inflammation comes into the leg, then the color changes, and the vein begins to protrude outwardly, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens, you must wrap it with a piece of lead that is three and a half to two inches long, tie it, and leave the lead hanging on the leg. Whenever it exudes again, rewrap it with the lead, and if it is too long, cut off a part and rewrap the remainder; but do not cut it at its root until it is completely exposed, for if you cut it, it retracts into the flesh, causing abscesses and putrefaction where it was, as well as severe illness. Therefore, it must be treated gradually from beginning to end without leaving any part inside the body. Sometimes this vein, when treated, measures five palms or ten in length, and a man came to me twenty years ago whose [vein] extended for ten palms; when you cut it, it produced one ray or channel, and pierce through until all of it comes out; empty the contents within it, and introduce antiseptic medicines against putrefaction there for several days, then treat it like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this wound is minor, especially when it appears in the ankle joint or foot area and there are many perforations from which pus flows, therefore one must heal it as we have explained before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Maggots that breed between flesh and skin.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "ox sickness" in our land because it often affects cattle and is caused by tiny worms that breed between flesh and skin, moving throughout the body up and down, causing a sensation as they move from one limb to another until they break through the skin where they began, then die; these are spawned by the decay of some bodily fluids, just as flies, serpents, worms, and roundworms come from the belly; its maliciousness is feared because when it moves throughout the body, if it reaches the head and gets into an eye, perhaps entering it, it can destroy the eye; this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and drained, one cannot be rid of it until it is ready: therefore, you must bind the area above and below with a strong tight bond, then cut above and drain it forcefully, and if the poison has gone deep into the flesh, and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire until it dies; and its greatest harm is that it runs to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming towards the head near the eye, firmly tighten the eyebrow above it, then cut above, and drain it forcefully; and the patient must use bodily cleansing medicines of soluble purgatives for harmful humours, and avoid foods that cause decay.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	Of the pain that comes from windiness.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called "vakirir" in our land and it's a pain that appears in some body parts, then moving from one body part to another and I've seen what I'm telling you about.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to see a sick woman, and she uncovered her arm, revealing a small swelling in the vein of the arm; then I saw it move up towards the shoulder like a worm, more than anything else, like quicksilver when it flows from one place to another; the pain departed from that spot and fixed itself at the shoulder, then ran all over the body so that it reached the other arm. Then she told me how it was now traveling around her body as I saw with my own eyes.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly surprised at how it moved from limb to limb because I had never seen this illness behave in such a way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Toutevoie, I had wished many that they would want to move the pain from one place to another, but I never wanted it myself, just as I saw it in the woman; and I thought it was because the woman had a dry body, and her veins were exposed, which is why this compelled air appeared; and it does not appear according to this reason for those who are delicate, and have moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see this disease being treated, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, then wrap around above and below until the compelled air is gone; cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your eyes, treat it with what removes the winds, such as fetid pills, serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	from arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and the parts of the body they hit.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of arrows lies in the fact that there are those with large points, small ones, and some that are feathered or welded; there are also arrows with two angles, those with long shafts, and those made up of pieces. When an arrow hits a body part, it can do so in two ways: it can penetrate a vital organ such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When an arrow strikes one of these vital organs, and you notice the signs of death that I will mention later, you must be cautious about extracting this arrow, as many patients die in such situations; but if these fatal signs are not evident, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then withdraw it and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when an arrow falls into it and pierces the bone, and breaks the membrane that is above the brain, is when you see a coma, stiffness, and swelling in the eyes, redness and inflammation of the tongue, spasms and mental confusion, and vomiting bile; perhaps blood flows from the nostrils or ears; maybe they lose speech and voice; and there also comes out of the wound white moisture resembling pus, as well as something like charred flesh. If you see these signs, then abstain from treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is still inside.
