Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of the arrow when it strikes the heart are that it is close to the left nipple, and one feels as if it were fixed in a hard object, not empty; perhaps the pulse changes like the beating of an arrow, and black blood flows out, coldness and cold sweat appear, and syncope: then know without doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow that has not pierced the lung is that the wound is full of foam, and the throat swells up, and the patient changes colour, breathing heavily and seeking cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow falls onto the chest covering, it is near the small ribs; and it causes great pain and great distress, and all the shoulder muscles move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow falls on the stomach, perhaps something undigested comes out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow falls on the belly, and no faeces come out through the lower intestine, there is no hope in treating it or extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and flows away, and the patient feels intense pain: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limb, like the cheek and neck and throat and shoulder and armpit and spine of the back and ribs and hips and thighs and legs, and similar limbs, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow fell on his collarbone in the root of the neck: I took hold of it, and drew it out from under the ear on the other side, and he was healed without incident.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And thrust into the eye socket beneath the paper beneath is an arrowhead which struck the fatty tissue of the eye and was lodged within it. The arrow had no barb, but its head measured as long as a Turkish bow, entirely made of iron, light without being thin; the wound healed and there were no ill effects.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	Thrust an arrow from the throat of a Christian and it was an Arabic arrow with barbs; I extracted the barbs and drew out the arrow gently until I removed it completely, then the Christian healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	Thrust an arrow into a man which struck him in the belly and I thought he would die; after thirty days had passed without any change to his condition I incised above the arrowhead and drew it out, but there were no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man with an arrow in his back or side, and the wound has healed over while the arrow remains inside him; yet he experiences no change to his natural functions nor finds hindrance in any of his natural activities.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man with an arrow in his face, and the wound has healed but he remains without suffering great pain or any other similar issues.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I drew an arrow from the king's man, which had lodged in his nose and was slightly tilted to the right; the arrow was completely bent, and I was called upon to treat him three days after it happened.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I sought it thoroughly with my finger, but did not feel anything; he felt pricking and pain beneath his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrowhead. I applied an attractive digestive poultice to that spot so the flesh would not swell; and there appeared the flesh of the arrowhead.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I left the poultice on for several days, and the wound healed initially, but the patient remained ill for a long time, feeling the arrowhead inside his nose every day; he told me so himself.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a strong corrosive medicine to the wound for many days until it opened up, and I probed with my finger, feeling the arrowhead's tip at the spot; then I inserted into the wound's opening some of that same corrosive medicine until the arrowhead's head became clearly visible; after several months the end finally emerged, and once the wound had expanded sufficiently I was able to insert pincers and pull it out from one side and the other, but could not remove it; so I kept on probing and contriving various instruments until eventually with a well-made pair of pincers, as described in this chapter's conclusion, I grasped hold of it and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	The mirror judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored: I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	You have been told the quality of extracting certain arrows, so that you may focus your care on what I do not mention, for books cannot cover everything; but wise masters compare well little to much, and for what is present and lacking, they find new work, and new instruments, in the discovery of strange occurrences within this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not exit the body from where they enter but according to two methods: either by their point of entry or by another part; and one which exits by its entry point is an arrow entering fleshy tissue, and this may occur sometimes now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not come out now, let it stay until the flesh is completely rotten around it, and the exit is widened; likewise, if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it there for a few days, moving it every day; then it will come out, and if it does not, pierce all around with a very fine drill, so that the surrounding tissue is enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the brain's ventricles, and any of the accidents that I have mentioned appear in the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it until it becomes even after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the pia mater, it will cause death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is not stuck solely in the bone, and does not come out through the skin, and the patient remains a few days without any bad incident, devise its extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is deeply embedded and cannot come out on its own, apply cups around the wound as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is buried inside the body and cannot be seen, search for it throughout the wound; and if you can feel it, extract it with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot due to the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves or veins involved, open up the wound until it is large enough. Extract the arrow if you can, and if it has barbs that keep it in place, remove the flesh that is attached on two sides as far as possible without damaging any muscles; then break or bend the barbs of the arrow so you may extract it; do this carefully to avoid breaking the arrow which would make extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do it all at once, leave it until the surrounding flesh is rotten, then pull it out, for the extraction will be eased.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the loss of blood opposes you, then manage this as we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and be wary of incising the nerve and the vein, and use whatever means you can to extract the arrow without danger, either quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to how they were positioned when the arrow struck them, for it is the greatest aid there is, and if you cannot, then do as the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	If the arrow has come from elsewhere or if there is nothing apparent of it, or if the skin is swollen in that area where you can see or feel it plainly: cut above until the tongs can grasp it, and then pull it out: do this now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, turn your hand roundly until it enters the bone, and enlarge the bone, then draw it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot come out, leave it there again, and then restart the extraction until it comes out completely; if it was an arrow stuck in the bone, push along the whole shaft; if it is blunt, and you want to administer a thrusting motion, use an instrument with a pointed end so that the tip of the arrow enters the hole of the instrument; then push forcefully, and if the arrow is embedded, insert the instrument with its point entering first in order to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	If the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom has entered, if you can, then treat the wound as appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow falls on the foot or thigh or belly or bladder or flank, and it is near the surface, and you can cut above it, then cut; be careful not to cut a vein or nerve, then extract [the arrow], and close the wound if necessary; treat until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used to extract arrows is similar to a bird's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many types of forceps: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the wedge is like a bird's feather, to push against the tip of the arrow, as shown here:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the tongs for pushing and extracting is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins in the body that can be used for bloodletting, sixteen of which are in the head: two jugulars behind the ears known as "herbech," two arteries visible at the temples, two veins at the corners of each eye called "aspires," one vein across the forehead, a vein at the top of the nose, two subclavians in the neck, two veins above the mouth known as "augeherich," and two veins beneath the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	There are five veins commonly used for bloodletting in each arm: the cephalic vein is on the left side and lay people call it the "vein of the head;" the median vein is called the "fast" by the common folk and consists of the cephalic and basilic veins; the basilic vein is found on the right side, which the commoners name the "belly vein," and appears on the forearm.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: 
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of veins that are located behind the ears is beneficial for chronic colds and headaches; and the qualities of the bleeding, as I tell you, are that you raise the patient's head, and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tighten the patient's neck with a cord so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two places dependent on the head: look for them with your finger, and where you feel the pulse beneath your finger, there let the blood flow out; then take the lancet, and insert it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand across the entire length of the vein, and cut both the skin and the vein thoroughly with two fingers' width, making the blood come out as much as you wish; then release and bind (it) until it is healed; and I have already mentioned incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples is beneficial for chronic migraine, severe headache, and habitual ophthalmia, as well as for the body of acute tears from the eyes; and the qualities of bleeding are as I say: it is necessary for the patient to stretch their neck so that the two veins open clearly; then you feel the pulse beneath your thumb, and proceed to bleed afterwards; next lift the heart above the vein with your index finger, insert the lancet underneath, raise up the vein, and strip it just as you did in the other two veins, and let out blood according to your need; then release the patient, put your finger on the vein for an hour, then apply cotton; after that bind it firmly and leave it until healed; we have already spoken of their stripping and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein in the forehead is as valuable as the bleeding of the cephalic vein for ancient facial diseases, and for migraines, and redness; and its quality is such that the patient strains their neck by twisting, so much that the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called 'fosseur', whose form is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	Place the tip of the instrument over the vein and press it with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow out according to the amount you desire; then untie the patient's neck and bind the wound until it is healed, but never use a wide flame for this.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, the flame should not be too sharp; and do not bleed across the bone, for it is close by, and may break the instrument if it is delicate.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The draining of the two veins that are in the armpits helps with eye ailments, scurvy, redness, swelling in the eye, and facial diseases; and its quality is such that the patient must keep their neck immobile using a cloth tied around it, as mentioned before; then drain the vein, making the incision slightly oblique to the length of the arm, a little long, and broad, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the veins are delicate, they might break; then let the blood flow until you need it to stop, and then bind it with cotton, tying it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vein in the nose is drained for fevers, sudden madness, and facial diseases like migraine and redness on the face, especially when it's an old ailment; and its quality is such that the patient must keep their neck immobile, then pinch their nose with your left hand, take a delicate, long vein, and insert it between the lips in the space between the two nostrils, as the vein does not open very well there, and the blood will begin to flow now; do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it for one night, as it heals quickly; this is the form of the incision:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two veins helps with narrowing the shoulder joint, starting a broken bone, many diseases, gout, corrosion, herpes, and tumors; the qualities of this bleeding are that the patient tightens their neck underneath either one as we have said before; and the masters should be standing above the head of the patient, while the patient is sitting on a chair, then open the vein for an inch or so widely, then draw out blood temperately until it's necessary to do so; then start again in another vein, then unbind the ligature, and close all veins moderately, so that the patient doesn't suffocate; and let them be until morning, when the wound has healed.
de la sainie des leivres	The bleeding of the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The draining of veins above the lips aids in healing sores within the mouth, and treats gum inflammation, cracked lips, and surrounding areas.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	Make the patient sit before you and hold their neck as I have described; then turn up their lip, and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left side, and they can be recognized by their black color and small dark vessels surrounding them: thus cut each of these, if you do not know which to choose or are in doubt, cut the larger one on either side; proceed similarly with the two veins above and below, as it is all done in the same way.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Draining below the tongue.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of veins below the tongue is beneficial after the bleeding of the cephalic vein, and it is done at the narrowing of the throat, for diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the bleed should be such that the patient sits between your hands facing the sun, with their tongue raised, and look beneath each side for a black vein: bleed one or both, but do not go too deep, as beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly bled are bled in two ways: either by incising with a wide flame-heated iron or an olivewood stylet as sharp blades, and it is called 'anesil'; they are broad and thin according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of Martin's flame is very renowned, and it is broad as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the swollen veins full of thick blood, and those that contain thick and troubled blood; this is Martin's flame form:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and sharp, and this is for bleeding thin veins or where there is thin yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	Bleeding from the basilica, which is one of these veins, aids illnesses located below the throat, and under the neck, and at the chest, and in the belly; and the bleeder must take care to avoid the artery that lies beneath it.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and blood flows out, it must be stanched as I have said; and the flame should not be held still but moved like a knife.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not open clearly, you must extract it and change to another one; or take a part of it, or treat in its place the vein within the arm: it opens clearly; and cauterize with flame as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the place of the incision, it is necessary that you first extend the arm so you can feel for the pulse; then mark the spot and bind the arm firmly, cauterize the vein with a flame, and take care not to cut into the artery when you see swelling, for this is the artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it spurt upwards like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is from an artery: be quick then, and apply pressure with your finger for a long time; remove your finger if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm tightly, leave it thus, do not let the patient move his arm; have fear and doubt, but make sure he does not move until healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped and it overpowers you, cut the artery if it is exposed, for this will hinder the blood flow; staunch the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of fustic bark, split it, and take one half, binding it tightly until the next day; if the bleeding has stopped, that is well; but if not, treat as we have said with hemostatic powders; and be aware that staunching blood may be less effective in certain circumstances due to the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm's muscles.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	Bleeding from the median vein helps by drawing blood away from the head above and the body below, as it is composed of both the basilica and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the one bleeding must take care to avoid the nerve beneath, and if they cut too deep and find the nerve, and it swells and their incision becomes serious, and perhaps cannot heal; this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some people due to its subtlety, then you must incise it with a fine instrument; remove the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	Et if has a vein between the two nerves, then open it lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding of the cephalic vein is beneficial as it draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and one must bleed with a prick near the olive-shaped flame or the myrtle-shaped flame, for this is the safest of all veins as there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, one must seek the lighter spot and cause no harm if they miss the first time, and start again; perhaps for some men, the veins swell when pricked the first time, but it causes no great harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of bleeding depends on your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not done except to maintain health and prevent future illnesses; and let the bleeding be performed in one of the three veins which are as follows: namely, cephalic, basilic, and median cubital; and it must be done at the beginning of spring, in autumn, and in winter after eating when signs of fullness appear; and you should bleed on the first or third day, two to three hours after the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bleeding for illnesses has no determined time, but rather when the need arises during the day or night, at any hour and in all seasons; and one should not bleed children until they are fourteen years old, nor a pregnant woman from the fourth month until the seventh.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	They must not bleed old men who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wants to bleed themselves, in any manner, it is necessary that they cleanse their intestines with a light clyster if they have too much retained feces, so that the veins do not draw out from the intestines harmful superfluities damaging to vital organs; and one must not bleed those who are overly full of meat, or drunk, until such time as he is sober again, nor those suffering from dropsy; and take care not to bleed someone following a fit of colic, vomiting, diarrhoea, sexual intercourse with women, or hard labour involving watching or fasting, or any other thing causing great weakness in the body's strength (whether caused by weapons, or some other bodily accident); then purify the humours if the blood is thick through meats and drinks and medicines as you have power to do; then enter into a bath if nothing prevents this, to thin out the blood, and bleed yourself from the vein of the arm around two-thirds up (as we've said) ; and be aware that day of work, or pain, or lust, and all other like things; and rest and cheerfulness must attend you, and let the bleeder be higher than him who is bled, then rub his arm twice or three times, and tighten the ligature moderately, for if it's too tight or little, blood will not flow; and then rub around the place with your hands until the veins swell up, and can be felt; then moisten the bleeder's palm with a little old oil, next put his left hand to that vein below where he is to bleed himself some little distance so as not to let the vein fall or fail in wounding.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow like cords to the blood-letting cup, and among them are those filled with windiness, so that when one applies flame, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein; thus it is for these [veins]; if one opens the vein, the wound becomes too narrow, therefore medical practitioners must take heed of such things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens on the first attempt, it is good; but if not, one should begin again a little below that place or above, unless the location is swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	If the location is swollen and the patient panics, leave it for one or two days, do not bind the arm: perhaps hot abscesses will form; do not immerse in a bath, then begin blood-letting again if you wish; and if the opening is small, the blood may flow quickly and you doubt that enough blood has come out as intended, apply all the flame directly to this same opening; perform the procedure slightly above rather than below so that the vein is not swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not reopen the wound, and apply a poultice of oil, as it eases the body from blood, and the oil is beneficial in this location for the poultice; and thus administer the poultice of oil in every dressing that you dress wounds to staunch the flow of blood; also triacle and bowels of them, when applied on the place, very subtly the blood diminishes and parts itself as it becomes too great.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess occurs there often, especially when it is not dressed except for that time or the opening of the wound is small, then hasten and apply to the place a sponge moistened with warm water and salt, and bind it tightly for an hour; and you must do this after the flow of blood from the wound has ceased, and if there remains on the place after some days any blackness or greenness, it will not harm them; and if you see it, apply something made of aloe or myrrh infused in galbanum juice, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and appearance in the wound of the basilica: so place your hand on it, and if you find the spot soft under pressure from the hand, then this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid applying anything we have mentioned here, for perhaps the artery is nearby; instead apply a dry poultice to harden the spot, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Treat each of the blood types according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red; and if you see it as thick, let it flow until it becomes thin; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for someone who is full and healthy but needs bloodletting to have a wider wound created; the flames should be broad as well. For those who are weak, do the opposite: let them bleed less often, but frequently; they must be bled by cutting across the vein, not pricking it. This method of bleeding is safer from excess loss of blood and damage to nerves, and it is better than a long or wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for someone who requires bloodletting due to bodily ailments, it is appropriate to give them bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if they are warm-blooded, draw three or four times the amount of blood. If their complexion is cold, let them eat moistened bread in muscatel syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, along with a well-scented syrup beforehand.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints during the operation, after the loss of a great deal of blood, it is necessary that he sniff broth from meat, and subtle perfumed syrup, and use other things we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wishes to open his arm and bleed it again, when he is weakened by great bloodletting, it is necessary that he bleed little by little, according to the quantity of his continuous strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if someone wishes to open his arm after the first bleeding, and he has strong constitution, he should bleed seven hours after the first bleeding or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if someone wishes to bleed from another part of the body, he should be bled on the second day or third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For it has an excess of blood within the body that is already heated up and causes fever; thus we must draw out a large quantity and widen the wound until it heals slightly; then you should fulfil all conditions for healing, and place your hand on their pulse as they heal so death does not come in this spot of partial healing, and this happens many times when surgeons are neglectful; and one should never press strongly down if wanting to release an arm from a tourniquet for the second time after blood has been drawn out once before and the wound is closed; nor should you extend their arm forcibly if it is curved, as that would be bad; but rather leave them until they heal again for a second time; or make a small cut at the tip of the flame, so that any congealed blood escapes from this opening in the vein, and apply some wool soaked in water to this area, and press down lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the wound is swollen, leave it alone and do not constrict it until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it becomes necessary to draw blood a second time, then do so from the same place, or from another vein, or from the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein between the arms is used for bleeding instead of the one on the head because it is composed [in a different way].
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	The method of bleeding is as follows: the patient immerses their hand in warm water until the nails turn red; then they are tied loosely so that the vein can be seen clearly, and it is bled across its width rather than length; the incision should be wide, and the bloodletting must occur close to where the fingers join the hand; if the bleeding stops, return the hand to warm water and allow the blood to flow into the water until you have drawn enough out; and for those who are ill with fevers [and need bleeding], do not immerse their hands in warm water again since it is more commonly done during winter than summer; bleeding from this vein is safer than any other, as there are neither arteries nor nerves present.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The bloodletting from the little finger of the right hand is beneficial for all liver ailments and here is how to do it: remove the hand, and immerse in warm water until the vein swells up so you can see it; if the bleeding occurs transversely, and you cut through completely, there will be no harm done; don't go too deep though as the nerves are all bare underneath, without flesh covering them. And then return the hand to warm water, if blood has congealed in the wound and cannot flow out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And once you have drawn out the required amount of blood, apply oil and salt to the vein to weld it together, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	Bloodletting from the little finger of the left hand is beneficial for ailments of the spleen, and do everything just as I told you regarding the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The draining of the spleen is effective for all ailments that are below the body, such as diseases of the uterus, retention of urine, kidney disease, and similar illnesses in the thighs and lower legs.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its drainage is such that the patient immerses their foot in hot water and rubs it over the vein until it ruptures, then bind it above the ankle joint; this vein is located at the ankle, and many run up along the leg towards the kidneys; drain whichever kidney is wider, or at the ankle where it moves better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you drain it at the foot, be careful not to injure the nerves that lie underneath, and treat it as you would a wound by cutting into it; let the flame of the cautery be gentle.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot escape, return the foot to water, and let it drain thoroughly from the vein.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the incisions fail on the first attempt, begin a second time slightly above, for the skin is salty; do not doubt the nerve, as we have said, and proceed in this way with the other foot likewise.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The skin of the sciatic vein is near the ankle bone, and its incision aids in relieving hip pain when the blood is hot.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	The quality of this incision is such that the patient should enter the bath, and press above the ankle for four days by twisting, as otherwise the vein will not open; if it does open, then cauterize in all ways you can, crossing at various points; take care that you do not cut too deep, because the skin here is salty, and this area is quite sensitive to many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you cannot find it, press any vein that appears on the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and be careful not to hit the nerves; make sure blood flows from where you wish, then untie the bandage, apply cotton and hold [it]; she is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	Cupping sessions.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cups are made of horn, brass or glass; cupping is done in two ways: either by drawing blood and creating a bruise, or without bruising.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this non-bruising cupping is also performed in two ways: either using hot cups or cold ones; the bruising and bloodletting method of cupping is done on fourteen body parts: primarily the head; then the neck; twice on both sides of the neck; under the chin; twice over the shoulders; over the hips; twice over both arms; twice over both legs; twice over both ankles; this type of cupping draws only small amounts of blood from many tiny veins scattered throughout the body, and therefore doesn't weaken it as much as vein-opening does; neither hot nor cold cups should be administered to any illness caused by an excess in the body until it has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if it is necessary due to illness or for treatment purposes that cupping must be done, we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, or towards the end, and throughout; because there are some who, when they need cupping, suffer from a heavy head; and there are others who experience fullness and redness in their face, neck, and head, as well as darkness around the eyes; and there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, have an inflamed tongue, and vomit blood; and some feel dizzy, seeing blood, wounds, death, and similar things during sleep.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially when it is the middle of the month, we instruct them to undergo cupping after three hours during the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with the inflammation of the head ... that reaches the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of all body fluids; this venesection takes the place of the bleeding from the temporal artery, and it is not suitable for those who have a cold constitution or who suffer from catarrh, as it does them great harm; and therefore it is not appropriate for the elderly to use it, nor for those who have cold diseases in their head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often bleed in this way become forgetful, and so it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little further down due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The venesection in the middle of the neck takes the place of bleeding from the head and from the temple, and because of this it is useful for narrowing of the chest, splitting of the lung canal, cough, and fullness; and it should not be pushed too hard, for if it holds too tightly, it causes oblivion or stomach and heart problems.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The windings of the two ribs of the neck are useful for pains in the head, and ophthalmia, migraine, strangulation, pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is located where the basilic vein passes; and you must instruct the surgeon to apply pressure with their hand to occlude the artery, without compressing it too much so that blood does not escape.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The windings under the chin are useful for mouth diseases, and gum inflammation, as well as similar ailments that occur in the mouth; and it is located where the two labial veins pass.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders are useful for illnesses that arise from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings of the axillae are just as effective as those of the three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the surgeon not to apply them too vigorously, because the area is devoid of flesh, and there are nerves and arteries underneath.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup that is placed on the buttocks is effective for hemorrhoids and ailments below, and it must be large and made of bronze to have a strong pull; perhaps if it were more delicate, it would break, and it causes big wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The suction cups on the legs are beneficial as they draw blood from all over the body and help with chronic pain in the kidneys, bladder, and uterus; they can be placed on two knees and two ankles, but prolonged use weakens the body and causes dizziness in many cases.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the suction cup is by first placing it empty and then sucking gently, putting pressure on it, and moving evenly without stopping until you see redness and swelling in the area and the appearance of blood; stop and remove the cups, being careful with different body types since some have thick skin while others are more delicate: one should strike only once, creating wide and somewhat deep wounds, and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to loosen the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out little by little, we are content with just one blow.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to draw a lot of blood, we begin again often; and if the blood is thick, strike hard thoroughly, and in such a way that the heart is pierced suddenly, and it is necessary for those who have thick and hard skin, and whose pores are narrow, that you anoint the cups of the ventouse with apertif and dissolutive oil: if it is in summer, violet oil, or almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if it is in winter, cress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the surplus is large and cold, take oil of amaranth, or balsamite oil, or oil of anise, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the one being healed has tender flesh and large pores, it is not advisable to use oil, but rather wash it after ventilation with rose water, or cold water, or morelle water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those with excess moisture, they should rise with myrtle water, or sumac water, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those with large surplus should rise with old wine, or garlic water, or anise decoction, or chamomile, or others similar; and they must not be bled with cupping before the bath nor during the bath, but after the bath by one or two hours; and they must not sleep after the ventilation, it is necessary that they wash when they need to be cupped and when they are being cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware if the person being treated is choleric, and if their blood is too acrid and inflamed; they should take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce with ease, and similar things; and eat little pork, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And for those with a cold constitution, they should take syrup of honey and moderately fragrant wine, which is between old and new, and eat little pork, and moist meats, as well as small birds and pigeons; on the day they are cupped, they must drink more than they eat; and sometimes it is necessary to give some men treacle or nutmeg before or after cupping, to strengthen their principal members; and let the blood be subtle, but those who are hot should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cups that are applied without wounding are those placed over the liver, and on the breast, podagra, and on the belly, buttocks, kidneys, and hip, because these members cannot endure wounding at all; rather they cause blood to be drawn from member to member, just as we place them on the breasts when there is a nursing child. To remove the viscosity that has accumulated in a member, we put cups on the belly or buttocks to reduce the size of the member; and it removes pain where there are stones or concretions - perhaps by its attractive power it draws out the concretion, or shifts the stone from its position; and thus it acts when placed on the liver if there is windiness retained therein, and these cups are administered empty for only sucking up; sometimes they are administered together with fire, and at other times filled with warm water - as in diseases of the pleurisy. And in this manner we fill a cup with hot water alone, or some water in which appropriate herbs have been cooked
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The method of applying the fire cautery is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And let it be two inches wide and half a palm in length, with a small hole on its side near the middle, just large enough to insert a needle, and made of brass, soft enough so as not to injure the patient when applied to the limb; and in the center there should be a transverse bar of brass or iron, upon which to place a lighted candle, and these should vary in size, some being larger and others smaller according to the disease and the age of those who use them; for the cups for children are different from those used on old persons, and those employed on lean people differ from those applied to fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	One should thus place this cup upon the limb in the following manner: Take a wax candle or the lint previously mentioned, and insert it across the bar which is within the cup so that the flame shall be at the bottom of the latter without burning the patient; then apply the cup to the limb, with your two fingers over the hole we have spoken of, so that when you wish to allow the vapour to escape, you may raise the cup and take it away; and take the lint as before, and repeat this operation frequently if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping procedure applied to pleurisy, being entirely aqueous, it has no handle nor any aperture, and is only used when full of water, placed solely on the affected limb; its shape is thus:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	They are not used except for members where cupping cannot be applied due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas; also on denuded flesh like the tongue or nails, and others of a like nature; and in regard to their quality, whenever you find leeches that have been kept in clear fresh water without any rotting, take them; keep them one night in sweet water until they are familiar with it, and have nothing inside their bodies; then bleed from both vein and cup, rub the member red, and apply the leeches; when they are full and drop off, if this is a place where cupping can be done, do so as it follows later.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If this doesn't work, lift the wound easily, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the wound heals too much after the flesh closes, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and apply it until the blood is stanched; and if the blood is multiplied, apply ground vitriol or gallstones, and similar things, until it is staunched; or you can put half of a peeled pea on the wound, leaving them there until they dry on the wound, this will now staunch [the bleeding]; if more is needed, take other compresses.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the compresses are not available for use, rub the wound with fresh blood, or stick a needle in it until blood flows out, and then apply them, as soon as they feel the blood, they will dry; when you see that they fall off, sprinkle some powdered aloe and ground salt, or ash, now they will staunch [the bleeding].
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it deals with setting fractures and resetting dislocations.
