Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish surgeon who neglects this chapter will never see any of the ancient books, nor read a letter from them; and for this reason science is lost in our land, for I have never found any good [surgeons]; and I know nothing but through the science of these ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have mastered their knowledge, and through experience, and through the practice of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained herein, and I have abridged it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I did in these two previous chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is necessary then that we say in the prologue of this book the main points and chapters where the sage puts his understanding, and dwells on the truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	When fracture or dislocation or torsion or breakage occurs to anyone, you must hasten to bleed the patient on both sides if nothing hinders you, such as bodily weakness, childhood, or old age; or if the weather is not very hot, or too cold; and avoid eating cold foods, that is, cold dishes, goat meat, and beef, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not overeat flesh-based foods which fill the veins with blood until you have no doubt about a warm abscess, or the spreading of matter in the limb; then may the patient return to his first diet that he used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that the patient be nourished with meats that produce rich nourishment, or something viscous, such as boiled wheat in water, and rice, and testicles, and feet, and calf's stomach, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with too rich nourishment, the healing is impeded and the fracture heals more slowly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bone of the elderly and decrepit cannot heal or fuse well according to their nature due to the dryness of their limbs; nor can those who are too young, such as small children; but you must take care and apply thick splints above the broken bone which bind and join the limb together, ensuring it is as strong as before; do not cease this work, and for that reason, they should be nourished with rich meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from that of the spine or leg, and I shall tell you in this chapter all the types of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	As there is fracture that heals by callus formation, and another through sharpening, like the cut of a quill to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is fracture with a wound, or fracture with only a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And for each type of fracture there is its own method and proper instrument for restoration, according to how the memory returns to its place; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the line is twisted, and it appears clearly on the outside, and it sounds hollow when pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or sounding upon touch, and the patient feels little pain, then there is no fracture; but there may be a twist, crack, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You shouldn't move it with your hand, but apply medicine as follows, then hold the joint firmly yet delicately.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that a bone fracture where the two parts are separated requires immediate realignment to avoid abscesses developing at the wound site; if hot abscesses do develop then it should be left for one day until the abscess subsides; then reset as gently as possible without causing further injury, knowing this type of break is easier to treat than those with pieces missing; and hold it as described below.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if the bone is broken into pieces you must extend it with two splints, be it an arm or leg, use one splint for a small limb or finger and hold it in place with string, set the limb according to its natural shape so that when the broken ends of the bone are brought together they should be realigned as closely as possible without causing further injury, ensuring no harm comes to the patient; align the two ends of the bone in their best form.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And you will feel it with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well; so handle it gently, and do not hold or press too much as they often cause hot abscesses and contractions in the limb due to their actions, just as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is in place, admonish the patient well not to move it, neither while awake nor sleeping, nor when turning over, or in any other way; and ensure that the limb is so secure that they feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when they feel no pain, it is not yet in place, and you must put it into such a position that they feel no pain; and be careful that it is set straight, so that no crookedness comes about once restored; and the qualities of the broken limb are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme. 
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For the small members, such as arms and fingers and similar: one must wrap soft and fine linen bandages; and for those that are large, like thighs and legs: one must wrap with a wide and hard bandage, because wide bandages embrace the entire large member, and constrict it evenly from all sides, so there is no strain. Then bind light pads around [the limb], three or four turns according to the size of the member, and tighten your hand slightly on the whole bandage, then move above the fracture and tighten less, so that the fracture can move away a little; and loosen the bandage a bit at a time, until you take up most of the healthy part, then add another bandage, and turn it back around onto the broken place. Then return to the lower part of the break, and constrict moderately - not too hard or too soft - as we have said above in the first binding; then put linen or cloth pads between the bandages, so that they are all even, then bind everything with a strip on top, and then put your splints well-made on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or abscess, apply a soothing poultice to the abscess, hot and draining, for a few days; then strain out some oil from your stars [astrolabe?], and let it be half of a length of cane resin, or from wood that makes clogs, or palm fibers, and make them into this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but the star [astrolabe?] that is placed on the fracture should be slightly thicker and wider than the others; it should also be as long as required for the limb, small or large; then tighten them onto the stars like you did with the first binding, then bind a thread over them appropriately, just like in the first binding of the fracture; make sure that it is tighter on top and looser at the bottom; the thread should be medium-sized, neither too thick nor too thin, and made of soft flax; for if the thread is too thick, as I have seen with the work of fools who bind their wounds with twisted linen threads, this is a great error, because the binding cannot be even if it is too fine, and there should not be less than one finger-width between each star.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is injured by the bones of the vertebrae after a compression injury to their spine, place pads made from linen or wool below them so they do not become bruised.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by a broken heart, I will describe its treatment afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And remember, it is not advisable to manipulate the vertebrae right away when all limbs are broken.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is large, one should not insert any vertebrae for at least five or seven days, or more depending on how severe your abscess appears; and here is the method of ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and sprains: you take some flour that sticks to the walls of the mill, mix it with plenty of egg, apply this preparation, neither too runny nor too thick, as needed for various types of fracture, especially in women and children, because it is neither too hot nor cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another type of plaster to treat broken bones, dislocations, and twists: Take three ounces of beech mast, ladanum, nettle, asafetida, and gum arabic; mugwort, also three ounces; nine ounces of alchiloe; make them into a powder, and mix with egg white. If the patient's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it has good composition, restores broken bones quickly, and works well on many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another type of plaster useful for twists: Take mugwort and marshmallow root, each three ounces; myrrh and aloe, nine ounces; six ounces of acacia; ten ounces of Armenian bole, grind well, and mix with water or egg white until it forms a paste, then apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another plaster application method for dislocated joints and broken bones out of place, to ease the pain that arises, and reduce swelling or bone fractures: take new linen, soak it in warm water and oil, and apply it onto the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore [the joint or bone], but it is good to ease hot abscesses, and properly remove pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another plaster application method that resets broken bones: take dry fig leaves and earth-pavement leaves [possibly 'ivy' or 'ground ivy'], grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another plaster application method for resetting broken bones and reducing remaining abscesses [or swelling].
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of marsh mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, one part each; grind and mix with wine, if the limb is hot treat it with moist coriander water or plain water mixed together, apply as needed.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another plaster method stronger than the first, when a severe abscess develops during limb restoration.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of marsh mallow, flax seed, pomegranate, honey plant, sanicle, violet and chamomile flowers, one part each; grind and mix with salty water or fresh water or wine according to the warmth of the limb and its state.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates writes in his book not to put anything on the broken limb for restoration except wax and oil, nothing else at all, and says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen [a famous physician] suggests placing drying substances which are slightly warm on the broken member, to repair it, like myrrh, aloe and frankincense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another type of plaster useful for injury and pain: take mugwort and chopped human hair or bird feathers, and viscum, and an equal amount of flax [or: and combine them equally], grind these into a powder, make it into a poultice, and bind it in place.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you loosen it a little after that [time], and pay attention if the patient feels no pain or hasn't moved the bone from its place - don't remove by hand for two days. And if pain appears in that place, or itching or restlessness or swelling occurs, then hurry to take off the bandage and plaster; and get a light cloth and moist sponge of sea [or: fresh] water, dip it in liquid, and lift up this area until the irritation stops, and the pain is eased. Then let them rest for one hour, and put on dry woollen fabric, soaked in water or rose oil, bind onto this overnight so that you are sure about warm abscess; and calm down inflammation of the limb, remove their pain, then start a gentle bandaging again, with some plaster and do not tie it too tightly as before. Do gently until they heal.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess has become cold and red, causing pain and swelling despite its removal, then you must apply an ointment and bandage, so restart it as you did initially equally.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If none of the methods we have mentioned work on the limb, do not release it until after three or four or five or seven days; sometimes leave it for twenty days as needed, so that the fracture heals and the flesh aligns properly. Then restrain it more firmly than before to thicken its meat, as I said earlier. If you see the place becoming too dry, know that nourishment cannot reach there; therefore wash it with warm water each time you release it, every three days, and loosen the bandage a little. By this method, then, nourish the limb, and correct what foolish doctors do when they restore the limb crookedly: this is bad and dangerous work, and I see no other option but to leave it alone and treat it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various types of fracture
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures and diverse forms, and their causes are distinct; for there are fractures caused by the blow of a sword, and the point removes all the bone up to the marrow beneath the bone, just as an axe or stick does; and thus this type of fracture is called 'axe-fracture'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword chops the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called 'chop-fracture'; and the wound from these two types of fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded blow, or splintering, or from the point of a stone, or from falling onto stones, or similar.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture, which reaches up to the membrane beneath the bone, or it is on top of the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that pierces the bone as subtly as hair, and it has a small crack, therefore this fracture is called "capillary"; and if the wound is caused by striking with a stone or falling from a height or similar things, and the fragment of the bone enters inwardly, causing the scalp to be pushed outward like what happens when coppersmiths strike upon copper kettles; then the stone goes within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this occurs more often in those who have moist and soft bones like children's heads, so all these types of fractures involve small fragments being detached as stars, I will discuss them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures through their dislocation, and the inquiry at touch, and by the corrupted flesh that is upon them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of the hair is known for this: when the bone is exposed, and one rubs upon it, the black fracture opens up.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating the fracture, take care of the patient's accidents and if you see no ill accident, such as vomiting bile, loss of understanding, extension [?], faintness, acute fever, eyes issuing forth fire and reddening, and other similar things in different conditions, it cannot heal without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you see no terrifying accident but hope for recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound first comes to you, and it is in winter, you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day so that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, lest the membrane beneath the bone become corrupted, and the accidents we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the bone fracture extends to the membrane covering the brain, you must split the affected part in this way: take the wounded person's head and uncover the bone thoroughly, especially over the wound area as much as you can. If there is any bleeding when uncovering the bone or abscess formation, treat it accordingly; fill the space with soft cloths moistened in rose oil until the hot abscess subsides and no more bleeding occurs. Then begin to work around the bone, employing two methods of treatment: one method involves cutting a narrow opening in front, shaped like this
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then he makes another cut even greater than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second method is to have several different cutters, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed and made of soft iron; operate with care so as not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and strong, you must bore around it rather than using cutters with trepans, which are not perfect as they do not penetrate beyond the skull bone, and they should have a margin or circle on the tip to prevent it from passing through the bone; several of these are needed so that each fits its place according to the type of bone, thus providing trepans for all parts of the skull; this is how three types of trepans are formed:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities to pierce around the broken bone are that you place I tarere (a drilling tool) on the bone, and turn it with your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then move the tarere elsewhere a little later, and do this all around, then cut with the incisors the space of the bone between the holes, and do this more delicately than you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you draw out the bone by hand or any instrument like tongs, pincers; be careful not to touch the brain or the marrow.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and extracted the bone, it is necessary that you use an implement to scrape off whatever remains of the bone with any other instrument similar to an incisor, but it must be sharper and more delicate than the other incisors; if there are still small bones or scales remaining, remove them lightly with one of the instruments; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is more safe; and he praised it strongly, and these are his words.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone, where the fracture is visible, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place under the head of this lens-shaped cutter, which is formed like this:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side only, as the cutting edge has two sides, so that the blades are facing towards the bone; then strike gently with a small mallet above it, so that you lightly chip away at the bone all around, and be mindful of the membrane that lies beneath; if it is stuck to the bone, remove it gently, for it can be removed without harm or fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	Et if the bone fracture does not pierce through to the marrow, and the bone is merely cut above it, and there are small pieces, then one must remove this roughness, and scrape off the scales with a delicate rasp that you ought to have in various sizes, to apply to each place the most suitable tool, according to the work and shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Use large rasps first before smaller, more delicate ones, and do not stop until it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	For each of the other delicate fractures and hairline cracks, one must apply an appropriate remedy according to its direction; this is something that cannot be answered by someone who has merely studied this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the ulcer is uncovered, then one must take a piece of linen cloth, according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, placing it upon the wound; next, take another cloth folded in two or three layers, moistening it in wine and rose oil, and place this on top of the first cloth; do this as gently as possible so as not to harm the ulcer, then apply another bandage without tying too tightly, only enough to keep the wound covered; leave it like this for one or two days until the hot abscess is healed, then remove it and apply healing medicines such as lily roots, wheat flour, incense powder, aristologist's remedies, and similar things; make a powder from these things, placing it on the wound, and apply non-biting medicine afterwards; watch that the wound remains clean, never leaving ointment nor allowing pus to gather, for when pus gathers above the brain tissue, it corrupts and endangers the patient; when biting medicines are applied, they corrupt further.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take heed therefore, if any adverse incident occurs to the patient, as we have said, it is undoubtedly doubtful.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if redness does not appear due to the medicine applied, which has such properties, you must take a portion of honey and three parts rose oil, mix them together with one piece of cloth, and place it on the affected area; then treat it according to the manner of treatments necessary until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes both parts of the collarbone are broken or just one of them, as there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break but only becomes swollen or twisted, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you must insert your little finger into the collarbone's hole and place this broken part within it so that your index finger holds an equal amount to your middle finger outside; until the collarbone returns to its natural shape; do this gently, taking care not to cause pain during treatment.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nose and it cannot be returned to its place, you should set it equal to the head of a slightly thicker pin.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, remake it similarly, and hasten to restore the first on that day if you can; otherwise after the seventh or tenth day, when the hot abscess has cooled, then cover the head of the nose with strips of linen cloth, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you put the other one on another side if there is a break there; and let the strips be so thick that they fill the openings of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one should wet the strips with butter, changing them each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It seems not good to me, but they should be moistened with a concoction of egg white and mill powder; then leave the tent until the bone is set and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Sometimes goose feathers are used instead of tents, and if so wrap soft cloth around them, and have the patient blow through it to hold the break in place; do as you wish.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess appears at the nose while you are working, apply a mix of red oil and wax, or place some moist cotton in rosewater, or use dew of aquilon.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If an abscess does not appear, apply plaster externally made of bran flour and incense powder mixed with egg white, then place light tow over it, but do not tie the nose; and if the bone is broken in small pieces, extract them with suitable instruments for this, then cut open the wound and treat it with appropriate things like charring and cauterizing, or plasters and ointments as needed; and if there is no wound inside the nose, treat it with tents and place splints of lead until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	For the fracture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured from below, and there is no external wound, and the break is only outside, not inside, it can be discerned easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, you should insert your index finger into the patient's mouth; if the fracture is on the left jawbone, use the index finger of your right hand and gently push the broken part inside, then align it with the other hand from outside, making sure it is even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is divided into two parts, you must apply traction to both sides until they are aligned.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movement of the teeth occurs or fracture happens, bind them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, then apply a broken jaw cerate on top and cover it with double linen cloth; put over that cloth a large well-made starched pad or an equal piece of leather, long and wide according to the mandible; secure it as firmly as you can, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, loosen it on the third day and then reset what has changed; apply an ointment of mill powder with sufficient egg or sesame flour after removing the cerate; cover the ointment with a light woolen cloth, and if the plaster hardens and the patient's condition does not change, let it be until healed; often this heals in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess comes about, bring about what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture with an accompanying wound, remove no part of the bone; do so delicately with instruments suited to this task.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, clean the wound, if it is wide, apply suitable dressings to promote flesh growth until it heals.
de la forcele	Of forceful things.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	Forceful impacts break many times in front, toward the shoulder, and this fracture occurs in three ways: either it is broken and split into two, with pieces, and is the easiest to reset; or there is a fracture with an accompanying wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is such when there is a fracture without an open wound, you should have two assistants: one to hold the shoulder that feels the broken force; and the other extends the neck towards the affected part; then align the fracture with your hands so that its form is as it should be, and leave neither protrusion nor unevenness.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend it further, place under the patient's shoulder a round sphere of cloth or wool, according to your needs; and stretch and lift the broken force with one hand while holding the sphere tightly in another so that you align the fracture as needed.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the broken bone out, because it is embedded too deep, then the patient must often lie on their back and place a medium-sized pillow under the shoulder; have assistants push the shoulder down until the bones of the fracture are lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then turn your attention to the broken bone with both hands, and if you find it splintered, you must cut above it; and pull apart the pieces gently, and if the bone cannot be joined by any manipulation, insert one of the incision knives underneath it; but place this instrument below the fracture to protect the wound:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	be like a spoon, and is not sharp-edged, and be as broad as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength required; and have two handles, as you see, one being wide, and the other narrow, like the route of the wound which was made when you pulled apart the bones; and when you are assured that there is a hot abscess, sew up the wound, and if the rupture is small, or you doubt a hot abscess, fill the wound with lint and dressings according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if a hot abscess comes about, soak a cloth in rose oil, olive oil, and wine, then apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	Bind the bone when it is fractured and uncut, by applying an emollient of mill dust and egg white to the bone, then place light tampons over it, and use a pole if needed beneath the armpit; next take a very wide bandage one palm in width, then put on doubled cloth over the tampons, and the emollient; then take a thin splint three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around the bandage so that its head hangs down; place the splint on the fracture, and wrap the bandage around the neck, under both armpits, and tighten from each side, until you see the splint hold the fracture well, and confirm clearly that the splint is not moving over the broken bone, then rewrap it daily, and retighten when loosened; have the patient lie on their back, and put a small pillow under the armpit to elevate the shoulder during sleep, which lightens the fracture by aligning the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck, without untying unless an ill accident comes about, for twenty days; then reapply the emollient if needed, and tighten it, leaving it so until restored; in most cases this takes twenty-eight days, but some recover sooner.
de la brisure de l’espaule	For the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Before it occurs that the shoulder breaks in or out of place, and is not put back by force through touch; arrange it according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it following its natural form, in every way you can; then apply flour powder with an abundance of egg, light tampons, and place a double cloth on top; then add a broad thin canvas slightly wider than the shoulder, and if there are incisions at any point of the shoulder, fill those openings with linen tampon swabs so that the canvas lies evenly; and finally secure it all firmly with a large bandage, ensuring the canvas does not move from its place, and check the binding each day; every time it loosens, tighten again, and level out the canvas if it has moved away from its position, and have the patient lie on their side; in twenty or twenty-five days, the shoulder will be restored. Once this duration is complete, you may release the bandages, but remain vigilant because the bones are not yet fully set.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a bone fragment juts out before the chest and pierces below the heart, open it up above, remove it, and do as we have said for treating an abscess after breaking the humerus.
de la brisure dou pis	Of the rib fracture
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The rib is sometimes broken in two, but this occurs rarely; however, it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in two, it moves downwards and the patient feels great pain, suffers from shortness of breath, coughs, and may even vomit blood; the ends of the bone can be seen protruding through the skin, which is very evident.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	The method of restoration is as follows: let the patient lie frequently on their back and place a cushion between their shoulder blades, then press on the shoulders and use your hands to bring together the sides of the two broken ribs; adjust carefully so that the bone regains its proper shape; then apply plasters and lay over them fine cloth soaked in salt or other light substance, wrap it all in a linen cloth, tied securely to the broken bone so that there is no movement; make the bandage go around the back, binding tightly but not too tight, and relieve the pressure every hour; if the plaster becomes loose, bind more firmly; if you need to remove it due to decay or itching at the site, pain or abscess, then do so quickly, and remove the plasters, clean what is there with proper treatment methods; then reapply the plaster, binding tightly until healing occurs.
de la brisure des costes	Of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that rib fractures only occur in the upper back and near the head, due to their fragile nature; this can be confirmed through examination of the patient's ribs.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The treatment involves resetting the fracture so that it is aligned correctly, as required.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply a plaster cast and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	If the rib fracture is towards the inside of the body, the patient will experience severe pain and pricking sensations, as well as coughing up blood due to the bone piercing the lung; they will also suffer shortness of breath, constant pain, and significant loss of blood, requiring immediate treatment and often extensive medical intervention for older patients.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And some say it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, to push the hernia out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, unless hot abscesses have already come about.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have, then heal them.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some of you say that we should apply cupping glasses to the site, to extract strongly, and this seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the cup will not draw the excess to the site due to weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some of you say that we should cover the site with moist wool in hot oil, and place tents between the ribs to level the skin around it, then be cured by treatment for pleurisy, diet, and medication.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear due to the bone pressing on the flesh, and there is doubt about the condition, it is necessary to make an incision over the site of the broken rib, and one must place an instrument underneath to protect the internal organs; then one should cut into the bone, and extract it gently, and afterwards sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat it with ointments until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hot abscess appears, place on it moistened rags soaked in rose oil, and put it over the site; treat the area with what is necessary for an abscess, and let it lie frequently on its side where it should, until it heals.
de la brisure dou col	From the broken neck.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is breakage of bones at the neck, and sometimes it bends; also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, observe: if their hands are softened, swollen, and numb; they cannot move them or extend them; and when you prick them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in many cases, and if they feel better when you move them and press upon them, know that the bone's joint is saved, and the patient will recover with proper treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if they will recover or not: observe if their feet are softened, and there is an accident involving their hands; and on their back, watch for windiness and involuntary defecation; and when they are laid down onto their stomach, look for involuntary defecation.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is reminded of it on his back and he wishes to mount, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that they are mortal; so do not labor excessively in their treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these accidents do not befall him, then the matter is more slight.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is such that you reward him if there is hot abscess, so apply on it red poppy or oil of quicken egg, until it subsides; then place upon it one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is severed, you must cut above the heart; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a suture, then treat it with ointment promoting flesh growth until it heals; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "head of the cow", put your fist from your left hand into it, and align it to your other hand, then apply plaster and splint on top, should you need them; then hold it tight, and if there are any severed bones, do this, and remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the broken hip bone.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Before the hip bone is broken, and if it is, there will only be a little thinning at the head; and it bends downward, and declines towards the back, and the patient experiences pain in that place, and tenderness, and swelling of what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over it, so that you are above the broken part; and understand which is the break and its shape; and if the break is only at the head, then make this break even, so that it is in natural alignment.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is in the lengthwise direction, or where it declines inwardly, then make the patient lie on their stomach, so that you can see the restoration of this break.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have aligned it evenly, apply the plaster, then place a wooden or heartwood splint on top, and secure the fracture, so that it does not move; use padding under the armpit to ensure evenness.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess forms there, do not touch it until the hot abscess has cooled down, then apply what we have previously mentioned; afterwards return to the restoration process and secure it appropriately, provided that no complications arise; this is the procedure.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	On the fracture of the shoulder.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires is what lies between the cut and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of two methods: the first involves taking a piece of wood of medium thickness, in this shape:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And bind the two ends of the wood to the two bones, and hang them up, and place the patient on a seat; then cast their broken arm onto the piece of wood so that it reaches the axilla, and put in a curved piece of wood underneath, then suspend some heavy object or weight which your assistants should pull down upon; then have the physicians align the fracture evenly with both hands together until the break is restored as it ought to be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The other method is to have the patient lie down on their back, and bind their hand to their neck, then instruct two assistants to hold either end of what has been broken in their hands, and for each assistant to pull at their respective ends.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more powerful, tighten the cord below the fracture and above it too, stretching each of the assistants to their respective sides.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder joint, then you should place a cord halfway below the acromial edge and the other towards the scapula, beneath the fracture; similarly, if the fracture is towards the scapula, it must be gently tied with little effort such that both ends are level on the scapula and on the side; then align the break equally as required, tightening it so abscesses do not form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if abscesses form, do not tighten it for seven days, placing moist wool smeared in rose oil on it until the abscess is relieved; then you may proceed to tie it up, and the way of doing so is as follows: place a plaster on the fracture, then reunite the arm with the support device, and put your hand over their shoulder or chest; wrap a cloth around it, tightening both onto the support and the arm such that the arm is immobilized at the armpit, unless something else prevents this, or if the bone has moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have two inches of space between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it extends three inches beyond the break on either side; then stretch upon the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter concerning the fracture, more firmly and less distantly.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the placement of the splints and the binding, as we have said, when you restore the broken limb, and you doubt that the abscess is hot, leave it bound until the seventh day, as we have mentioned; then examine every three days to ensure no itching or swelling occurs in this place, nor any numbness comes upon the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the address, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if none of these accidents occur, do not loosen it before three days or more, and let the patient sleep on their back with their hands on their stomach; place a wool-filled cushion evenly under the shoulder joint, and check every hour during the day or night that the broken limb does not move nor the bandage become loose; if it heals by the virtue of medicine, feed them the diet we have previously mentioned, in such a way that the food is first delicate; and when they start to recover, let their food be more substantial.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary that the shoulder bandage and leg should be removed after forty days in total; then you must loosen them, give a bath, and apply ointments as medicine to correct their position.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the dislocation is bad and stuck, it takes one day or two months to heal.
de la brisure du bras	From a broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "humerus", where one is small, and it follows the wrist; and the other is large, and it is below, towards the little finger; perhaps only the large humerus breaks, or the small one, and maybe both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small humerus is broken, restoration is easy, as are cures; when the large one is broken, treatment is bad, and more severe than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only a small bone that is broken, you should stretch it gently and set it evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone that is broken, you should pull it more forcefully and stretch it on a cushion, holding the wrist of the hand higher than the other one, with the small fingers lower than the others, and have the patient cross their legs over themselves, with the cushion in front of them at an elevated height so they do not suffer any strain; then have your assistants extend their arms to the part below the patient's hand or ligament, while another assistant holds the other arm above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then place the mirror flatly in line with its original form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each piece back in its place and grasp the one that is torn from the heart but cannot be restored to its proper position firmly; then cut off what you have done before as we mentioned earlier.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breaking of skin and wound, I have spoken about it in the singular chapter, then take its care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of restoration sore abscesses arise, then glue with soft cloth made of rose oil and white wax, that is neither too hard nor too soft; bind the cloth subtly above, so that the hot abscess may be eased.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.
