Then remove the wax, and apply the plaster made with mill powder and an abundance of egg, then place the splints, and let the splint for the broken bone be closest and slightly wider than the others; know that there must be six splints or arms in various arrangements: whether the fracture is in one bone, or two; bind tighter over the fracture rather than elsewhere, and always less so as you move away, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter; let the cloths which are upon the fracture be soft and moist, not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And bind the member and the joint after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident befalls the member, such as an itch that arises in the member, you must bathe the member with warm water until the itching is soothed; and let the member rest freely without restriction.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then resume the binding, and if the ligature is softened and the bone dislodged, or a similar thing happens, address it accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you take note that nourishment cannot reach the member because it is too constricted, you must soften it a little, and leave it thus for a few days until nourishment flows to it, then bind it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to pass for the patient, do not release them until 20 days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Around this place, then paint their hands to his neck, and let their necks be even, and beware of movement and disturbance, and sleep on their back; know that this fracture is healed in 30 days or 35, perhaps in 20 days, depending on the compounds and the constitutions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	On the fracture of the hand.
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that on the back of the hand and the knuckles there are few fractures, but rather dislocations occur many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is fractured or dislocated, it is necessary that the patient should sit cross-legged, and sit upright directly in front of them evenly; then place their hand on a stretched cloth, and have the ministers straighten the broken bones, and make them equal to the model, so they are well aligned; apply the plaster and bandages, unless an abscess appears, then put in a peg according to the size of the place; it should be wrapped in one linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is around the front of the shinbone, make a pad of linen cloth and instruct the patient to bind it tightly to their broken leg; then take a long strip of linen, and let the heart-shaped splint be as large as the palm of the hand, and tie it just so.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is on the outside, you must place a splint above and another below the leg so that the hand is open and straight, then bind everything around the hand with a bandage, securing it between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture occurs in any of our fingers, except for the thumb, make it even as required and bind it with the leg; if you see fit to place a small straight splint to elevate the break without moving it, do so; if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or one of the others, make them equal and tie it with the healthy finger next to it; or you can tie all the fingers together into an "I" shape, whichever works best, or place a splint above like for the thumb; take care during restoration and in dealing with hot abscesses, provide treatment as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and one can easily see this when it turns forward or backward; the restoration involves binding a ligature above and another below the break.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on their face, then each assistant extends their ligature to an equal part; this is when the break occurs in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, let one ligature be towards the armpit, and the other ligatures below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	Also, if it is near the knee, let the ligatures be around the knee, and their extension be downwards; then have the assistants hold the bone equal with their two hands, so that it aligns with its natural shape, and then apply a plaster cast and bind it, unless an abscess appears.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let it subside before returning to your work and treatment; the dressing is made in such a manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You must wrap the fracture with a hard bandage doubled over twice or three times, leaving excess, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the thigh, and pass the thread between the thigh and leg, below the knee, and bring the end of the thread above; then go back up the leg and thigh with the bandage, then place splints over the fracture, and put a splint on top of the bone in the leg; then fill the empty space between the leg and thigh with soft cloth to equalize pressure, then start tying firmly three or four turns over the fracture; as you go up above the fracture, lessen the tension; take hold of both ends of the thread that you passed between the leg and thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread until you reach near the foot; tighten it so that there is no movement from its place, then leave it like this for abscesses, swellings or other similar conditions to go away.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, you must undo it and address the issue at hand, as we have said many times before; if there are bone fragments caught in the joint, they should be removed if possible; if not, then one must split open the area and pull out those fragments; treat the wound as we have explained until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken and fixed with rods like in the shoulder or arm, however, despite this restoration being done correctly, the patient still suffers pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And note that the thigh is restored in 20 days or slightly less or more depending on the patient's constitution.
de la ruelle dou genoil	From the tendon of the knee.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that there is little breakage in the kneecap region, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is but a crack or a hole, and this occurs in all wounds, both felt and unseen, and one feels well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	The restoration is such that one places what is equal to its two sides until it is assembled as close as possible; then apply the plaster, and add a round stick if needed, and hold it tight as required, then follow all the procedures we have mentioned for other fractures, like hot abscesses and similar conditions; assign each accident what it needs, until it heals.
de la brisure de la jambe	On the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one rightfully called "mustelz," and the other is named "foscile"; they both have similar fractures as seen in the arm, hence the restoration process is equal to that of the arm, and all procedures are the same. If the two bones are broken together, the leg will turn or twist from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the subtle bone is broken, it twists forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it is well seen; it twists downward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, apply traction and make it equal, bind the bone ends equally; however, if the fracture is bad and there are multiple fragments, let the traction be lesser and lighter; adjust according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, and le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, and ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, and proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From the breaking of bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no breaking, but in the bones of the foot comes breaking and two bumps, with only fractures occurring in multiple places.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is breaking in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones rising above one another, let the patient place their foot on the ground, as though they want to walk, then put your foot on theirs, where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their places; then apply a plaster cast and wrap it up, and place under the belly of the foot a small board with two feet long, then strap it to the foot properly, once you have wrapped it with bandages, and other things as needed.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, untie the bandage, for you will find the bones equalized, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are any of the fingers broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place in the broken finger a peg according to its length and slightly wider, then put underneath the foot that board I mentioned and strain it appropriately; if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place on each finger a peg according to its measure, wrapped in a piece of linen cloth, and tighten the board beneath the foot; let this be attached above the head of the board outside the bottom side so that it holds firmly.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things I have said about other fractures, as we have mentioned before; attend to each accident as is fitting.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	Of the fracture of the wrist bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman's nature is fractured, make her sit with an enlarged opening, then incline her to her back part and hold her from behind; then fill the fracture with cotton, using as much as it holds; stand the woman up, lift her back little by little, and when the cotton comes out at the entrance of the nature, the bone will return with the stool; when she wishes to urinate, remove the cotton, and once she has urinated, replace it; do this for seven days or so: the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a goat's bladder, tie a cane to its opening, then push the entire bladder into the nature; blow through the cane forcefully until the bladder is inflated inside; the nature will heal the fracture; fill it with cotton again, and leave it for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the wrist of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from one who applies his study and practice to them, and reads my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break indicates in many positions the correct way of restoration: understand this, then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose's windpipe and insert the penis into it; then wrap it with fine cloth, and leave it there for three days, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	De fracture cum ulcere.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	One who has a fracture with an open wound, especially if it is large, like the bones of the thigh or shoulder, should be quickly treated, so that the treatments we have described will testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, apply a vitriol compress, if you have nothing else; then start to treat the fracture again that same hour or day, before hot abscesses form.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	If hot abscesses do form, leave the treatment until the ninth day, until the abscess is appeased; do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause harm to occur.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on an uncovered heart, you must gently put it back into place with your hands using slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if extension with your hands is not possible to align the bone, then realign it with this instrument of iron which has seven or eight fingers in length and its width depends on the size of the wound; and for this, the surgeon needs to grip it with three or four [fingers], depending on what is needed in each treatment of a fracture; and let it be round and slightly thick so that it does not bend when compressed against the limb during your work, and let it be sharp at the tip, and thick towards the middle, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", for this reason the curved head must be placed on top of the visible bone; push it once until it returns and becomes even with the other one.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle, and the instrument cannot properly grasp the bone, then you must cut off the head of the bone until the instrument has a hold on it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then cut it off with an appropriate instrument, either a saw or a knife, according to your ability; remove what remains in the bone of roughness and small shreds.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	Si make sure it is in its place, then moisten a cloth with black styptic wine, and properly so if it is injured; and do not put any cerote or other oily substance on the wound, as it would cause festering and corruption; then apply stars once you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut away the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and be careful that the wound is not constricted with the fracture; and many times these foolish doctors have done this, and caused the patient or death or corrosion at times; and be the constriction softer and gentler than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that bad accidents might occur as we have said, and you find pain in the area, then it is not suitable to apply stars; but wrap around, instead of stars, hard cloths, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that the wound has started to heal, remove what you have placed on it entirely, and apply healing ointment such as tetrafarmacoun and similar remedies.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary that you stretch the limb twice daily, in the morning and at night, until it is mended and healed.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is fitting that the limb be immobilized in such a way that the bowels flow easily downwards.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if it remains open for many days, and does not heal but repeatedly dislocates again, know that there are small bone fragments present, which is why you must carefully explore the wound with a probe, and remove all these troublesome pieces causing this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula forms or any other kind of corruption occurs in its place, you must treat it according to what he said in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, such as the thighbone or the humerus, and other similar large bones, do not extract it, for often death occurs, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall off by itself after twenty or thirty days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, just leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Scabs that form over the healing process.
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often see the recovery from a fracture, especially when it is close to a joint, and the deformed appearance of the limb is an unpleasant sight; and perhaps the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care therefore if the wound is fresh: administer styptic medicines such as aloe, incense, and myrrh, as well as gum Arabic, galbanum, and similar others; mix any of these substances with either wine, egg whites, or honey; wrap them in gauze compresses; keep it tight and don't change it for several days. Then remove the poultice and apply another one until the swelling has reduced, or use a piece of well-made lead instead since this material also reduces swellings on the body. If the accumulation is already hardened like stone, you should scrape away at its surface to expose the excess; or have someone shave it with a razor so that it can be removed and cured properly until it heals completely.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Of the limb which is weak after recovery
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed, and afterward the limb remains weak and delicate, it happens for many reasons: one being that it was bound too tightly, and not as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, preventing nourishment from reaching the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or through large movements made at the wrong time; or because there is little blood in their body, thus making them weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat and soften their body so blood multiplies within them; administer a bath to them, give joy and leisure; then place pitch on the limb, so that the pitch attracts great nourishment, and often rinse with warm water until nourishment flows into the limb; returning it to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	Of the twisted limb after healthiness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the broken bone is clearly visible, and the form of the limb is ugly, yet it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish ones who say that the limb should be rebroken entirely, and many a fool has done this in our land; these procedures are criticized and cause great harm and, perhaps, death; however, if the knots and swelling are fresh, they should be soaked in warm water or with cooked softening herbs such as mullein leaves, roots, and fenugreek, and similar things; and make a softening poultice, like well-made diachylon, and take the mucilage of mullein, mix it with chicken fat or sesame oil and apply as a poultice; or take fatty figs, grind them with bran flour, and similar medicines that reduce inflammation.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the adhesion is removed by continuous and lengthy rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	Let gentle movement be given to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is hardened like stone and must be removed with an iron tool, it should be cut down to the bone using a subtle light incision; then apply stitches and focus on healing.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in someone, it should be promptly reset without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the flesh swells, and it may be put back in with difficulty; therefore, it must not be moved when swollen: many times this causes spasms and other pains; nevertheless, when this happens, have the patient bled, then leave them alone until all the abscesses are healed; afterwards bathe the limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as its cure presents itself.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from head to toe.
des mandibules	of jaws.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jaws become dislocated on both sides, and their dislocations occur in two ways: either they are slightly out of place and softened; or they become completely dislocated, hanging downwards, and saliva falls from the mouth which it cannot hold, nor can it close its mouth, and it wraps around its tongue when speaking.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return through various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete and finished, you must reduce it promptly without delay; in such a way that the assistant holds the patient's head, and insert your fingers from one of your hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; while the other hand provides counter-pressure to balance; instruct the patient to relax their jaws and move them around.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And you should adjust it evenly until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if reducing it is difficult, especially when both jaws are dislocated together, bathe them in hot water and oil until they can be gently reduced; do not delay the reduction as we have said before.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are realigned evenly, and the patient's wound is well-closed without softening it, apply moist compresses made of rose oil and wax onto the affected area, then lightly bind it with soft bandages; have the patient lie on their back while keeping their shoulders apart using two cushions, ensuring that neither side nor front movement occurs, and don't let them strain to chew; instead feed them a light diet until pain subsides, jaw motion is restricted. Then they may slowly eat what they want, but never force themselves to open wide for eating or drinking until the mandible heals completely.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two jaws cannot be reset to their proper position within an hour and do not return to their place, feverish chills will occur along with persistent diarrhea, and vomiting clear mucus may also happen.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, know that it is destruction; and many times the one who experiences it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	Of the fork.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The collarbone cannot dislocate from the inside along its length or from below, and it rarely dislocates outwardly, which is easily felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient often lies on their back and extends their arms; then press the place firmly with your palm, and it will return; then apply a plaster and bandage, and hold it tight; and the head which is towards the neck cannot dislocate; if not, and if it dislocates at all, reset it to its place as we have said; then put on the plaster and bandage, and hold it tight, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; likewise, the shoulder head is reset when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You know that the shoulder is dislocated in three ways: first, it dislocates at the part of the socket underneath; secondly, it dislocates at the part of the back; and perhaps it dislocates above, which happens rarely; it does not dislocate behind because of the shoulder, nor does it dislocate inside because of the nerves; often it dislocates beneath towards the socket, especially in those with little flesh, for it easily dislocates in them; in those with enough flesh, it dislocates with difficulty and enters with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men that there is an injury or fracture, and the shoulder swells from a hot abscess, and they believe it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	You must therefore test it until you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is known that the dislocation occurs when it moves downward toward the armpit, and creates a difference between the affected shoulder and the healthy one, with an obvious disparity between them; you will find at the head of the shoulder a depression, and underneath the armpit touching the head of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose or move in any way; also, if it is dislocated upward, it is not hidden, for you will clearly feel it upon touch; this kind of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is recent, or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the minister lifts the patient's hand upwards, then places your palms underneath the shoulder blade, and lifts the joint forcefully upward to its place; the minister lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then puts it underneath; thus it will come to pass quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not happen as we have said with bare hands afterward, then the patient must be bathed in warm water; and the administrator gently applies a softening and soothing ointment, such as a decoction of altee, fenugreek, and mellilot in water, and let it be administered; then remember to place the patient on their back, and put underneath the shoulder blade a cushion of wool that is even, neither too soft nor too hard, then place the afflicted's heel onto the cushion, and lift the head of the shoulder virtuously, and pull the patient's hand; and another administrator holds the patient's head so it does not move downward; this shoulder returns all at once now, and if you wish to reset it in this manner: and ensure that there is present a man who is larger than the patient; and be standing upright next to their side, then push their shoulder underneath the afflicted's shoulder blade, and lift the blade upwards so the patient hangs in mid-air; another administrator pulls the patient's hand downward towards their belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, attach something heavy to them, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	One also resets it in another way: insert a long peg into the ground so that the shoulder joint is just as wide as the barrel and neither too thick nor too slender; then place [the patient] underneath with soft cloths above them and have the patient stretch out along the length of the pole; then extend their arm to the other side forcefully, and the joint will pop back into its socket immediately. If it won't go back in after all these things we've said, proceed as follows: take a pole two arms long and four fingers wide with a rounded head for insertion through perfectly aligned holes underneath the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then place a soft cloth on top of the head of the board to protect the patient from injury, then remove the patient's weight from under the shoulder; and stretch his arm out along the long side of the board, and bind the limb to the board, and secure the arm at the head of the bed, then put the other arm across a stool on one side with its hand hanging down, and let the body dangle off the edge on the opposite side: the joint will come back into place now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	Once it is in place, no matter the manner, you must put beneath the shoulder a pad of even woolen cloth, then apply an ointment prepared with flour powder, frankincense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around it; then bandage beneath the shoulder appropriately, re-tightening the tourniquet above the ointment, embracing the hand to his neck, and let the hands stay in that position.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eat little for a while so the limb is strengthened, for then it will heal sooner; and then let him eat more after five or seven days, and move [the limb]; and if it stays firm and is not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has gone out of place due to moisture or another reason, you must apply cauterization at three openings, as described before in the chapter on cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint is not held in place, and cannot lift their arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is either cut, stretched or weakened; and know that the joint will never be put back into its proper position.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that affects the hip and breasts or the area behind them is caused by a push or pull of the hands and can be treated in another place; treat it until it heals.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing process, there is cracking in the limb and delayed movement, the patient should frequently take baths until this cracking eases and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	On the dislocation of the neck...
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the neck joint is repeatedly dislocated and returns to its place; if it is completely dislocated from all sides, especially front and back, then the dislocation must be corrected because it can easily be seen and felt; this will vary according to each person's anatomy.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick man's wound with healthy flesh, you can clearly see it.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is swollen, and he cannot bend his arm nor reach his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it before any abscesses form, for if an abscess forms, it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is at the back; thus this dislocation is worse than others, causing greater pain, and death may occur.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is done when it can be reset; you extend his arm with both your hands; his arms are spread out, and the hands of the mirror according to the cut around, above and below, and push the joint towards its shoulders or at the root of his palm until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it happens when he bends his hand towards his hand, and press at the root of the palm to fix the dislocated joint.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	If it does not want to return to its place, perform a strong extension; with two people assisting, extend the arm and bend it so that it cannot move during the extension; then rotate the arm in all directions while wrapped tightly in a long and wide cloth; when you have manipulated the joint back into alignment, apply some oil to soften the joint, then press the joint firmly until it returns; once in place, apply a dry poultice with egg white on top, secure it tightly, and attach the arm to the patient's neck using a bandage, leaving it for several days before removing it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in place, untie the bandage and leave it alone; but if you see that the joint is not properly immobilized, replace the poultice and bandage, leaving it there for a few days until it is securely set, then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels soreness after the joint is reset and it swells up again, bathe and massage it gently, pressing until it is soothed; or apply to the joint a poultice of fatty sheep's wool, leaving this on for a day and a night before removing it, then place him in a bath, and when he perspires, rub his joints with moderation. After which reapply the poultice, repeat the process two or three times until healed; if you see fit, apply moist cow dung heated with butter to draw out any remaining inflammation; this will restore its proper condition.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joints of the hand dislocate easily and return lightly more than other joints However, it must be reset immediately when dislocated, unless the area is swollen or a hot abscess develops.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the method of resetting is that you place the affected hand on a table and the assistants stretch out the hand, aligning it so its palm appears above the joint Then push until it returns However, ensure it is correctly aligned; then have the patient lay their back of the hand flat on the table for extension and reset.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient lay their back of the hand flat on the table and place your hand over the affected joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it comes back now, that's good If not, apply a strain of soothing emollients for hot abscesses, and leave it like this without starting over.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, the joint remains deformed; and it causes no harm to the patient as long as the hand is weakened, and unable to grip anything at all: then know that the nerves are severed, or the artery; there is no other mechanism left except cauterization near the wound, and perhaps nothing else will help.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, apply the emollient we mentioned, then strain it and leave it for five days, then undo the strain and leave it like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any tear, then bathe it with warm water, and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	On the dislocations of the fingers of the hand:
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or on the palm itself; then stretch the finger and push the dislocation with your fingers until it returns to its place, then hold the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is disjointed; leave it like that for two days, and then make it equal that day; at night bind it as we have said, and during the day untie it, move it, and rebind it at night; do this often until it becomes narrow, and also do likewise if it is dislocated on the palm of the hand, act just as you did before until it is healed; and do all the same when it is dislocated elsewhere.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, or there are multiple dislocations, there is no treatment, as death comes quickly to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that urine escapes uncontrollably, and they cannot hold it back, and often parts of the body become weak, such as both thighs or arms, or one side may twist into four parts; this twisting at the rear is called 'gilbositez': the treatment is to turn if the 'gilbositez' came from childhood: there is no cure or total recovery.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from a fall or blow or similar events, the ancient methods of treatment say there is little benefit in all this talk; but I have shortened it according to my understanding, and designed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the hunchback condition which comes to the base of the neck, neither a physician nor any expert knows its cure; and likewise for the one that directly affects both sides, but it is possible to heal only those that manifest on the back as I said; and so the patient should be stretched out face down onto an equal surface, with something beneath them so they do not injure themselves; then stick a spit at their head firmly in the ground, and another at their feet, and tie one bandage above the shoulders of the sick person, and another across the hips, knees, and ankles; and two servants should hold the bandages taut, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two spits; and these must be secured properly, both the spit as I said earlier, and the patient's spine with hands placed firmly onto it until it is straightened.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this cure, take a plank three arms long and place it under the wall, let the patient be on their side, push the head of the plank underneath the wall, then put the middle of the plank on the spine; have the examiners place their feet on the other end of the plank, press well until it returns to its place; if you wish, do it with a wrench that turns in the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	Stick two stakes one arm's length apart at the patient's head and another two toward their feet with about a palm span between each stake; have a hole in each stake through which the wrench passes, secure the stakes firmly in the ground so they do not move; between each pair of stakes place a turning stake over which pass the ropes whose ends are attached to a smaller stake one palm long for winding the rope onto it; then tie one end of the rope that passes around the armpits to the wrench near the patient's head, and attach the other end to another wrench at the feet, have each assistant wind their respective rope onto its corresponding turning stake while the master makes sure the spine remains aligned as previously described.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, apply a drying poultice with an abundance of egg, then pack with lint, and insert a rod made from three fingers' length of wood to support the place of curvature and the healthy part of the spine, then bind with a bandage as we have said, and the patient should use subtle nourishment until he is healed; but if anything comes up towards the end of healing, then one must administer softening and soothing medicines along with the rod that we mentioned earlier; sometimes one administers instead a piece of lead, and occasionally the protruding part shows itself behind the last vertebra in the spine, which people think to be dislocation; but it is just bone showing through, so there should not be any presumption: perhaps it could cause death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Of hip dislocations.
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	The joints of the hip and shoulder only cause dislocations, unlike other joints, and there are four types of dislocations of the hip joint: inside and outside, front and back, mostly deep inside, and sometimes in the front or rear.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the recognition of an internal dislocation is as follows: when you bring together the afflicted leg with the healthy one, it appears longer, and the knee of the patient seems larger than that of a healthy person; furthermore, they cannot bend their knee fully to the front; there is also swelling on the affected side from heat caused by an abscess because the head of the thigh bone has come out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes to dislodge is that these accidents are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of him who encounters it in advance are that he stretches his leg according to the accomplishment; nevertheless, the knee does not bend without pain, and if one tries to make him walk, he cannot go forward, and retains urine, and the vein swells up, and when he defecates, he steps on his heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of him who encounters it behind are that he cannot spread his knee, or bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the vein is softened, and the head of the thigh bone is in place under the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The resetting of this similar dislocation is that you must support it if the dislocation is old and remains according to its position, for there is no treatment; and one should not have any assumption about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for someone with a fresh dislocation, which has four types, you should act quickly and return the joint to its place, stretching it both inwardly and outwardly, and moving it right and left; perhaps it will go back into position, and no further treatment is required.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	If it does not return with this method, then you must prepare one strong assistant, and have them grasp the leg firmly with both hands, or use a strap tied above the knee; another assistant should put their hand underneath his armpit, then pull him tight with a soft strap around the thigh; while another holds the head of the strap; all assistants should extend upwards and downwards at once, raising the patient from the ground in one motion, leaving them suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to four similarities, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, you must treat it accordingly. When the dislocation is on the outside, you should have the patient lie on their healthy side, then place the bandage on the root of the thigh, and the part below the groin, then stretch the bandage upwards towards the groin and towards the hip; then have another minister take their arms, embrace the thick part of the diseased thigh, and extend it outward forcefully: it will return to its place now; and this type of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot secure it in the manner we have described, you must bind the patient's two feet together with a strong soft bandage over their two heels and knees, with the diseased leg extended twice as much as the other; then hang them from a post so that they are two arms' lengths above the ground; command one minister to embrace the head of the thigh, and have another minister hanging with the patient, embracing the thigh tightly, for the joint will return quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are external, the patient lies down as we have said in the case of one with curvature, and bind tightly above the affected leg, also on the foot; then place two red-hot irons, one on the head and another on the feet, then insert an iron rod between the patient's thighs into the dislocated joint; and let moist cloths be placed around it so that it does not burn the patient, then have each attendant stand at his side, and a mirror is held even with his hand near the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place him on the operating table, and press as we have said for curvature, and let the patient lie on his sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when dislocation is in front, it is necessary to stretch the affected leg slowly, as I have said; and have the patient put their weight on the healthy side, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	If the dislocation is outward, it should not be stretched downwards nor lifted upwards, but rather, it should be positioned as if the hip were dislocated outwards, similar to what we have said about lying on two hips; let them lie face down, and extend the bindings as I have mentioned earlier, then press at the joint with a board; it will be sufficient when the patient can stretch their legs evenly, and they are of equal length. Then bring the thighs together, apply the plaster, and bind with a bandage so that the hip does not move; let them rest for three or four days, then untie the binding and reapply the plaster; if you see that they remain even in length, bind as before and leave it for three days; then undo it, and have them walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	For the knee's dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inwardly and outwardly, and behind; and it does not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.
