And the sign of this is that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at the thigh, and if it does not reach the thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration for all such cases is that you make the patient sit upright, and stretch out their leg if they can, and put your back on their face, and place their foot on your feet; then take their knee in your palms, and pull it between your two hands, then bend both sides of the knee sharply; and another assistant stretches their foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that the leg touches the thigh lightly; then apply a plaster cast over it, and make the leg rest against the thigh, and bind them tightly together for three or four days, then untie them; and do not allow the patient to walk, until their limbs are strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limb is not broken, apply strong stretching, as we have mentioned in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	Of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels sometimes become bruised, and other times fully dislocated, internally and externally.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen and tends to swell more where it has dislocated; the reset must be gentle, and when only bruised one should stretch it gently by hand.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	When it is completely dislocated, you must make the patient sit upright and have an assistant support them except for their leg above the ankle; then pull the foot towards yourself with your right hand, and then twice to the left side, stretch upwards, and push the foot up strongly; do this twice as we have said, by pushing and pulling on the foot; if it returns, that is good; but if not, begin the work again because it will return; and if it cannot be returned thus, make the patient lie down on their back on the ground, firmly fix a pole in the ground between their thighs, and wrap cloth around it to avoid hurting the patient; then have an assistant hold the thigh, while another stretches the foot by hand or with rope tied above the ankle; each assistant must stretch evenly, and the pole should be positioned next to the patient's thighs for support during stretching; finally, place your hands equally over the dislocation and have another assistant hold their healthy leg underneath it; then as you pull from below on the healthy leg an assistant will return the dislocation swiftly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is ready, apply the plaster and pads on top, bind it tightly, tie the foot to the leg, and keep the nerves above the ankle in the back free, making sure the binding isn't too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the binding loosens, rebind it; afterward, release the binding on the third or fourth day, but prevent the patient from walking for four days; and if they walk before this term is over, there's no guarantee that it won't dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if hot abscesses appear there, you must soothe them until they heal as we have mentioned elsewhere.
des dois	twice
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the wrist is dislocated, it should be gently stretched without exertion; this is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any joint of the foot or back, you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or on a straight table, and place your foot on what appears to be the joints, then press hard with your foot until it returns; when it is even, and nothing appears out of place, put a two-legged table under the sole of their foot, then strain it strongly, and leave it for three days, then release them; and let them rest until they are healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wounds and dislocations altogether.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation and one wants to restore it, often the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in your treatment if you are not wise in this art and have not practiced it long, and if you lack compassion, mercy, and courage; use at first soothing medicines for hot abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hands if you see no hope of recovery; but when you see hope, then reset the limb now, even though a hot abscess comes with this; once the limb is back in place, administer soothing medicines for the hot abscess, and treat the wound as required, using drying ointments; if there are small bone fragments along with dislocation, remove them, and do what we have said before about simple illnesses; take care not to become afraid of your work, as I explained earlier, since it is worth pleasing God according to his creation, and for the safety of your hands and body.
Amen	Amen
